Orientation to Mantiq Kabir and Its Author
Title page presenting the book's name, author, and publication details.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author and title of Mantiq Kabir and explain its significance in the Islamic logical tradition.

Core Idea
Mantiq Kabir is the magnum opus of Fakhr al-Din al-Razi in logic.

The title page of a classical text is more than a formality—it tells us the author, the scope, and the scholarly lineage. In this lesson, we examine the title page of Fakhr al-Din al-Razi's Mantiq Kabir to orient ourselves to the work and its author, a towering figure in Islamic theology and logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the book title and author
Locate 'المنطق الكبير' and 'فخر الدين الرازي' in the Arabic. The title means 'The Great Logic' and the author is Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi.
This establishes the foundational identity of the text.
2
Extract the editor and supervisor
Find the names of the modern editors: Dr. Turghud Aq Yuz and Prof. Dr. Ali Duroswi, and their affiliations. This shows contemporary scholarly engagement.
Editors ensure the text's accuracy and provide critical apparatus.
3
Determine the volume and publisher
The title page states 'المجلد الأول' (first volume) and 'دار فارس' (publisher). This indicates a multi-volume work and the publishing body.
Such details help locate the edition and understand its scope.
4
Summarise the significance
Given that Fakhr al-Din al-Razi is a major scholar of kalam and tafsir, his comprehensive logic work is a cornerstone of Islamic logical studies.
This prepares you to engage with the content deeply.

The book is a significant work on logic in the Islamic tradition. The title page indicates this is the first volume, and lists the editor and supervisor.

Introducing Al-Mantiq al-Kabir and Its Author
Title page of the textbook

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author, title, and scholarly editors of Al-Mantiq al-Kabir from its title page.

Core Idea
Al-Mantiq al-Kabir by Fakhr al-Din al-Razi is your guide to mastering Islamic logic.

Every great journey begins with knowing your guide. This lesson introduces the textbook you will be studying: Al-Mantiq al-Kabir by Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, a towering figure in Islamic theology and logic. You will learn to recognize the key details from the title page so you can situate this work within the tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the book's full title
Locate 'المنطق الكبير' on the page. This is the name of the text you will be studying. It means 'The Great Logic'.
2
Identify the author
Look for the author's name: 'للإمام فخر الدين الرازي'. This is Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, a renowned scholar of kalam, tafsir, and logic.
3
Identify the editors and supervisors
The title page also lists the scholars who prepared this edition: Dr. Tur Awad Aq Yuz (researcher) and Prof. Dr. Ali Durusuy (supervisor and reviewer). This ensures the text is reliable.
4
Note the volume and structure
The phrase 'المجلد الأول' indicates this is Volume One. The full work likely consists of multiple volumes, so you know where to start.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
The Formation of Islamic Logic: Aristotle, al-Farabi, and Ibn Sina
Author traces the development of logic from Aristotle through al-Farabi to Ibn Sina.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to trace the transmission of Aristotelian logic into the Islamic world and identify the contributions of al-Farabi and Ibn Sina.

Core Idea
Islamic logic is built on Aristotle's Organon, refined by al-Farabi and perfected by Ibn Sina.

This lesson provides the historical backdrop for your study of Islamic logic. You will learn how the logical works of Aristotle were translated into Arabic, how al-Farabi systematized them earning the title 'Second Teacher', and how Ibn Sina brought logic to maturity in his encyclopedic work al-Shifa'. Understanding this history will help you appreciate the authority and structure of the logical texts you will encounter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the foundational figure
Note that Aristotle is called the 'First Teacher' (al-mu'allim al-awwal) because he founded the science of logic. His logical works are collected in the Organon.
2
Recognize the translated corpus
The passage lists six core books (Categories, On Interpretation, Prior Analytics, Posterior Analytics, Topics, Sophistics) plus Rhetoric, Poetics, and Porphyry's Isagoge. These were translated into Arabic in the 9th-10th centuries.
3
Understand al-Farabi's role
Al-Farabi studied Aristotle's nine books and was called the 'Second Teacher'. However, he excluded the Isagoge from Aristotle's own works, limiting the logical corpus to eight books.
This exclusion shows a shift in how the logical corpus was defined.
4
See Ibn Sina's synthesis
Ibn Sina, in his book al-Shifa', added the Isagoge back and treated logic in nine parts. The passage declares that logic reached its maturity in his work.
5
Connect to later tradition
Post-Farabi logical studies in the Islamic world were commentaries on Aristotle's nine books. This coursebook is part of that commentarial tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الله الحر الرحيم

الدراسة
تقديم الأستاذ الدكتور علي دوروسوي |
لا يخفى على كل باحث أن أرسطو طاليس هو مؤسس علم المنطق، وهذا هو سبب تسميته بـ«المعلم الأول» والذي يقصد به المنطقي الأول.
وأن مجموعة كتب أرسطو المنطقية المكونة من ست مصنفات: المقولات، العبارة، القياس، البرهان، الجدل، السفسطة التي تسمى بالأورغانون (الآلة) ومن ضمنها الشعر والخطابة لأرسطو وإيساغوجي (المدخل) لفرفوريوس الصوري الذي وضعه ليكون مدخلاً لتوضيح وتفسير كلام أرسطو ترجمت إلى العربية في القرنين التاسع والعاشر الميلاديين. ولذلك يعتبر الفارابي هو المؤسس الثاني لعلم المنطق من خلال دراسته لكتب أرسطو التسعة، وهو ما تسبب بتسميته بـ «المعلم الثاني» والذي يقصد به المنطقي الثاني، إلا أن الفارابي حصر مجموعة المنطق في كتب أرسطو الثمانية ولم يعتبر كتاب إيساغوجي لفرفوريوس من ضمن كتب أرسطو المنطقية.
أما ابن سينا فقد تناول في كتابه الكبير المسمى بـ«الشفاء» المنطق الذي أنشأه الفارابي في تسعة أجزاء بعد إضافته كتاب إيساغوجي، وبإمكاننا القول أن المنطق الذي أنشأه أرسطو قد وصل إلى مرحلة النضج والكمال في قسم المنطق من كتاب «الشفاء» لابن سينا، وبذلك يمكننا القول أن دراسات المنطق التي تمت في العالم الإسلامي في القرنين التاسع والعاشر الميلاديين هي دراسات مرتكزة بشكل عام على كتب أرسطو التسعة المذكورة، إما على شكل شرح أو تفسير أو حاشية أو تصحيح أو غير ذلك، ونقصد بذلك أن التصانيف المنطقية ما بعد الفارابي كانت عبارة عن شروح المتون وتصانيف أرسطو المنطقية.
In the name of God, the Beneficent, the Merciful. The Study. Introduction by Professor Doctor Ali Dorusoy. It is no secret to any researcher that Aristotle is the founder of the science of logic, and this is the reason for his being called the 'First Teacher', by which is meant the first logician. And that the collection of Aristotle's logical books consisting of six works: Categories, On Interpretation, Prior Analytics, Posterior Analytics, Topics, Sophistics, which is called the Organon (the instrument), and including Rhetoric and Poetics by Aristotle and Isagoge (the Introduction) by Porphyry of Tyre, which he wrote to be an introduction to clarify and interpret Aristotle's words, were translated into Arabic in the ninth and tenth centuries CE. Therefore, al-Farabi is considered the second founder of the science of logic through his study of Aristotle's nine books, which caused him to be called the 'Second Teacher', by which is meant the second logician, except that al-Farabi restricted the collection of logic to Aristotle's eight books and did not consider Porphyry's Isagoge among Aristotle's logical books. As for Ibn Sina, he treated in his great book called 'al-Shifa'' the logic that al-Farabi had established, in nine parts after adding the book of Isagoge, and we can say that the logic that Aristotle founded reached the stage of maturity and perfection in the logic section of Ibn Sina's 'al-Shifa''. Thus we can say that the logical studies that took place in the Islamic world in the ninth and tenth centuries CE are studies generally based on the mentioned nine books of Aristotle, either in the form of commentary, interpretation, gloss, correction, or otherwise, meaning thereby that the logical compositions after al-Farabi were commentaries on texts and on Aristotle's logical works.
Source pages p. 4

Commentary
This passage is a historical introduction to the development of logic in the Islamic tradition. It begins by establishing Aristotle as the founder of logic, hence his title 'First Teacher' (al-mu'allim al-awwal). It then describes the corpus of Aristotle's logical works: six core books (Categories, On Interpretation, Prior Analytics, Posterior Analytics, Topics, and Sophistics), collectively called the Organon ('the instrument'). Additionally, Aristotle's Rhetoric and Poetics and Porphyry's Isagoge (an introduction to logic) were included in the translated corpus. These works were translated into Arabic in the 9th and 10th centuries CE. The passage then highlights al-Farabi's role as the 'Second Teacher' because he studied and systematized Aristotle's nine books (the six plus Rhetoric, Poetics, and probably the Isagoge initially, though al-Farabi later excluded the Isagoge from Aristotle's own logical works, considering only eight books as strictly Aristotle's). Ibn Sina (Avicenna) further developed logic in his encyclopedic work al-Shifa', where he treated logic in nine parts after adding the Isagoge. The passage concludes that logic reached its maturity in Ibn Sina's work, and that post-Farabi logical studies in the Islamic world were largely commentaries on Aristotle's nine books. This sets the stage for the coursebook to follow, as it is part of that commentarial tradition.

Key Takeaway
Islamic logic originates from Aristotle's Organon, was systematized by al-Farabi, and reached perfection with Ibn Sina's al-Shifa'.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
10 min
Aristotle and the Organon: The Foundation of Logic
Author introduces Aristotle as founder and lists his logical works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the six books of Aristotle's Organon and explain why logic is called an 'instrument' for science.

Core Idea
Aristotle's six logical works form the tool (Organon) for all scientific inquiry.

This lesson introduces you to the founder of logic, Aristotle, known as the 'First Teacher' in the Islamic tradition. We will explore the core texts that were translated into Arabic and became the foundation for all later Islamic logical works. Understanding this origin helps you appreciate why logic was seen as a universal tool, not just a Greek philosophy.

Guided Path
1
Identify Aristotle's title and its meaning
Find the phrase 'al-mu'allim al-awwal' in the Arabic passage. Note that it means 'the First Teacher' and is given to Aristotle as the founder of logic.
2
List the six writings of the Organon
From the passage, extract the six books: Categories, On Interpretation, Prior Analytics, Posterior Analytics, Topics, Sophistical Refutations. These together are called the Organon (instrument).
The passage also mentions Rhetoric and Poetics, which were added later in the Islamic tradition.
3
Understand the meaning of 'Organon'
The term 'Organon' means 'instrument' or 'tool'. Logic was considered a tool for the sciences, not a science itself. This idea was later emphasized by al-Ghazali.
4
Check the role of Porphyry's Isagoge
Note that Porphyry's Isagoge (Introduction) was translated and often included as a preface to Aristotle's works, but al-Farabi later excluded it from the logical corpus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدراسة
تقديم الأستاذ الدكتور علي دوروسوي |
لا يخفى على كل باحث أن أرسطو طاليس هو مؤسس علم المنطق، وهذا هو سبب تسميته بـ«المعلم الأول» والذي يقصد بها المنطقي الأول.
وان مجموعة كتب أرسطو المنطقية المكونة من ست مصنفات المقولات العبارة القياس البرهان الجدل السفسطة التي تسمى بالأورغانون (الآلة) ومن ضمنها الشعر والخطابة لأرسطو وإيساغوجي (المدخل) لفرفوريوس الصوري الذي وضعه ليكون مدخلاً لتوضيح وتفسير كلام أرسطو ترجمت إلى العربية في القرنين التاسع والعاشر الميلاديين. ولذلك يعتبر الفارابي هو المؤسس الثاني لعلم المنطق من خلال دراسته لكتب أرسطو التسعة، وهو ما تسبب بتسميته بـ «المعلم الثاني» والذي يقصد بها المنطقي الثاني، إلا أن الفارابي حصر مجموعة المنطق في كتب أرسطو الثمانية ولم يعتبر كتاب إيساغوجي لفرفوريوس من ضمن كتب أرسطو المنطقية.
أما ابن سينا فقد تناول في كتابه الكبير المسمى بـ«الشفاء» المنطق الذي أنشأه الفارابي في تسعة أجزاء بعد إضافته كتاب إيساغوجي، وبإمكاننا القول أن المنطق الذي أنشأه أرسطو قد وصل إلى مرحلة النضج والكمال في قسم المنطق من كتاب «الشفاء» لابن سينا، وبذلك يمكننا القول أن دراسات المنطق التي تمت في العالم الإسلامي في القرنين التاسع والعاشر الميلاديين هي دراسات مرتكزة بشكل عام على كتب أرسطو التسعة المذكورة، إما على شكل شرح أو تفسير أو حاشية أو تصحيح أو غير ذلك، ونقصد بذلك أن التصانيف المنطقية ما بعد الفارابي كانت عبارة عن شروح المتون وتصانيف أرسطو المنطقية.
في القرن الحادي عشر الميلادي قام ابن سينا بإحداث نقلة نوعية في تقاليد التأليف المنطقي ( الشرح التفسير وكتابة الحواشي) من خلال تصنيفه لكتاب «الشفاء» الذي يتألف من الطبيعيات والنظريات والإلهيات، وكتاب «الشفاء» يشبه بشكل كبير الموسوعة العلمية الشاملة التي تضم الكثير من العلوم الأنسانية التي تم توارثها عن العصور الأولى، ويعتبر قسم المنطق من كتاب «الشفاء» أضخم متن عرفه تاريخ علم المنطق، وبعد إنتهاء حقبة ابن سينا لم تهتم الأوساط والمراكز العلمية إلى مجموعة أرسطو المنطقية، بإستثناء ابن رشد الحفيد فقد قام بتحليل وشرح كتب أرسطو التسعة من جديد وفق رؤيته العلمية، وقام كذلك بتفسير كتاب البرهان لأرسطو، كما لخص كتب ورسائل الفارابي المنطقية (الجوامع).
على الرغم من أن الفارابي عمل على إيجاد حل للجدل الواقع بين النحو والمنطق ( مثال على ذلك: مناظرة القاضي أبي سعيد السيرافي النحوي ومتى بن يونس المنطقي) والتي تسببت في تداخل علم المنطق مع اللغة العربية، وبالرغم من أن ابن سينا ألف كتباً تعليمية ضخمة في المنطق كـ«الشفاء» و«النجاة» و«الإشارات والتنبيهات» إلا أنه لم يستطيع إدخال المنطق في العلوم الدينية كالكلام والفقه، وبعبارة أخرى لم يهتم الفقهاء والمتكلمون المعاصرون للفارابي وابن سينا بعلم المنطق.
أول محاولة لجعل المنطق آلة لفهم الفقه والكلام جاءت من قبل ابن حزم الظاهري (تقريب لحد المنطق بالألفاظ العامية والأمثلة الفقهية)، وقد أكمل الغزالي الفقيه الشافعي والمتكلم الأشعري مشروع ابن حزم، ولكنه رفض حصر المنطق بالفلسفة، إذ اعتبر المنطق آلة كل العلوم بما فيها الفقه والأصول
The Study
Presentation by Professor Dr. Ali Durusoy |
It is no secret to any researcher that Aristotle is the founder of the science of logic, and this is the reason for his being called 'the First Teacher', by which is meant the first logician.
And Aristotle's logical works, consisting of six books: Categories, On Interpretation, Prior Analytics, Posterior Analytics, Topics, Sophistical Refutations, which are called the Organon (the instrument), including also Aristotle's Poetics and Rhetoric, and Porphyry's Isagoge (the Introduction) which he wrote as an introduction to clarify and explain Aristotle's words, were translated into Arabic in the ninth and tenth centuries CE. Therefore, al-Farabi is considered the second founder of the science of logic through his study of Aristotle's nine books, which caused him to be called 'the Second Teacher', by which is meant the second logician, except that al-Farabi limited the logical corpus to Aristotle's eight books and did not consider Porphyry's Isagoge among Aristotle's logical works.
As for Ibn Sina, he dealt in his great book called 'al-Shifa' with the logic that al-Farabi had established in nine parts after adding the Isagoge. And we can say that the logic that Aristotle established reached maturity and perfection in the logic section of Ibn Sina's 'al-Shifa'. Thus, we can say that the logical studies that took place in the Islamic world in the ninth and tenth centuries CE were studies based generally on the aforementioned nine books of Aristotle, either in the form of commentary, explanation, gloss, correction, or otherwise, meaning that logical writings after al-Farabi were commentaries on texts and Aristotle's logical works.
In the eleventh century CE, Ibn Sina brought about a qualitative shift in the traditions of logical authorship (commentary, explanation, and writing glosses) through his composition of 'al-Shifa', which consists of physics, mathematics, and metaphysics. And 'al-Shifa' greatly resembles a comprehensive scientific encyclopedia containing many human sciences inherited from earlier ages. The logic section of 'al-Shifa' is considered the most massive text known in the history of logic. After the end of Ibn Sina's era, scientific circles and centers took no interest in Aristotle's logical corpus, with the exception of Ibn Rushd the grandson, who analyzed and commented on Aristotle's nine books anew according to his scientific vision, and also interpreted Aristotle's Posterior Analytics, and summarized al-Farabi's logical books and treatises (al-Jawami').
Although al-Farabi worked to find a solution to the controversy between grammar and logic (for example: the debate of Judge Abu Sa'id al-Sirafi the grammarian with Matta ibn Yunus the logician), which caused the intermingling of logic with the Arabic language, and although Ibn Sina wrote huge didactic books on logic like 'al-Shifa', 'al-Najat', and 'al-Isharat wa al-Tanbihat', he was unable to introduce logic into the religious sciences such as kalam and fiqh. In other words, the jurists and theologians contemporary with al-Farabi and Ibn Sina did not take interest in the science of logic.
The first attempt to make logic an instrument for understanding fiqh and kalam came from Ibn Hazm al-Zahiri (approximating logic to common expressions and juristic examples), and al-Ghazali, the Shafi'i jurist and Ash'ari theologian, completed Ibn Hazm's project, but he refused to restrict logic to philosophy, considering logic an instrument for all sciences including fiqh and usul.
Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This passage is a historical introduction provided by Professor Dr. Ali Durusoy. It outlines the transmission and development of Greek logic into the Islamic world. The author begins by stating that Aristotle is the undisputed founder of logic, known as the 'First Teacher'. He then lists Aristotle's six logical works (Categories, Interpretation, Prior Analytics, Posterior Analytics, Topics, Sophistics), which together with the Isagoge by Porphyry and Aristotle's Rhetoric and Poetics form the Organon. These were translated into Arabic in the 9th–10th centuries CE. Next, the author highlights al-Farabi as the 'Second Teacher' because he studied Aristotle's nine books (including the Isagoge and Rhetoric/Poetics) and established logic in the Islamic world, though he personally excluded the Isagoge. Then Ibn Sina appears: his encyclopedic work al-Shifa brought Aristotle's logic to maturity, containing the most extensive treatment of logic. After Ibn Sina, interest in Aristotle's original works waned except for Ibn Rushd (Averroes), who wrote new commentaries. The author also mentions al-Farabi's efforts to resolve the grammar-logic debate, exemplified by the famous debate between al-Sirafi and Matta ibn Yunus, which led to an intermingling of logic with Arabic. Despite the works of al-Farabi and Ibn Sina, logic was not initially integrated into Islamic religious sciences like fiqh and kalam. The first to attempt this was Ibn Hazm al-Zahiri, who used simple language and fiqh examples. Finally, al-Ghazali completed this integration, insisting that logic is a tool for all sciences, including fiqh and usul al-fiqh, not just philosophy.

Key Terms
المعلم الأول
الأورغانون
إيساغوجي

Key Takeaway
Aristotle's Organon, consisting of six logical works, was translated into Arabic and became the foundation of logic as a tool for all sciences in the Islamic world.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
Al-Farabi: The Second Teacher and Systematizer of Logic
Author describes al-Farabi's role and the debate with grammarians.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe al-Farabi's role in the development of Islamic logic and explain why he is called the 'Second Teacher'.

Core Idea
Al-Farabi studied Aristotle's nine books and established logic in the Islamic world, earning the title 'Second Teacher'.

After the translation of Aristotle's works, al-Farabi emerged as the foremost scholar of logic. He is called the 'Second Teacher' because he not only studied but also systematized Aristotle's logic, making it accessible to Islamic scholars. His work also sparked a debate with grammarians about the relationship between logic and language.

Guided Path
1
Identify al-Farabi's title
Find where the passage calls al-Farabi 'al-mu'allim al-thani' (the Second Teacher). Understand that this title indicates he is second only to Aristotle in logic.
2
Determine which books al-Farabi considered part of logic
The passage says al-Farabi limited the logical corpus to Aristotle's eight books and excluded Porphyry's Isagoge. This shows he had a specific view of what constitutes logic.
Later, Ibn Sina added the Isagoge back, making nine books.
3
Recall the grammar-logic debate
The author mentions the debate between al-Sirafi (grammarian) and Matta ibn Yunus (logician) as a key event. Al-Farabi worked to resolve the tension between grammar and logic.
This debate shows how logic began to intermingle with Arabic language studies.
4
Assess al-Farabi's influence
Note that despite his efforts, logic was not yet integrated into religious sciences like fiqh and kalam during his time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدراسة
تقديم الأستاذ الدكتور علي دوروسوي |
لا يخفى على كل باحث أن أرسطو طاليس هو مؤسس علم المنطق، وهذا هو سبب تسميته بـ«المعلم الأول» والذي يقصد بها المنطقي الأول.
وان مجموعة كتب أرسطو المنطقية المكونة من ست مصنفات المقولات العبارة القياس البرهان الجدل السفسطة التي تسمى بالأورغانون (الآلة) ومن ضمنها الشعر والخطابة لأرسطو وإيساغوجي (المدخل) لفرفوريوس الصوري الذي وضعه ليكون مدخلاً لتوضيح وتفسير كلام أرسطو ترجمت إلى العربية في القرنين التاسع والعاشر الميلاديين. ولذلك يعتبر الفارابي هو المؤسس الثاني لعلم المنطق من خلال دراسته لكتب أرسطو التسعة، وهو ما تسبب بتسميته بـ «المعلم الثاني» والذي يقصد بها المنطقي الثاني، إلا أن الفارابي حصر مجموعة المنطق في كتب أرسطو الثمانية ولم يعتبر كتاب إيساغوجي لفرفوريوس من ضمن كتب أرسطو المنطقية.
أما ابن سينا فقد تناول في كتابه الكبير المسمى بـ«الشفاء» المنطق الذي أنشأه الفارابي في تسعة أجزاء بعد إضافته كتاب إيساغوجي، وبإمكاننا القول أن المنطق الذي أنشأه أرسطو قد وصل إلى مرحلة النضج والكمال في قسم المنطق من كتاب «الشفاء» لابن سينا، وبذلك يمكننا القول أن دراسات المنطق التي تمت في العالم الإسلامي في القرنين التاسع والعاشر الميلاديين هي دراسات مرتكزة بشكل عام على كتب أرسطو التسعة المذكورة، إما على شكل شرح أو تفسير أو حاشية أو تصحيح أو غير ذلك، ونقصد بذلك أن التصانيف المنطقية ما بعد الفارابي كانت عبارة عن شروح المتون وتصانيف أرسطو المنطقية.
في القرن الحادي عشر الميلادي قام ابن سينا بإحداث نقلة نوعية في تقاليد التأليف المنطقي ( الشرح التفسير وكتابة الحواشي) من خلال تصنيفه لكتاب «الشفاء» الذي يتألف من الطبيعيات والنظريات والإلهيات، وكتاب «الشفاء» يشبه بشكل كبير الموسوعة العلمية الشاملة التي تضم الكثير من العلوم الأنسانية التي تم توارثها عن العصور الأولى، ويعتبر قسم المنطق من كتاب «الشفاء» أضخم متن عرفه تاريخ علم المنطق، وبعد إنتهاء حقبة ابن سينا لم تهتم الأوساط والمراكز العلمية إلى مجموعة أرسطو المنطقية، بإستثناء ابن رشد الحفيد فقد قام بتحليل وشرح كتب أرسطو التسعة من جديد وفق رؤيته العلمية، وقام كذلك بتفسير كتاب البرهان لأرسطو، كما لخص كتب ورسائل الفارابي المنطقية (الجوامع).
على الرغم من أن الفارابي عمل على إيجاد حل للجدل الواقع بين النحو والمنطق ( مثال على ذلك: مناظرة القاضي أبي سعيد السيرافي النحوي ومتى بن يونس المنطقي) والتي تسببت في تداخل علم المنطق مع اللغة العربية، وبالرغم من أن ابن سينا ألف كتباً تعليمية ضخمة في المنطق كـ«الشفاء» و«النجاة» و«الإشارات والتنبيهات» إلا أنه لم يستطيع إدخال المنطق في العلوم الدينية كالكلام والفقه، وبعبارة أخرى لم يهتم الفقهاء والمتكلمون المعاصرون للفارابي وابن سينا بعلم المنطق.
أول محاولة لجعل المنطق آلة لفهم الفقه والكلام جاءت من قبل ابن حزم الظاهري (تقريب لحد المنطق بالألفاظ العامية والأمثلة الفقهية)، وقد أكمل الغزالي الفقيه الشافعي والمتكلم الأشعري مشروع ابن حزم، ولكنه رفض حصر المنطق بالفلسفة، إذ اعتبر المنطق آلة كل العلوم بما فيها الفقه والأصول
The Study
Presentation by Professor Dr. Ali Durusoy |
It is no secret to any researcher that Aristotle is the founder of the science of logic, and this is the reason for his being called 'the First Teacher', by which is meant the first logician.
And Aristotle's logical works, consisting of six books: Categories, On Interpretation, Prior Analytics, Posterior Analytics, Topics, Sophistical Refutations, which are called the Organon (the instrument), including also Aristotle's Poetics and Rhetoric, and Porphyry's Isagoge (the Introduction) which he wrote as an introduction to clarify and explain Aristotle's words, were translated into Arabic in the ninth and tenth centuries CE. Therefore, al-Farabi is considered the second founder of the science of logic through his study of Aristotle's nine books, which caused him to be called 'the Second Teacher', by which is meant the second logician, except that al-Farabi limited the logical corpus to Aristotle's eight books and did not consider Porphyry's Isagoge among Aristotle's logical works.
As for Ibn Sina, he dealt in his great book called 'al-Shifa' with the logic that al-Farabi had established in nine parts after adding the Isagoge. And we can say that the logic that Aristotle established reached maturity and perfection in the logic section of Ibn Sina's 'al-Shifa'. Thus, we can say that the logical studies that took place in the Islamic world in the ninth and tenth centuries CE were studies based generally on the aforementioned nine books of Aristotle, either in the form of commentary, explanation, gloss, correction, or otherwise, meaning that logical writings after al-Farabi were commentaries on texts and Aristotle's logical works.
In the eleventh century CE, Ibn Sina brought about a qualitative shift in the traditions of logical authorship (commentary, explanation, and writing glosses) through his composition of 'al-Shifa', which consists of physics, mathematics, and metaphysics. And 'al-Shifa' greatly resembles a comprehensive scientific encyclopedia containing many human sciences inherited from earlier ages. The logic section of 'al-Shifa' is considered the most massive text known in the history of logic. After the end of Ibn Sina's era, scientific circles and centers took no interest in Aristotle's logical corpus, with the exception of Ibn Rushd the grandson, who analyzed and commented on Aristotle's nine books anew according to his scientific vision, and also interpreted Aristotle's Posterior Analytics, and summarized al-Farabi's logical books and treatises (al-Jawami').
Although al-Farabi worked to find a solution to the controversy between grammar and logic (for example: the debate of Judge Abu Sa'id al-Sirafi the grammarian with Matta ibn Yunus the logician), which caused the intermingling of logic with the Arabic language, and although Ibn Sina wrote huge didactic books on logic like 'al-Shifa', 'al-Najat', and 'al-Isharat wa al-Tanbihat', he was unable to introduce logic into the religious sciences such as kalam and fiqh. In other words, the jurists and theologians contemporary with al-Farabi and Ibn Sina did not take interest in the science of logic.
The first attempt to make logic an instrument for understanding fiqh and kalam came from Ibn Hazm al-Zahiri (approximating logic to common expressions and juristic examples), and al-Ghazali, the Shafi'i jurist and Ash'ari theologian, completed Ibn Hazm's project, but he refused to restrict logic to philosophy, considering logic an instrument for all sciences including fiqh and usul.
Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This passage is a historical introduction provided by Professor Dr. Ali Durusoy. It outlines the transmission and development of Greek logic into the Islamic world. The author begins by stating that Aristotle is the undisputed founder of logic, known as the 'First Teacher'. He then lists Aristotle's six logical works (Categories, Interpretation, Prior Analytics, Posterior Analytics, Topics, Sophistics), which together with the Isagoge by Porphyry and Aristotle's Rhetoric and Poetics form the Organon. These were translated into Arabic in the 9th–10th centuries CE. Next, the author highlights al-Farabi as the 'Second Teacher' because he studied Aristotle's nine books (including the Isagoge and Rhetoric/Poetics) and established logic in the Islamic world, though he personally excluded the Isagoge. Then Ibn Sina appears: his encyclopedic work al-Shifa brought Aristotle's logic to maturity, containing the most extensive treatment of logic. After Ibn Sina, interest in Aristotle's original works waned except for Ibn Rushd (Averroes), who wrote new commentaries. The author also mentions al-Farabi's efforts to resolve the grammar-logic debate, exemplified by the famous debate between al-Sirafi and Matta ibn Yunus, which led to an intermingling of logic with Arabic. Despite the works of al-Farabi and Ibn Sina, logic was not initially integrated into Islamic religious sciences like fiqh and kalam. The first to attempt this was Ibn Hazm al-Zahiri, who used simple language and fiqh examples. Finally, al-Ghazali completed this integration, insisting that logic is a tool for all sciences, including fiqh and usul al-fiqh, not just philosophy.

Key Terms
المعلم الثاني
الفارابي
مناظرة السيرافي ومتى

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) He taught at the second university in Baghdad

Key Takeaway
Al-Farabi's systematization of Aristotle's logic and his engagement with the grammar-logic debate laid the groundwork for the later integration of logic into Islamic sciences.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
10 min
Ibn Sina and the Culmination of Islamic Logic
Author describes Ibn Sina's contribution and the shift in logical tradition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how Ibn Sina's al-Shifa advanced Aristotle's logic to its mature form and why it is considered the most comprehensive logical work in the Islamic tradition.

Core Idea
Ibn Sina's al-Shifa brought Aristotle's logic to maturity, becoming the most massive and influential logical text in the Islamic world.

Ibn Sina (Avicenna) built upon al-Farabi's work and produced a monumental encyclopedia, al-Shifa, which includes the most extensive treatment of logic. This lesson explores how Ibn Sina perfected the Organon by adding Porphyry's Isagoge and creating a comprehensive system. His works like al-Isharat also became standard textbooks, but initially, they did not gain traction among religious scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify Ibn Sina's major logical work
From the passage, find 'al-Shifa' and note its structure: it includes natural sciences, mathematics, and metaphysics, with a massive logic section.
2
Understand the addition of the Isagoge
Al-Farabi had excluded the Isagoge, but Ibn Sina included it, making the logical corpus nine books. This indicates his broader view of what comprises logic.
3
Assess the maturity of logic in al-Shifa
The author states that logic reached maturity and perfection in al-Shifa. Consider what this means: comprehensive coverage, clear organization, and integration of earlier works.
4
Note the shift after Ibn Sina
After Ibn Sina, interest in Aristotle's original works waned except for Ibn Rushd. Most subsequent logical writings were commentaries or glosses on Ibn Sina's works.

intermediate

Ibn Hazm and al-Ghazali: Integrating Logic into Islamic Sciences
Author describes the integration of logic into religious sciences by Ibn Hazm and al-Ghazali.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to trace how Ibn Hazm and al-Ghazali integrated logic into fiqh and kalam, and explain why al-Ghazali considered logic a tool for all sciences.

Core Idea
Ibn Hazm first attempted to make logic accessible to jurists, and al-Ghazali completed the integration, insisting logic is indispensable for all Islamic sciences.

Despite the advanced logical works of al-Farabi and Ibn Sina, religious scholars initially rejected logic as foreign to Islam. This lesson covers the pivotal contributions of Ibn Hazm al-Zahiri and al-Ghazali, who reframed logic as a universal tool rather than a Greek philosophy. Their efforts led to logic becoming a standard part of the curriculum in usul al-fiqh and kalam.

Guided Path
1
Identify Ibn Hazm's approach
Find the phrase 'taqrib li hadd al-mantiq bi al-alfaz al-'amiyya wa al-amthila al-fiqhiyya'. Ibn Hazm simplified logic using everyday language and fiqh examples.
2
Understand al-Ghazali's completion
Al-Ghazali built on Ibn Hazm's project. He refused to restrict logic to philosophy, claiming it is a tool for every science, including fiqh and usul al-fiqh.
3
Note the resistance before them
The passage earlier mentioned that jurists and theologians (fuqaha' and mutakallimun) contemporary with al-Farabi and Ibn Sina did not care for logic. Ibn Hazm and al-Ghazali overcame this resistance.
4
Apply the concept
Consider how al-Ghazali used logic in his usul work al-Mustasfa. Logic became the 'mizan' (scale) for evaluating arguments in fiqh and kalam.

الدراسة
تقديم الأستاذ الدكتور علي دوروسوي |
لا يخفى على كل باحث أن أرسطو طاليس هو مؤسس علم المنطق، وهذا هو سبب تسميته بـ«المعلم الأول» والذي يقصد بها المنطقي الأول.
وان مجموعة كتب أرسطو المنطقية المكونة من ست مصنفات المقولات العبارة القياس البرهان الجدل السفسطة التي تسمى بالأورغانون (الآلة) ومن ضمنها الشعر والخطابة لأرسطو وإيساغوجي (المدخل) لفرفوريوس الصوري الذي وضعه ليكون مدخلاً لتوضيح وتفسير كلام أرسطو ترجمت إلى العربية في القرنين التاسع والعاشر الميلاديين. ولذلك يعتبر الفارابي هو المؤسس الثاني لعلم المنطق من خلال دراسته لكتب أرسطو التسعة، وهو ما تسبب بتسميته بـ «المعلم الثاني» والذي يقصد بها المنطقي الثاني، إلا أن الفارابي حصر مجموعة المنطق في كتب أرسطو الثمانية ولم يعتبر كتاب إيساغوجي لفرفوريوس من ضمن كتب أرسطو المنطقية.
أما ابن سينا فقد تناول في كتابه الكبير المسمى بـ«الشفاء» المنطق الذي أنشأه الفارابي في تسعة أجزاء بعد إضافته كتاب إيساغوجي، وبإمكاننا القول أن المنطق الذي أنشأه أرسطو قد وصل إلى مرحلة النضج والكمال في قسم المنطق من كتاب «الشفاء» لابن سينا، وبذلك يمكننا القول أن دراسات المنطق التي تمت في العالم الإسلامي في القرنين التاسع والعاشر الميلاديين هي دراسات مرتكزة بشكل عام على كتب أرسطو التسعة المذكورة، إما على شكل شرح أو تفسير أو حاشية أو تصحيح أو غير ذلك، ونقصد بذلك أن التصانيف المنطقية ما بعد الفارابي كانت عبارة عن شروح المتون وتصانيف أرسطو المنطقية.
في القرن الحادي عشر الميلادي قام ابن سينا بإحداث نقلة نوعية في تقاليد التأليف المنطقي ( الشرح التفسير وكتابة الحواشي) من خلال تصنيفه لكتاب «الشفاء» الذي يتألف من الطبيعيات والنظريات والإلهيات، وكتاب «الشفاء» يشبه بشكل كبير الموسوعة العلمية الشاملة التي تضم الكثير من العلوم الأنسانية التي تم توارثها عن العصور الأولى، ويعتبر قسم المنطق من كتاب «الشفاء» أضخم متن عرفه تاريخ علم المنطق، وبعد إنتهاء حقبة ابن سينا لم تهتم الأوساط والمراكز العلمية إلى مجموعة أرسطو المنطقية، بإستثناء ابن رشد الحفيد فقد قام بتحليل وشرح كتب أرسطو التسعة من جديد وفق رؤيته العلمية، وقام كذلك بتفسير كتاب البرهان لأرسطو، كما لخص كتب ورسائل الفارابي المنطقية (الجوامع).
على الرغم من أن الفارابي عمل على إيجاد حل للجدل الواقع بين النحو والمنطق ( مثال على ذلك: مناظرة القاضي أبي سعيد السيرافي النحوي ومتى بن يونس المنطقي) والتي تسببت في تداخل علم المنطق مع اللغة العربية، وبالرغم من أن ابن سينا ألف كتباً تعليمية ضخمة في المنطق كـ«الشفاء» و«النجاة» و«الإشارات والتنبيهات» إلا أنه لم يستطيع إدخال المنطق في العلوم الدينية كالكلام والفقه، وبعبارة أخرى لم يهتم الفقهاء والمتكلمون المعاصرون للفارابي وابن سينا بعلم المنطق.
أول محاولة لجعل المنطق آلة لفهم الفقه والكلام جاءت من قبل ابن حزم الظاهري (تقريب لحد المنطق بالألفاظ العامية والأمثلة الفقهية)، وقد أكمل الغزالي الفقيه الشافعي والمتكلم الأشعري مشروع ابن حزم، ولكنه رفض حصر المنطق بالفلسفة، إذ اعتبر المنطق آلة كل العلوم بما فيها الفقه والأصول
The Study
Presentation by Professor Dr. Ali Durusoy |
It is no secret to any researcher that Aristotle is the founder of the science of logic, and this is the reason for his being called 'the First Teacher', by which is meant the first logician.
And Aristotle's logical works, consisting of six books: Categories, On Interpretation, Prior Analytics, Posterior Analytics, Topics, Sophistical Refutations, which are called the Organon (the instrument), including also Aristotle's Poetics and Rhetoric, and Porphyry's Isagoge (the Introduction) which he wrote as an introduction to clarify and explain Aristotle's words, were translated into Arabic in the ninth and tenth centuries CE. Therefore, al-Farabi is considered the second founder of the science of logic through his study of Aristotle's nine books, which caused him to be called 'the Second Teacher', by which is meant the second logician, except that al-Farabi limited the logical corpus to Aristotle's eight books and did not consider Porphyry's Isagoge among Aristotle's logical works.
As for Ibn Sina, he dealt in his great book called 'al-Shifa' with the logic that al-Farabi had established in nine parts after adding the Isagoge. And we can say that the logic that Aristotle established reached maturity and perfection in the logic section of Ibn Sina's 'al-Shifa'. Thus, we can say that the logical studies that took place in the Islamic world in the ninth and tenth centuries CE were studies based generally on the aforementioned nine books of Aristotle, either in the form of commentary, explanation, gloss, correction, or otherwise, meaning that logical writings after al-Farabi were commentaries on texts and Aristotle's logical works.
In the eleventh century CE, Ibn Sina brought about a qualitative shift in the traditions of logical authorship (commentary, explanation, and writing glosses) through his composition of 'al-Shifa', which consists of physics, mathematics, and metaphysics. And 'al-Shifa' greatly resembles a comprehensive scientific encyclopedia containing many human sciences inherited from earlier ages. The logic section of 'al-Shifa' is considered the most massive text known in the history of logic. After the end of Ibn Sina's era, scientific circles and centers took no interest in Aristotle's logical corpus, with the exception of Ibn Rushd the grandson, who analyzed and commented on Aristotle's nine books anew according to his scientific vision, and also interpreted Aristotle's Posterior Analytics, and summarized al-Farabi's logical books and treatises (al-Jawami').
Although al-Farabi worked to find a solution to the controversy between grammar and logic (for example: the debate of Judge Abu Sa'id al-Sirafi the grammarian with Matta ibn Yunus the logician), which caused the intermingling of logic with the Arabic language, and although Ibn Sina wrote huge didactic books on logic like 'al-Shifa', 'al-Najat', and 'al-Isharat wa al-Tanbihat', he was unable to introduce logic into the religious sciences such as kalam and fiqh. In other words, the jurists and theologians contemporary with al-Farabi and Ibn Sina did not take interest in the science of logic.
The first attempt to make logic an instrument for understanding fiqh and kalam came from Ibn Hazm al-Zahiri (approximating logic to common expressions and juristic examples), and al-Ghazali, the Shafi'i jurist and Ash'ari theologian, completed Ibn Hazm's project, but he refused to restrict logic to philosophy, considering logic an instrument for all sciences including fiqh and usul.
Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This passage is a historical introduction provided by Professor Dr. Ali Durusoy. It outlines the transmission and development of Greek logic into the Islamic world. The author begins by stating that Aristotle is the undisputed founder of logic, known as the 'First Teacher'. He then lists Aristotle's six logical works (Categories, Interpretation, Prior Analytics, Posterior Analytics, Topics, Sophistics), which together with the Isagoge by Porphyry and Aristotle's Rhetoric and Poetics form the Organon. These were translated into Arabic in the 9th–10th centuries CE. Next, the author highlights al-Farabi as the 'Second Teacher' because he studied Aristotle's nine books (including the Isagoge and Rhetoric/Poetics) and established logic in the Islamic world, though he personally excluded the Isagoge. Then Ibn Sina appears: his encyclopedic work al-Shifa brought Aristotle's logic to maturity, containing the most extensive treatment of logic. After Ibn Sina, interest in Aristotle's original works waned except for Ibn Rushd (Averroes), who wrote new commentaries. The author also mentions al-Farabi's efforts to resolve the grammar-logic debate, exemplified by the famous debate between al-Sirafi and Matta ibn Yunus, which led to an intermingling of logic with Arabic. Despite the works of al-Farabi and Ibn Sina, logic was not initially integrated into Islamic religious sciences like fiqh and kalam. The first to attempt this was Ibn Hazm al-Zahiri, who used simple language and fiqh examples. Finally, al-Ghazali completed this integration, insisting that logic is a tool for all sciences, including fiqh and usul al-fiqh, not just philosophy.

Key Terms

الغزالي
تقريب المنطق
آلة العلوم

Key Takeaway
Ibn Hazm and al-Ghazali successfully transformed logic from a foreign philosophy into an indispensable instrument for Islamic jurisprudence and theology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Compare Ibn Hazm's method (using everyday language and fiqh examples) with al-Ghazali's approach. What did al-Ghazali add that Ibn Hazm did not?
?

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
7 min
From Ibn Sina to al-Ghazali: The Integration of Logic into Islamic Sciences
Author narrates the historical development of logic from Ibn Sina to al-Ghazali, highlighting key figures and contributions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to trace the historical steps that led to the integration of logic into Islamic sciences, identifying the roles of key figures.

Core Idea
Al-Ghazali transformed logic from a Greek philosophical tool into an essential instrument for all Islamic sciences.

This passage narrates the journey of logic from Ibn Sina's encyclopedic work through al-Ghazali's final integration. You will see how logic moved from being a subject of philosophical debate to a required discipline for jurists and theologians.

Guided Path
1
Ibn Sina's transformation of logical literature
Observe how Ibn Sina's al-Shifa' replaced the original Aristotelian corpus in scope, becoming the largest text in the history of logic.
This shift marks the beginning of an independent Islamic logical tradition.
2
The grammar-logic debate and al-Farabi's role
Understand the tension between grammarians and logicians exemplified by the debate between al-Sirafi and Matta. Al-Farabi attempted to mediate by showing logic's universal applicability.
This debate caused logic to intermingle with Arabic language, but did not yet lead to integration into religious sciences.
3
Ibn Hazm's pioneering simplification
Identify the first attempt to make logic an instrument for fiqh and kalam by Ibn Hazm, who used colloquial terms and fiqh examples to make logic accessible.
This was a crucial step but limited in scope.
4
Al-Ghazali's completion: logic as a religious science
Analyze how al-Ghazali wrote multiple works to present logic as a tool for all sciences, including fiqh and usul. He declared logic a religious science and famously said that one who does not study logic cannot be trusted in their knowledge.
This completes the integration, making logic a prerequisite for Islamic scholarship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في القرن الحادي عشر الميلادي قام ابن سينا بإحداث نقلة نوعية في تقاليد التأليف المنطقي ( الشرح التفسير وكتابة الحواشي) من خلال تصنيفه لكتاب «الشفاء» الذي يتألف من الطبيعيات والنظريات والإلهيات، وكتاب «الشفاء» يشبه بشكل كبير الموسوعة العلمية الشاملة التي تضم الكثير من العلوم الأنسانية التي تم توارثها عن العصور الأولى، ويعتبر قسم المنطق من كتاب «الشفاء» أضخم متن عرفه تاريخ علم المنطق، وبعد إنتهاء حقبة ابن سينا لم تهتم الأوساط والمراكز العلمية إلى مجموعة أرسطو المنطقية، بإستثناء ابن رشد الحفيد فقد قام بتحليل وشرح كتب أرسطو التسعة من جديد وفق رؤيته العلمية، وقام كذلك بتفسير كتاب البرهان لأرسطو، كما لخص كتب ورسائل الفارابي المنطقية (الجوامع). على الرغم من أن الفارابي عمل على إيجاد حل للجدل الواقع بين النحو والمنطق ( مثال على ذلك: مناظرة القاضي أبي سعيد السيرافي النحوي ومتى بن يونس المنطقي) والتي تسببت في تداخل علم المنطق مع اللغة العربية، وبالرغم من أن ابن سينا ألف كتباً تعليمية ضخمة في المنطق كـ«الشفاء» و«النجاة» و«الإشارات والتنبيهات إلا أنه لم يستطيع إدخال المنطق في العلوم الدينية كالكلام والفقه، وبعبارة أخرى لم يهتم الفقهاء والمتكلمون المعاصرون للفارابي وابن سينا بعلم المنطق. أول محاولة لجعل المنطق آلة لفهم الفقه والكلام جاءت من قبل ابن حزم الظاهري التقريب لحد المنطق بالألفاظ العامية والأمثلة الفقهية)، وقد أكمل الغزالي الفقيه الشافعي والمتكلم الأشعري مشروع ابن حزم، ولكنه رفض حصر المنطق بالفلسفة، إذ اعتبر المنطق آلة كل العلوم بما فيها الفقه والأصول. الدراسة والكلام وذلك من خلال تأليفه لكتب في علم المنطق كـ«معيار العلم» و «محك النظر» و«المستصفى من علم الأصول» و «القسطاس المستقيم» و«أساس القياس، بل إن الغزالي اعتبر المنطق من العلوم الدينية، وقد أدخله في علم الكلام من خلال كتابه إحياء علوم الدين ، وقد قال في المستصفى: «من لم يدرس المنطق لا يوثق بعلمه».
In the eleventh century CE, Ibn Sina brought about a qualitative shift in the traditions of logical authorship (commentary and writing glosses) through his composition of the book al-Shifa', which consists of the natural sciences, the theoretical sciences, and the divine sciences. The book al-Shifa' greatly resembles a comprehensive scientific encyclopedia that includes many of the human sciences inherited from ancient times. The logic section of al-Shifa' is considered the largest text known in the history of logic. After the end of Ibn Sina's era, scholarly circles and centers did not pay attention to Aristotle's logical corpus, with the exception of Ibn Rushd the grandson, who analyzed and explained Aristotle's nine books anew according to his own scientific vision, and also interpreted Aristotle's Posterior Analytics, and summarized al-Farabi's logical books and treatises (al-Jawami'). Despite al-Farabi's effort to find a solution to the debate between grammar and logic (example: the debate between judge Abu Sa'id al-Sirafi the grammarian and Matta b. Yunus the logician) which caused logic to intermingle with the Arabic language, and despite Ibn Sina's authorship of huge educational books on logic such as al-Shifa', al-Najat, and al-Isharat wa al-Tanbihat, he was unable to introduce logic into the religious sciences like kalam and fiqh. In other words, the contemporary jurists and theologians of al-Farabi and Ibn Sina did not pay attention to logic. The first attempt to make logic an instrument for understanding fiqh and kalam came from Ibn Hazm al-Zahiri (approximating the definition of logic with colloquial terms and fiqh examples), and al-Ghazali, the Shafi'i jurist and Ash'ari theologian, completed Ibn Hazm's project, but he refused to confine logic to philosophy, considering logic an instrument for all sciences including fiqh and usul. Al-dirasah wa al-kalam [the study and speech] and that was through his authorship of books on logic such as Mi'yar al-'Ilm, Mihakk al-Nazar, al-Mustasfa min 'ilm al-usul, al-Qistas al-Mustaqim, and Asas al-Qiyas. Moreover, al-Ghazali considered logic a religious science and introduced it into kalam through his book Ihya' 'Ulum al-Din. He said in al-Mustasfa: 'Whoever does not study logic, his knowledge is not to be trusted.'
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage provides a historical overview of the development of Islamic logic up to al-Ghazali. It begins with Ibn Sina's transformative contribution to logical literature through his encyclopedia al-Shifa', which became a major reference. Then it notes the decline of interest in Aristotle's texts except for Ibn Rushd. It discusses al-Farabi's attempts to reconcile grammar and logic, and Ibn Sina's failure to integrate logic into religious sciences. The first successful integration was by Ibn Hazm, who simplified logic using colloquial language and fiqh examples. Then al-Ghazali completed this project by writing several works that presented logic as an instrument for all sciences, including fiqh and kalam. The passage emphasizes al-Ghazali's famous statement that one who does not study logic cannot be trusted in his knowledge, showing his elevation of logic to a religious science. All examples are drawn from the historical development of Islamic logic, consistent with the Islamic sciences context.

الفقه

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
7 min
Al-Ghazali's Integration of Logic into Kalam
Describes al-Ghazali's role in integrating logic into Islamic theology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify al-Ghazali's key arguments for logic as a religious science and describe how he integrated it into kalam.

Core Idea
Al-Ghazali made logic a religious duty, transforming Islamic theology forever.

Before al-Ghazali, logic was largely seen as a philosophical tool. This lesson explores how al-Ghazali reframed logic as essential for religious knowledge, writing dedicated works and embedding it into his theological writings. Understanding this shift helps you appreciate why later scholars treated logic as a prerequisite for ijtihad.

Guided Path
1
Identify al-Ghazali's logical works
List the works mentioned in the passage: 'Mi'yar al-Ilm', 'Mihakk al-Nazar', 'al-Mustasfa', 'al-Qistas al-Mustaqim', 'Asas al-Qiyas'. Note that these are not just philosophy books but integrated into usul al-fiqh and kalam.
2
Extract his claim about logic's status
Find the statement: 'من لم يدرس المنطق لا يوثق بعلمه' (Whoever has not studied logic, his knowledge is not to be trusted). This shows al-Ghazali elevated logic to a criterion for reliable scholarship.
This is from 'al-Mustasfa'.
3
Trace integration into kalam
Al-Ghazali introduced logic into 'Ihya' Ulum al-Din', a theological work. This move made logic acceptable for religious scholars who previously avoided it.
The passage explicitly says: 'وقد أدخله في علم الكلام من خلال كتابه إحياء علوم الدين'.
4
Contrast with earlier views
Compare al-Ghazali's view with al-Baghdadi's earlier position that dialectic (jadal) is superior to philosophical logic. Al-Ghazali's approach overcame this resistance.

الدراسة والكلام وذلك من خلال تأليفه لكتب في علم المنطق كـ«معيار العلم» و «محك النظر» و«المستصفى من علم الأصول» و «القسطاس المستقيم» و«أساس القياس، بل إن الغزالي اعتبر المنطق من العلوم الدينية، وقد أدخله في علم الكلام من خلال كتابه إحياء علوم الدين ، وقد قال في المستصفى: «من لم يدرس المنطق لا يوثق بعلمه». أما الفقيه الشافعي والمتكلم الأشعري عبد القاهر البغدادي الذي عاصر ابن سينا والذي عاش قبل الغزالي بربع قرن فقد أطلق في كتابه عيار النظر في علم الجدل مصطلح أهل الجدل على المتكلمين و أهل المنطق على الفلاسفة، وذهب إلى أن الجدل أعلى من منطق الفلاسفة، وإذا استثنينا بعض الأسماء كالسهروردي المقتول وأبو البركات البغدادي فإن المصنفات المنطقية التي تم تأليفها في العالم الإسلامي بعد الغزالي تم تصنيفها من قبل المتكلمين الأشاعرة، وقد ذهب المتكلمون الأشاعرة الذين جاؤوا بعد الغزالي إلى أن بين المنطق وعلم الكلام علاقة تلازم ، وقد اعتمد هؤلاء المتكلمون في منطقهم بشكل كبير على متون ابن سينا المنطقية الواردة في كتابيه «الشفاء» والإشارات والتنبيهات». تعتبر الحقبة ( من بداية القرن الحادي عشر وإنتهاء بالقرن الثالث عشر الميلادي) هي الحقبة التي برز فيها المتكلمون الأشاعرة بشكل كبير وهي بمثابة العصر الذهبي لتاريخ المنطق الإسلامي، ومن بين المناطقة الذين برزوا في هذه الفترة فخر الدين الرازي وسيف الدين الآمدي وسراج الدين الأرموي وأثير الدين الأبهري ونصير الدين الطوسي وأفضل الدين الخونجي ونجم الدين الكاتبي القزويني والمنطق الكبير وقطب الدين الشيرازي، وقد كان فخر الدين الرازي المسمى بالإمام الشارح الفاضل) على رأس وطليعة هؤلاء المنطقيين. وكذلك نجد أن قطب الدين الرازي في كتابه التقرير «شرح الشمسية» يجعل لكل من الفارابي وابن سينا والفخر الرازي مذهبًا ومدرسة منطقية، وقد قرر الشيرازي هذه النتيجة من خلال تتبعه لتأثير كل شخص منهم على الأوساط والمحاضن العلمية المنطقية، وهو ما جعل المناطقة الذين جاؤوا بعد الفخر الرازي (الأبهري والخونجي) يعتبرونه الإمام وأن له مدرسة منطقية مستقلة يطلقون عليها مدرسة الإمام ويحتجون بأقوالها وتقريراتها. كتاب الرازي المنطق الكبير الذي بين أيدينا يعتبر أضخم وأكبر كتاب في المنطق تم تأليفه بعد مجموعة ابن سينا المنطقية المسماة بـ«الشفاء»، وهو أول كتاب ألفه الرازي في علم المنطق، والدليل على ذلك نسبته بعض الأقوال الواردة في الشروح والملخصات التي كتبها على عيون الحكمة» و«الإشارات» إلى هذا الكتاب، وقد اعتمد الرازي في هذا الكتاب بشكل كبير على أقسام المنطق الموجودة في كتابي ابن سينا الشفاء» و«الإشارات والتنبيهات». على الرغم من أن كتاب المنطق الكبير» أكثره اقتباسات ونقولات من كتب ابن سينا إلا أن طريقة الرازي في التصنيف والتأليف جعلت من هذا الكتاب مصنفًا فريدا من نوعه، ويظهر ذلك من خلال المصطلحات التي نقلها إلى علمي الفقه والكلام، وطريقة تحليل النصوص والأخبار، فعلى سبيل المثال استخدم الرازي مصطلحي اللفظ المستعمل واللفظ المهمل بدلاً من اللفظ الدال واللفظ الغير الدال، وضمن الحقيقة والمجاز إلى مبحث الدلالة وكذلك ما تم ذكره في مقدمة كتابة الكبير المؤلف من مدخل وخمسة أقسام
The study and discourse, and that through his writing of books on logic such as 'Mi'yar al-Ilm', 'Mihakk al-Nazar', 'al-Mustasfa min Ilm al-Usul', 'al-Qistas al-Mustaqim', and 'Asas al-Qiyas'. Indeed, al-Ghazali considered logic among the religious sciences, and he introduced it into theology through his book 'Ihya' Ulum al-Din'. He said in al-Mustasfa: 'Whoever has not studied logic, his knowledge is not to be trusted.' As for the Shafi'i jurist and Ash'ari theologian Abd al-Qahir al-Baghdadi, who was a contemporary of Ibn Sina and who lived a quarter century before al-Ghazali, he coined in his book 'al-Ayn al-Nazar fi Ilm al-Jadal' the term 'people of dialectic' for the theologians and 'people of logic' for the philosophers, and he held that dialectic is superior to the logic of the philosophers. If we exclude some names like al-Suhrawardi al-Maqtul and Abu al-Barakat al-Baghdadi, then the logical works composed in the Islamic world after al-Ghazali were authored by the Ash'ari theologians. The Ash'ari theologians who came after al-Ghazali held that there is a necessary relationship between logic and theology. These theologians relied heavily in their logic on Ibn Sina's logical texts in his two books 'al-Shifa' and 'al-Isharat wa al-Tanbihat'. The period (from the beginning of the eleventh century to the end of the thirteenth century CE) is considered the period in which the Ash'ari theologians emerged prominently, and it is the golden age of the history of Islamic logic. Among the logicians who emerged in this period were Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, Sayf al-Din al-Amidi, Siraj al-Din al-Urmawi, Athir al-Din al-Abhari, Nasir al-Din al-Tusi, Afdal al-Din al-Khunji, Najm al-Din al-Katibi al-Qazwini, and Qutb al-Din al-Shirazi. Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, called 'al-Imam al-Sharh al-Fadil' (the virtuous commentator), was at the forefront of these logicians. Likewise, we find that Qutb al-Din al-Razi in his book 'al-Taqrir Sharh al-Shamsiyya' attributes to each of al-Farabi, Ibn Sina, and Fakhr al-Din al-Razi a doctrine and a logical school. Al-Shirazi established this result through tracing the influence of each of them on the circles and institutions of logical sciences. This led the logicians who came after Fakhr al-Razi (al-Abhari and al-Khunji) to consider him the Imam and that he had an independent logical school which they called the School of the Imam, and they argue with his statements and reports. The book of al-Razi, 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir', which is before us, is considered the largest and greatest book on logic authored after Ibn Sina's logical collection called 'al-Shifa'. It is the first book al-Razi wrote on logic. The proof of that is the attribution of some statements found in the commentaries and summaries he wrote on 'Uyun al-Hikma' and 'al-Isharat' to this book. Al-Razi relied heavily in this book on the sections of logic found in Ibn Sina's two books 'al-Shifa' and 'al-Isharat wa al-Tanbihat'. Although the book 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir' is mostly quotations and transmissions from Ibn Sina's books, al-Razi's method of classification and composition made this book a unique work. This is evident from the terms he transferred to the sciences of fiqh and kalam, and his method of analyzing texts and reports. For example, al-Razi used the terms 'used word' (al-lafz al-musta'mal) and 'unused word' (al-lafz al-muhmal) instead of 'signifying word' and 'non-signifying word', and he included 'truth and metaphor' (al-haqiqa wa al-majaz) in the topic of signification (al-dalala), as well as what was mentioned in the introduction of his great book, which consists of a preamble and five sections.
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage is an introductory historical overview of the relationship between logic (mantiq) and Islamic theology (kalam). The author begins by noting al-Ghazali's significant role: he wrote several logical works and considered logic a religious science, even integrating it into his theological masterpiece 'Ihya' Ulum al-Din'. Al-Ghazali's famous statement in 'al-Mustasfa' that one who does not study logic cannot be trusted in his knowledge shows his high regard for the discipline. The passage then contrasts an earlier figure, Abd al-Qahir al-Baghdadi, a contemporary of Ibn Sina, who distinguished between 'people of dialectic' (theologians) and 'people of logic' (philosophers), arguing for the superiority of dialectic. After al-Ghazali, however, the Ash'ari theologians took up logic enthusiastically, producing major works based on Ibn Sina's texts. The author describes the period from the 11th to 13th centuries CE as the golden age of Islamic logic, listing prominent logicians such as Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, al-Amidi, al-Abhari, al-Tusi, and others. Fakhr al-Din al-Razi is highlighted as the foremost among them, called 'al-Imam al-Sharh al-Fadil'. The passage then explains how later logicians like Qutb al-Din al-Shirazi recognized al-Farabi, Ibn Sina, and al-Razi as having distinct logical schools, with al-Razi's school being called the 'School of the Imam'. Finally, the author introduces al-Razi's book 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir', noting it is the largest logic work after Ibn Sina's 'al-Shifa' and was al-Razi's first logical composition. The book, though largely quoting Ibn Sina, is unique due to al-Razi's method of classification and his transfer of logical terms to fiqh and kalam, such as using 'used word' and 'unused word' instead of 'signifying/non-signifying', and incorporating truth and metaphor into the discussion of signification. The book's structure consists of a preamble and five sections.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ghazali elevated logic from a philosophical tool to a required religious science, integrating it into theology and usul al-fiqh.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
From Dialectic to Logic: The Ash'ari Shift
Contrasts early dialectic-centered approach with later logic-centered Ash'ari theology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to contrast al-Baghdadi's position on dialectic with the post-Ghazalian Ash'ari embrace of logic, and explain why the latter prevailed.

Core Idea
Ash'ari theologians transformed logic from a rival into an ally of orthodoxy after al-Ghazali.

This lesson examines the pivotal shift from viewing logic as a foreign discipline to accepting it as complementary to kalam. You will compare the earlier stance of Abd al-Qahir al-Baghdadi, who championed dialectic over philosophical logic, with the later Ash'ari consensus that logic and kalam are inseparable. The passage shows how al-Ghazali's work catalyzed this change.

Guided Path
1
Identify al-Baghdadi's distinction
Find where al-Baghdadi uses the terms 'أهل الجدل' (people of dialectic) for theologians and 'أهل المنطق' (people of logic) for philosophers. Note his conclusion that dialectic is superior.
This is found in his book 'عيار النظر في علم الجدل'.
2
Note the historical context
Al-Baghdadi was a contemporary of Ibn Sina, before al-Ghazali. At that time, logic was associated with philosophy, which was seen as potentially heretical.
3
Trace the post-Ghazali shift
The passage states that after al-Ghazali, logical works were authored by Ash'ari theologians. They held that there is a 'علاقة تلازم' (necessary relationship) between logic and kalam.
This phrase indicates a firm integration.
4
Identify the consequence
The shift led to the golden age of Islamic logic, with Ash'ari scholars producing major commentaries and textbooks based on Ibn Sina's works.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
The School of Imam al-Razi and al-Mantiq al-Kabir
Highlights Fakhr al-Din al-Razi's logical school and the unique features of his book al-Mantiq al-Kabir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the distinctive features of Fakhr al-Din al-Razi's logical school and describe the unique contributions of his book al-Mantiq al-Kabir.

Core Idea
Fakhr al-Din al-Razi created an independent logical school and a unique textbook that reworked Ibn Sina's logic for Islamic sciences.

This lesson focuses on the towering figure of Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, the 'Imam' of logical studies after Ibn Sina. You will explore his recognition as the founder of an independent school (مدرسة الإمام) and the characteristics of his magnum opus, al-Mantiq al-Kabir. The passage highlights how al-Razi adapted logical terminology for fiqh and kalam, making his work a bridge between philosophy and Islamic jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recognition of al-Razi's school
Find the statement that Qutb al-Din al-Shirazi attributed a distinct logical school to al-Razi, alongside al-Farabi and Ibn Sina. Note that later logicians like al-Abhari and al-Khunji adopted this 'School of the Imam'.
This elevates al-Razi to the level of the founding figures.
2
Note the scope of al-Mantiq al-Kabir
The passage calls it 'أضخم وأكبر كتاب في المنطق' after Ibn Sina's al-Shifa. It was al-Razi's first logical work, referenced in his later commentaries.
3
Identify the innovative features
Al-Razi transferred logical terms to fiqh and kalam, e.g., using 'اللفظ المستعمل' and 'اللفظ المهمل' instead of 'اللفظ الدال' and 'اللفظ غير الدال'. He also included the topic of haqiqa and majaz under signification.
This shows practical integration with Islamic legal theory.
4
Assess the book's composition
Despite heavy reliance on Ibn Sina, al-Razi's method of classification made the work unique. The structure includes a preamble and five sections.

عليها مدرسة الإمام ويحتجون بأقوالها وتقريراتها. كتاب الرازي المنطق الكبير الذي بين أيدينا يعتبر أضخم وأكبر كتاب في المنطق تم تأليفه بعد مجموعة ابن سينا المنطقية المسماة بـ«الشفاء»، وهو أول كتاب ألفه الرازي في علم المنطق، والدليل على ذلك نسبته بعض الأقوال الواردة في الشروح والملخصات التي كتبها على عيون الحكمة» و«الإشارات» إلى هذا الكتاب، وقد اعتمد الرازي في هذا الكتاب بشكل كبير على أقسام المنطق الموجودة في كتابي ابن سينا الشفاء» و«الإشارات والتنبيهات». على الرغم من أن كتاب المنطق الكبير» أكثره اقتباسات ونقولات من كتب ابن سينا إلا أن طريقة الرازي في التصنيف والتأليف جعلت من هذا الكتاب مصنفًا فريدا من نوعه، ويظهر ذلك من خلال المصطلحات التي نقلها إلى علمي الفقه والكلام، وطريقة تحليل النصوص والأخبار، فعلى سبيل المثال استخدم الرازي مصطلحي اللفظ المستعمل واللفظ المهمل بدلاً من اللفظ الدال واللفظ الغير الدال، وضمن الحقيقة والمجاز إلى مبحث الدلالة وكذلك ما تم ذكره في مقدمة كتابة الكبير المؤلف من مدخل وخمسة أقسام
The study and discourse, and that through his writing of books on logic such as 'Mi'yar al-Ilm', 'Mihakk al-Nazar', 'al-Mustasfa min Ilm al-Usul', 'al-Qistas al-Mustaqim', and 'Asas al-Qiyas'. Indeed, al-Ghazali considered logic among the religious sciences, and he introduced it into theology through his book 'Ihya' Ulum al-Din'. He said in al-Mustasfa: 'Whoever has not studied logic, his knowledge is not to be trusted.' As for the Shafi'i jurist and Ash'ari theologian Abd al-Qahir al-Baghdadi, who was a contemporary of Ibn Sina and who lived a quarter century before al-Ghazali, he coined in his book 'al-Ayn al-Nazar fi Ilm al-Jadal' the term 'people of dialectic' for the theologians and 'people of logic' for the philosophers, and he held that dialectic is superior to the logic of the philosophers. If we exclude some names like al-Suhrawardi al-Maqtul and Abu al-Barakat al-Baghdadi, then the logical works composed in the Islamic world after al-Ghazali were authored by the Ash'ari theologians. The Ash'ari theologians who came after al-Ghazali held that there is a necessary relationship between logic and theology. These theologians relied heavily in their logic on Ibn Sina's logical texts in his two books 'al-Shifa' and 'al-Isharat wa al-Tanbihat'. The period (from the beginning of the eleventh century to the end of the thirteenth century CE) is considered the period in which the Ash'ari theologians emerged prominently, and it is the golden age of the history of Islamic logic. Among the logicians who emerged in this period were Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, Sayf al-Din al-Amidi, Siraj al-Din al-Urmawi, Athir al-Din al-Abhari, Nasir al-Din al-Tusi, Afdal al-Din al-Khunji, Najm al-Din al-Katibi al-Qazwini, and Qutb al-Din al-Shirazi. Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, called 'al-Imam al-Sharh al-Fadil' (the virtuous commentator), was at the forefront of these logicians. Likewise, we find that Qutb al-Din al-Razi in his book 'al-Taqrir Sharh al-Shamsiyya' attributes to each of al-Farabi, Ibn Sina, and Fakhr al-Din al-Razi a doctrine and a logical school. Al-Shirazi established this result through tracing the influence of each of them on the circles and institutions of logical sciences. This led the logicians who came after Fakhr al-Razi (al-Abhari and al-Khunji) to consider him the Imam and that he had an independent logical school which they called the School of the Imam, and they argue with his statements and reports. The book of al-Razi, 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir', which is before us, is considered the largest and greatest book on logic authored after Ibn Sina's logical collection called 'al-Shifa'. It is the first book al-Razi wrote on logic. The proof of that is the attribution of some statements found in the commentaries and summaries he wrote on 'Uyun al-Hikma' and 'al-Isharat' to this book. Al-Razi relied heavily in this book on the sections of logic found in Ibn Sina's two books 'al-Shifa' and 'al-Isharat wa al-Tanbihat'. Although the book 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir' is mostly quotations and transmissions from Ibn Sina's books, al-Razi's method of classification and composition made this book a unique work. This is evident from the terms he transferred to the sciences of fiqh and kalam, and his method of analyzing texts and reports. For example, al-Razi used the terms 'used word' (al-lafz al-musta'mal) and 'unused word' (al-lafz al-muhmal) instead of 'signifying word' and 'non-signifying word', and he included 'truth and metaphor' (al-haqiqa wa al-majaz) in the topic of signification (al-dalala), as well as what was mentioned in the introduction of his great book, which consists of a preamble and five sections.
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage is an introductory historical overview of the relationship between logic (mantiq) and Islamic theology (kalam). The author begins by noting al-Ghazali's significant role: he wrote several logical works and considered logic a religious science, even integrating it into his theological masterpiece 'Ihya' Ulum al-Din'. Al-Ghazali's famous statement in 'al-Mustasfa' that one who does not study logic cannot be trusted in his knowledge shows his high regard for the discipline. The passage then contrasts an earlier figure, Abd al-Qahir al-Baghdadi, a contemporary of Ibn Sina, who distinguished between 'people of dialectic' (theologians) and 'people of logic' (philosophers), arguing for the superiority of dialectic. After al-Ghazali, however, the Ash'ari theologians took up logic enthusiastically, producing major works based on Ibn Sina's texts. The author describes the period from the 11th to 13th centuries CE as the golden age of Islamic logic, listing prominent logicians such as Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, al-Amidi, al-Abhari, al-Tusi, and others. Fakhr al-Din al-Razi is highlighted as the foremost among them, called 'al-Imam al-Sharh al-Fadil'. The passage then explains how later logicians like Qutb al-Din al-Shirazi recognized al-Farabi, Ibn Sina, and al-Razi as having distinct logical schools, with al-Razi's school being called the 'School of the Imam'. Finally, the author introduces al-Razi's book 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir', noting it is the largest logic work after Ibn Sina's 'al-Shifa' and was al-Razi's first logical composition. The book, though largely quoting Ibn Sina, is unique due to al-Razi's method of classification and his transfer of logical terms to fiqh and kalam, such as using 'used word' and 'unused word' instead of 'signifying/non-signifying', and incorporating truth and metaphor into the discussion of signification. The book's structure consists of a preamble and five sections.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Al-Razi's Mantiq Kabir: The Founding of the Third Logical School
Historical significance of al-Razi's logical school

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key historical factors that established al-Razi's logical school and distinguish it from earlier traditions.

Core Idea
Al-Razi founded the third major logical school in Islam, recognized as Madrasat al-Imam.

This lesson places al-Razi's Mantiq Kabir within the broader history of Islamic logic. You will learn how later logicians like al-Abhari and al-Khunaji regarded al-Razi as the Imam of a distinct school, and how his work became a benchmark after Ibn Sina's Shifa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three major logical schools mentioned by Qutb al-Din al-Shirazi
According to the passage, Qutb al-Din al-Shirazi in his Sharh al-Shamsiyya assigned distinct doctrines to al-Farabi, Ibn Sina, and Fakhr al-Razi. This shows that al-Razi was considered the founder of an independent tradition.
2
Trace the influence of al-Razi on later logicians (al-Abhari, al-Khunaji)
The passage states that these scholars regarded al-Razi as the Imam and called his school 'Madrasat al-Imam'. They argued using his statements and determinations.
3
Recognize the scale of al-Mantiq al-Kabir
It is the largest logic work after Ibn Sina's Shifa, indicating its significance as a comprehensive reference.
4
Compare al-Razi's relation to Ibn Sina with Ibn Rushd's relation to Aristotle
The passage draws an analogy to highlight al-Razi's role as an interpreter and expander of Avicennan logic.

في مبحث مستقل نظرًا لأهميته وتحليل مواضع الجدل والمغالطة والخطابة والشعر في مبحث واحد، هي أمور ضرورية ومهمة ويجب التنبيه عليها لما لها من أهمية كبيرة ، ومن جهة أخرى يمكننا النظر إلى كتاب المنطق الكبير على أنه أشبه ما يكون بتفسير وشرح دقيق وموسع لأقسام المنطق الموجودة في كتاب الشفاء، كما يمكننا القول أن كتاب «دقائق الحقائق» لسيف الدين الآمدي وكتاب «أساس الإقتباس» لنصير الدين الطوسي قد تم تأليفهما على نهج كتاب «المنطق الكبير». وبإمكاننا القول أن الرازي في كتابه المنطق الكبير» وفي كتبه المنطقية الأخرى ومن خلال شروحه لمؤلفات ابن سينا قدم إضافات كبيرة في سبيل توضيح علم المنطق وخاصة المنطق السينوي، وبالتالي يمكننا فهم العلاقة القوية بين الفخر الرازي وتراث ابن سينا، ويمكن تشبيه هذه العلاقة كالتفاعل الظاهر بين ابن رشد الحفيد وتراث أرسطو، وكتاب المنطق الكبير الذي بين أيدينا يؤيد ما ذكرناه. وبعد هذا التقديم البسيط لا بد من تقديم الشكر والامتنان للفخر الرازي على ما قدمه من مؤلفات وإضافات علمية منطقية مهمة، كما نبارك للأستاذ
The Great Logic and Qutb al-Din al-Shirazi. Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, called the Imam, the virtuous commentator, was at the forefront of these logicians. Likewise, we find that Qutb al-Din al-Razi in his book al-Taqrir 'Sharh al-Shamsiyya' assigns to each of al-Farabi, Ibn Sina, and Fakhr al-Razi a doctrine and logical school. Al-Shirazi established this conclusion by tracing the influence of each of them on the logical circles and scholarly environments. This made later logicians after Fakhr al-Razi (al-Abhari and al-Khunaji) consider him the Imam and that he had an independent logical school which they called the School of the Imam, and they argue with its statements and determinations. Al-Razi's book al-Mantiq al-Kabir which is before us is considered the largest and greatest book on logic composed after Ibn Sina's logical collection called 'al-Shifa'. It was the first book al-Razi authored in the science of logic. Evidence for this is that some statements contained in the commentaries and summaries he wrote on 'Uyun al-Hikma' and 'al-Isharat' are attributed to this book. Al-Razi relied heavily in this book on the sections of logic found in Ibn Sina's two books 'al-Shifa' and 'al-Isharat wa al-Tanbihat'. Although al-Mantiq al-Kabir mostly consists of quotations and transmissions from Ibn Sina's books, al-Razi's method of classification and composition made this book a unique work. This appears through the terminology he transferred to the sciences of fiqh and kalam, and the method of analyzing texts and reports. For example, al-Razi used the terms 'al-lafz al-musta'mal' (the used word) and 'al-lafz al-muhmal' (the neglected word) instead of 'al-lafz al-dall' (the indicative word) and 'al-lafz ghayr al-dall' (the non-indicative word), and he included truth (haqiqa) and metaphor (majaz) in the topic of signification (dalala). Likewise, what was mentioned in the introduction of his book, consisting of an entrance and five sections (or main branches) of analysis and definition of knowledge, and of explanation of the relationship between knowledge and happiness, and between knowledge and logic, which are considered original ideas. He also added new names for logical forms such as 'al-'urfiyya' and others. All these examples indicate the originality, distinction and uniqueness of this book. Al-Razi's study of the topic of syllogism (qiyas) from al-Shifa within the topic of argument (hujja) and his clarification of related positions, and his treatment of the topic of demonstration (burhan) – composed of five arts – in an independent topic due to its importance, and his analysis of the topics of dialectic, sophistry, rhetoric, and poetry in one topic, are necessary and important matters that must be noted for their great significance. On the other hand, we can view al-Mantiq al-Kabir as being akin to a detailed and expanded commentary on the sections of logic in al-Shifa. We can also say that the book 'Daqa'iq al-Haqa'iq' by Sayf al-Din al-Amidi and the book 'Asas al-Iqtibas' by Nasir al-Din al-Tusi were composed along the lines of al-Mantiq al-Kabir. We can also say that al-Razi, in his book al-Mantiq al-Kabir and in his other logical works, and through his commentaries on Ibn Sina's writings, made great contributions to clarifying the science of logic, especially Avicennan logic. Therefore, we can understand the strong relationship between Fakhr al-Razi and the legacy of Ibn Sina. This relationship can be compared to the apparent interaction between Ibn Rushd the grandson and the legacy of Aristotle. The book al-Mantiq al-Kabir before us supports what we have mentioned. After this brief introduction, it is necessary to offer thanks and gratitude to Fakhr al-Razi for his important logical works and contributions. We also congratulate the professor.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage is a modern scholarly introduction to Fakhr al-Din al-Razi's 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir'. It begins by situating al-Razi within the history of Islamic logic, noting that Qutb al-Din al-Shirazi (author of Sharh al-Shamsiyya) recognized three major logical schools: those of al-Farabi, Ibn Sina, and Fakhr al-Razi. Later logicians such as al-Abhari and al-Khunaji regarded al-Razi as the 'Imam' and formed a school around his teachings. The passage then describes the book itself: it is the largest work on logic after Ibn Sina's al-Shifa, and was al-Razi's first logical composition. It relies heavily on Ibn Sina's al-Shifa and al-Isharat. Despite being largely a compilation of quotations, al-Razi's originality is evident in his adaptation of terminology for Islamic sciences (e.g., using 'musta'mal' and 'muhmal' instead of 'dall' and 'ghayr dall'), his inclusion of truth and metaphor in signification, his introduction of new logical form names like 'urfiyya', and his structural reorganizations such as treating demonstration in a separate section and grouping dialectic, sophistry, rhetoric, and poetry together. The passage compares al-Razi's relation to Ibn Sina to that of Ibn Rushd to Aristotle. Finally, it offers thanks and praise to al-Razi and to the contemporary professor (the author of this study).

Al-Razi's Terminological Innovations in Logic
Terminological changes in al-Mantiq al-Kabir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify al-Razi's new terminology in logic and explain how they reflect an integration of Islamic sciences.

Core Idea
Al-Razi replaced traditional logical terms with ones adapted from fiqh and kalam, showing logic's relevance to Islamic sciences.

This lesson focuses on al-Razi's deliberate changes to logical vocabulary. You will examine his use of 'al-lafz al-musta'mal' and 'al-lafz al-muhmal' instead of 'dall' and 'ghayr dall', and his inclusion of truth and metaphor in signification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the traditional terms for indicative and non-indicative words
Earlier logicians used 'al-lafz al-dall' (indicative word) and 'al-lafz ghayr al-dall' (non-indicative word). These are standard in Avicennan logic.
2
Recognize al-Razi's replacement: 'musta'mal' and 'muhmal'
Al-Razi used 'al-lafz al-musta'mal' (the used word) and 'al-lafz al-muhmal' (the neglected word). This shifts focus from signification to usage, aligning with fiqh terminology.
3
Understand the inclusion of truth (haqiqa) and metaphor (majaz) under signification
By incorporating these linguistic categories into the topic of dalala, al-Razi connected logic with tafsir and usul al-fiqh, where distinguishing haqiqa and majaz is crucial.
4
Recognize the originality of these changes
The passage states that these terminological shifts are evidence of the uniqueness of his book, showing his attempt to make logic a tool for Islamic sciences rather than a purely Greek discipline.
