المنطق الكبير وقطب الدين الشيرازي، وقد كان فخر الدين الرازي المسمى بالإمام الشارح الفاضل) على رأس وطليعة هؤلاء المنطقيين. وكذلك نجد أن قطب الدين الرازي في كتابه التقرير «شرح الشمسية» يجعل لكل من الفارابي وابن سينا والفخر الرازي مذهبًا ومدرسة منطقية، وقد قرر الشيرازي هذه النتيجة من خلال تتبعه لتأثير كل شخص منهم على الأوساط والمحاضن العلمية المنطقية، وهو ما جعل المناطقة الذين جاؤوا بعد الفخر الرازي (الأبهري والخونجي) يعتبرونه الإمام وأن له مدرسة منطقية مستقلة يطلقون عليها مدرسة الإمام ويحتجون بأقوالها وتقريراتها. كتاب الرازي المنطق الكبير الذي بين أيدينا يعتبر أضخم وأكبر كتاب في المنطق تم تأليفه بعد مجموعة ابن سينا المنطقية المسماة بـ«الشفاء»، وهو أول كتاب ألفه الرازي في علم المنطق، والدليل على ذلك نسبته بعض الأقوال الواردة في الشروح والملخصات التي كتبها على عيون الحكمة» و«الإشارات» إلى هذا الكتاب، وقد اعتمد الرازي في هذا الكتاب بشكل كبير على أقسام المنطق الموجودة في كتابي ابن سينا الشفاء» و«الإشارات والتنبيهات». على الرغم من أن كتاب المنطق الكبير» أكثره اقتباسات ونقولات من كتب ابن سينا إلا أن طريقة الرازي في التصنيف والتأليف جعلت من هذا الكتاب مصنفًا فريدا من نوعه، ويظهر ذلك من خلال المصطلحات التي نقلها إلى علمي الفقه والكلام، وطريقة تحليل النصوص والأخبار، فعلى سبيل المثال استخدم الرازي مصطلحي اللفظ المستعمل واللفظ المهمل بدلاً من اللفظ الدال واللفظ الغير الدال، وضمن الحقيقة والمجاز إلى مبحث الدلالة وكذلك ما تم ذكره في مقدمة كتابة الكبير المؤلف من مدخل وخمسة أقسام الدراسة أو جمل رئيسية) من تحليل وتعريف للمعرفة ومن بيان العلاقة بين المعرفة والسعادة وبين المعرفة والمنطق ما يعتبر من الأفكار الأصيلة، كما أضاف تسميات جديدة للصيغ المنطقية كالعرفية وغيرها، كل هذه الأمثلة تدل على أصالة وتميّز وتفرد هذا الكتاب. وقيام الرازي بدراسة مبحث القياس من كتاب الشفاء في مبحث الحجة وبيان المواضع المتعلقة به، وتناول لمبحث البرهان – المؤلف من خمسة فنون - في مبحث مستقل نظرًا لأهميته وتحليل مواضع الجدل والمغالطة والخطابة والشعر في مبحث واحد، هي أمور ضرورية ومهمة ويجب التنبيه عليها لما لها من أهمية كبيرة ، ومن جهة أخرى يمكننا النظر إلى كتاب المنطق الكبير على أنه أشبه ما يكون بتفسير وشرح دقيق وموسع لأقسام المنطق الموجودة في كتاب الشفاء، كما يمكننا القول أن كتاب «دقائق الحقائق» لسيف الدين الآمدي وكتاب «أساس الإقتباس» لنصير الدين الطوسي قد تم تأليفهما على نهج كتاب «المنطق الكبير». وبإمكاننا القول أن الرازي في كتابه المنطق الكبير» وفي كتبه المنطقية الأخرى ومن خلال شروحه لمؤلفات ابن سينا قدم إضافات كبيرة في سبيل توضيح علم المنطق وخاصة المنطق السينوي، وبالتالي يمكننا فهم العلاقة القوية بين الفخر الرازي وتراث ابن سينا، ويمكن تشبيه هذه العلاقة كالتفاعل الظاهر بين ابن رشد الحفيد وتراث أرسطو، وكتاب المنطق الكبير الذي بين أيدينا يؤيد ما ذكرناه. وبعد هذا التقديم البسيط لا بد من تقديم الشكر والامتنان للفخر الرازي على ما قدمه من مؤلفات وإضافات علمية منطقية مهمة، كما نبارك للأستاذ
The Great Logic and Qutb al-Din al-Shirazi. Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, called the Imam, the virtuous commentator, was at the forefront of these logicians. Likewise, we find that Qutb al-Din al-Razi in his book al-Taqrir 'Sharh al-Shamsiyya' assigns to each of al-Farabi, Ibn Sina, and Fakhr al-Razi a doctrine and logical school. Al-Shirazi established this conclusion by tracing the influence of each of them on the logical circles and scholarly environments. This made later logicians after Fakhr al-Razi (al-Abhari and al-Khunaji) consider him the Imam and that he had an independent logical school which they called the School of the Imam, and they argue with its statements and determinations. Al-Razi's book al-Mantiq al-Kabir which is before us is considered the largest and greatest book on logic composed after Ibn Sina's logical collection called 'al-Shifa'. It was the first book al-Razi authored in the science of logic. Evidence for this is that some statements contained in the commentaries and summaries he wrote on 'Uyun al-Hikma' and 'al-Isharat' are attributed to this book. Al-Razi relied heavily in this book on the sections of logic found in Ibn Sina's two books 'al-Shifa' and 'al-Isharat wa al-Tanbihat'. Although al-Mantiq al-Kabir mostly consists of quotations and transmissions from Ibn Sina's books, al-Razi's method of classification and composition made this book a unique work. This appears through the terminology he transferred to the sciences of fiqh and kalam, and the method of analyzing texts and reports. For example, al-Razi used the terms 'al-lafz al-musta'mal' (the used word) and 'al-lafz al-muhmal' (the neglected word) instead of 'al-lafz al-dall' (the indicative word) and 'al-lafz ghayr al-dall' (the non-indicative word), and he included truth (haqiqa) and metaphor (majaz) in the topic of signification (dalala). Likewise, what was mentioned in the introduction of his book, consisting of an entrance and five sections (or main branches) of analysis and definition of knowledge, and of explanation of the relationship between knowledge and happiness, and between knowledge and logic, which are considered original ideas. He also added new names for logical forms such as 'al-'urfiyya' and others. All these examples indicate the originality, distinction and uniqueness of this book. Al-Razi's study of the topic of syllogism (qiyas) from al-Shifa within the topic of argument (hujja) and his clarification of related positions, and his treatment of the topic of demonstration (burhan) – composed of five arts – in an independent topic due to its importance, and his analysis of the topics of dialectic, sophistry, rhetoric, and poetry in one topic, are necessary and important matters that must be noted for their great significance. On the other hand, we can view al-Mantiq al-Kabir as being akin to a detailed and expanded commentary on the sections of logic in al-Shifa. We can also say that the book 'Daqa'iq al-Haqa'iq' by Sayf al-Din al-Amidi and the book 'Asas al-Iqtibas' by Nasir al-Din al-Tusi were composed along the lines of al-Mantiq al-Kabir. We can also say that al-Razi, in his book al-Mantiq al-Kabir and in his other logical works, and through his commentaries on Ibn Sina's writings, made great contributions to clarifying the science of logic, especially Avicennan logic. Therefore, we can understand the strong relationship between Fakhr al-Razi and the legacy of Ibn Sina. This relationship can be compared to the apparent interaction between Ibn Rushd the grandson and the legacy of Aristotle. The book al-Mantiq al-Kabir before us supports what we have mentioned. After this brief introduction, it is necessary to offer thanks and gratitude to Fakhr al-Razi for his important logical works and contributions. We also congratulate the professor.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage is a modern scholarly introduction to Fakhr al-Din al-Razi's 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir'. It begins by situating al-Razi within the history of Islamic logic, noting that Qutb al-Din al-Shirazi (author of Sharh al-Shamsiyya) recognized three major logical schools: those of al-Farabi, Ibn Sina, and Fakhr al-Razi. Later logicians such as al-Abhari and al-Khunaji regarded al-Razi as the 'Imam' and formed a school around his teachings. The passage then describes the book itself: it is the largest work on logic after Ibn Sina's al-Shifa, and was al-Razi's first logical composition. It relies heavily on Ibn Sina's al-Shifa and al-Isharat. Despite being largely a compilation of quotations, al-Razi's originality is evident in his adaptation of terminology for Islamic sciences (e.g., using 'musta'mal' and 'muhmal' instead of 'dall' and 'ghayr dall'), his inclusion of truth and metaphor in signification, his introduction of new logical form names like 'urfiyya', and his structural reorganizations such as treating demonstration in a separate section and grouping dialectic, sophistry, rhetoric, and poetry together. The passage compares al-Razi's relation to Ibn Sina to that of Ibn Rushd to Aristotle. Finally, it offers thanks and praise to al-Razi and to the contemporary professor (the author of this study).

Key Terms
اللفظ المستعمل
اللفظ المهمل
اللفظ الدال
الحقيقة
المجاز
الدلالة

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did al-Razi use instead of the term 'al-lafz al-dall'?
A) al-lafz al-majaz
B) al-lafz al-haqiqa
C) al-lafz al-musta'mal
D) al-lafz al-muhmal

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi's terminological innovations brought logic closer to the sciences of fiqh and kalam by adapting its vocabulary to Islamic scholarly discourse.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Find a passage in a usul al-fiqh text (e.g., al-Mustasfa by al-Ghazali) where the terms 'haqiqa' and 'majaz' are discussed. Explain how al-Razi's inclusion of these under signification would affect the logical analysis of the passage.
?
Translate al-Razi's innovation into a simple logical example: Given the phrase 'zayd is a lion', analyze it using al-Razi's framework: is it 'musta'mal' or 'muhmal'? Is it haqiqa or majaz? Explain.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
5 min
Structural Reorganization in al-Mantiq al-Kabir
Structural innovations in al-Mantiq al-Kabir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the unique organizational structure of al-Mantiq al-Kabir and explain how it differs from Ibn Sina's al-Shifa.

Core Idea
Al-Razi restructured the topics of logic by grouping non-demonstrative arts and treating demonstration independently.

This lesson examines al-Razi's structural choices in his magnum opus. You will see how he rearranged the material from Ibn Sina's Shifa to create a more systematic and practical organization, emphasizing demonstration and unifying the non-demonstrative arts.

Guided Path
1
Identify how al-Razi treated the topic of syllogism (qiyas) from al-Shifa
The passage says he studied qiyas from al-Shifa within the topic of argument (hujja) and clarified related positions. So he did not treat it in isolation but as part of a broader discussion of argumentation.
2
Note the independent treatment of demonstration (burhan)
Al-Razi dedicated a separate section to burhan, composed of five arts, because of its importance. This is a departure from the Shifa where demonstration is integrated within the logic section.
3
Recognize the grouping of dialectic, sophistry, rhetoric, and poetry in one topic
Unlike previous works that treated these separately, al-Razi combined them into a single section. This suggests he saw commonalities in their persuasive or non-apodictic nature.
4
Understand the overall structure: an introduction (madkhal) and five main sections (jumal)
The passage mentions the book consists of an entrance and five main branches, analyzing knowledge, its relation to happiness and logic. This shows a thematic organization that links logic to broader philosophical and ethical goals.

Commentary
This passage is a modern scholarly introduction to Fakhr al-Din al-Razi's 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir'. It begins by situating al-Razi within the history of Islamic logic, noting that Qutb al-Din al-Shirazi (author of Sharh al-Shamsiyya) recognized three major logical schools: those of al-Farabi, Ibn Sina, and Fakhr al-Razi. According to the passage, how did al-Razi treat the topic of burhan (demonstration) in al-Mantiq al-Kabir?

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Originality and Structure of al-Mantiq al-Kabir
Editor's claims on originality and structure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the original contributions of al-Mantiq al-Kabir and its unique organization of the five arts.

Core Idea
Al-Mantiq al-Kabir redefines concepts and reorganizes the five arts distinctively.

This lesson explores the editor's assessment of al-Mantiq al-Kabir. You will learn about its original ideas, such as new logical terminology, and its distinctive treatment of Qiyas, Burhan, and the other arts. Understanding this helps you appreciate the work's importance as a teaching text in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the editor's claims of originality
Read the passage and list the specific claims: new analysis of knowledge, new definitions, new terminology like 'al-urfiyya'.
Distinguish claims that are entirely new vs. refinements of previous ideas.
2
Examine the treatment of Qiyas
Note that Razi studied Qiyas from Ibn Sina's al-Shifa within his own section on al-Hujja. This indicates a direct engagement with the source.
Consider why he chose to embed it in a new section rather than replicate it.
3
Analyze the organization of the five arts
Observe that Burhan is treated independently, while Jadal, Mughalata, Khitaba, and Shi'r are combined into one section. Think about the logic behind this grouping.
Burhan (demonstration) is the most certain, so it warrants its own section.
4
Assess the pedagogical rationale
Reflect on why such original analysis and reorganization are important for a textbook. How does it facilitate learning?
The editor emphasizes that these features make the book a valuable teaching tool.

الدراسة أو جمل رئيسية من تحليل وتعريف للمعرفة ومن بيان العلاقة بين المعرفة والسعادة وبين المعرفة والمنطق ما يعتبر من الأفكار الأصيلة، كما أضاف تسميات جديدة للصيغ المنطقية كالعرفية وغيرها، كل هذه الأمثلة تدل على أصالة وتميّز وتفرد هذا الكتاب. وقيام الرازي بدراسة مبحث القياس من كتاب الشفاء في مبحث الحجة وبيان المواضع المتعلقة به، وتناول لمبحث البرهان – المؤلف من خمسة فنون - في مبحث مستقل نظرًا لأهميته وتحليل مواضع الجدل والمغالطة والخطابة والشعر في مبحث واحد، هي أمور ضرورية ومهمة ويجب التنبيه عليها لما لها من أهمية كبيرة
The study, or the main sentences, from analysis and definition of knowledge and from statement of the relationship between knowledge and happiness and between knowledge and logic, are considered original ideas. He also added new names for logical formulas such as 'al-'urfiyya' and others. All these examples indicate the originality, distinction, and uniqueness of this book. Al-Razi's undertaking of studying the subject of Qiyas from the book al-Shifa in the subject of al-Hujja and clarifying the relevant places, and his treatment of the subject of Burhan – consisting of five arts – in an independent subject due to its importance, and his analysis of the subjects of Jadal, Mughalata, Khitaba, and Shi'r in one subject, are necessary and important matters that must be pointed out because of their great importance.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage from the editor's introduction highlights two key features of al-Mantiq al-Kabir: its original contribution to logic through new analyses and terminology, and its detailed engagement with Ibn Sina's al-Shifa, specifically in the study of Qiyas and the treatment of Burhan and the other arts. The editor asserts that the book's originality lies in its analysis and definition of knowledge, the relationship between knowledge and happiness, and its novel terminologies like 'al-'urfiyya' (customary) logical forms. Then, the editor notes that al-Razi undertook a study of the section on Qiyas from al-Shifa within his own section on al-Hujja (the argument), and treated Burhan (demonstration) independently while combining Jadal (dialectic), Mughalata (sophistry), Khitaba (rhetoric), and Shi'r (poetics) in one section, indicating the book's systematic approach and importance as a teaching tool.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

How al-Mantiq al-Kabir Serves as a Commentary on Avicennan Logic
Editor explains the book's role as a commentary on al-Shifa and thanks those involved

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key features of a logical commentary (sharh) by analyzing how al-Mantiq al-Kabir builds upon Ibn Sina's al-Shifa and influences later texts.

Core Idea
Razi's al-Mantiq al-Kabir is a deep commentary clarifying Avicennan logic, not an independent treatise.

In this introductory passage, the editor explains that al-Mantiq al-Kabir functions as a precise and extensive commentary on the logical sections of Ibn Sina's al-Shifa. Understanding this relationship reveals how Razi engaged with the Avicennan legacy and how his work shaped later texts like al-Amidi's Daqa'iq al-Haqa'iq and al-Tusi's Asas al-Iqtibas. In this lesson, you will learn to identify the characteristics of a logical commentary within the Islamic tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base text (matn) and the commentary (sharh)
The editor states that al-Mantiq al-Kabir is like a tafsir and sharh of the logic sections of al-Shifa. So al-Shifa is the matn, al-Mantiq al-Kabir is the sharh.
2
Identify the relationship with later works
The passage says that Daqa'iq al-Haqa'iq and Asas al-Iqtibas were composed 'ala nahj (on the methodology) of al-Mantiq al-Kabir, meaning they follow its approach or structure.
3
Note the comparison with Ibn Rushd and Aristotle
The editor compares Razi's relationship to Ibn Sina with Ibn Rushd's relationship to Aristotle, highlighting that Razi is an interpreter who clarifies and extends the tradition. Identify what this comparison adds to our understanding.
4
Confirm the evidence from the text
The editor says 'The book al-Mantiq al-Kabir which we have confirms what we have mentioned.' This reminds us to always refer back to the primary source as evidence.

ومن جهة أخرى يمكننا النظر إلى كتاب المنطق الكبير على أنه أشبه ما يكون بتفسير وشرح دقيق وموسع لأقسام المنطق الموجودة في كتاب الشفاء، كما يمكننا القول أن كتاب «دقائق الحقائق» لسيف الدين الآمدي وكتاب «أساس الإقتباس» لنصير الدين الطوسي قد تم تأليفهما على نهج كتاب «المنطق الكبير». وبإمكاننا القول أن الرازي في كتابه المنطق الكبير وفي كتبه المنطقية الأخرى ومن خلال شروحه لمؤلفات ابن سينا قدم إضافات كبيرة في سبيل توضيح علم المنطق وخاصة المنطق السينوي، وبالتالي يمكننا فهم العلاقة القوية بين الفخر الرازي وتراث ابن سينا، ويمكن تشبيه هذه العلاقة كالتفاعل الظاهر بين ابن رشد الحفيد وتراث أرسطو، وكتاب المنطق الكبير الذي بين أيدينا يؤيد ما ذكرناه. وبعد هذا التقديم البسيط لا بد من تقديم الشكر والامتنان للفخر الرازي على ما قدمه من مؤلفات وإضافات علمية منطقية مهمة، كما نبارك للأستاذ المشارك الدكتور طور غود آق يوز الذي توسع في دراسة هذه المؤلفات والذي أعد هذا الكتاب للنشر بعد أن قام بدراسة مخطوطات المنطق الكبير التي لم يصل إلى أيدينا سوى نسخة واحدة منها فقط دراسة دقيقة وذلك على شكل أطروحة علمية نال على إثرها درجة الدكتوراه. ٢٠٢١/٠٧/٣٠ أ.د. علي دوروسوي كلية الشريعة / جامعة مرمرة رئيس قسم الفلسفة والعلوم الدينية
On the other hand, we can view the book al-Mantiq al-Kabir as resembling an interpretation and a precise and extensive commentary on the sections of logic found in the book al-Shifa. We can also say that the book 'Daqa'iq al-Haqa'iq' by Sayf al-Din al-Amidi and the book 'Asas al-Iqtibas' by Nasir al-Din al-Tusi were composed in the methodology of the book 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir'. And we can say that al-Razi, in his book al-Mantiq al-Kabir and in his other logical works, and through his commentaries on the works of Ibn Sina, made significant additions in clarifying the science of logic, especially Avicennan logic. Consequently, we can understand the strong relationship between Fakhr al-Razi and the heritage of Ibn Sina, and this relationship can be likened to the apparent interaction between Ibn Rushd the grandson and the heritage of Aristotle. The book al-Mantiq al-Kabir which we have confirms what we have mentioned. After this brief introduction, it is necessary to offer thanks and gratitude to Fakhr al-Razi for what he provided of important logical works and contributions. We also congratulate the associate professor Dr. Turğ Güç Ay Yüz, who expanded on the study of these works and prepared this book for publication after conducting a precise study of the manuscripts of al-Mantiq al-Kabir, of which only one copy has reached us, in the form of a scientific thesis for which he received his doctorate. 30/07/2021. Prof. Dr. Ali Durusoy, Faculty of Sharia, Marmara University, Head of the Department of Philosophy and Religious Sciences.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage continues the editor's introduction, clarifying the nature of al-Mantiq al-Kabir as a detailed commentary on the logical sections of Ibn Sina's al-Shifa. It also notes the influence of this work on later important texts: Daqa'iq al-Haqa'iq by al-Amidi and Asas al-Iqtibas by al-Tusi, both composed following its methodology. The editor then emphasizes al-Razi's significant contributions to clarifying Avicennan logic through his commentaries and compares his relationship to Ibn Sina with that of Ibn Rushd to Aristotle, highlighting the depth of intellectual engagement. Finally, the editor expresses gratitude to Fakhr al-Razi and acknowledges the scholarly work of Dr. Turğ Güç Ay Yüz, whose doctoral thesis involved a meticulous study of the only known manuscript, leading to this publication. The passage concludes with the date and signature of the editor, Prof. Dr. Ali Durusoy.

The Significance of Critical Editions in Islamic Logic
Editor introduces the importance of al-Razi's work and the editorial process.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the significance of Fakhr al-Din al-Razi's al-Mantiq al-Kabir and explain why critical editions are essential for Islamic logic research.

Core Idea
Al-Razi's al-Mantiq al-Kabir, unpublished for centuries, is now accessible through a critical edition — a key to the Islamic logical tradition.

The passage you are about to read is the editor's preface to the first critical edition of al-Mantiq al-Kabir. It sets the stage by highlighting the author's stature and the manuscript's rarity. Understanding this context prepares you to appreciate the value of critical editions and the effort required to revive classical texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and work
Locate the name of the author and the title of the work in the Arabic passage. What is al-Mantiq al-Kabir and who wrote it?
The author is Fakhr al-Din al-Razi (d. 606/1210).
2
Assess the work's importance
Notice how the editor describes al-Razi: 'one of the most prominent philosophers in the Islamic logical tradition' who influenced later writings. Why was his work so influential?
Al-Razi integrated philosophy with kalam, shaping subsequent Islamic logic.
3
Understand the editorial challenge
Find the phrase indicating the number of manuscript copies available. What does it mean that only one manuscript exists? How does this affect the editorial process?
The editor states 'we obtained only a single manuscript copy' – a rare situation requiring meticulous work.
4
Recognize the purpose of the edition
Read the editor's goal: to contribute to the development of studies and research in Islamic logic. How does publishing this text achieve that?
By making the text accessible, scholars can analyze al-Razi's logical system and its place in the tradition.

يعد فخر الدين الرازي (ت: ٦٠٦ هـ / (۱٢١٠م)، أحد أبرز الفلاسفة في التراث المنطقي الإسلامي، وهو من الذين أثروا على محتوى ونطاق الكتابات المنطقية اللاحقة، ونظرًا لعظم أثره؛ تسابق الناس إلى نشر أعماله، حتى أصبحت أعماله محل اهتمام في الأبحاث وفي المراكز الأكاديمية المختلفة. وبالرغم من ذلك، ظل بعضها - على أهميته - رهين أدراج المخطوطات، لم ينشر بعد؛ ومنها الكتاب المسمى بعنوان «المنطق الكبير». وقد سعينا في نشره كي نلفت انتباه مراكز البحث العلمي إليه في عصرنا الحالي، ومن الضروري أن ننبه أننا لم نتحصل إلا على نسخة مخطوطة واحدة فقط من الكتاب. وقد بذلنا قصارى جهدنا لتقديم نشرة علمية بمنهج أكاديمي متقن في تحقيقنا لهذه المخطوطة الفريدة والنادرة. وقد قمنا بدراسة وتحقيق وتحرير هذه المخطوطة خلال مرحلة الدكتوراه بإشراف ثلة من فضلاء الأكاديميين؛ ولهذا نهدف من خلال هذه النشرة العلمية المحققة لكتاب المنطق الكبير أن نُقدَّم للأوساط العلمية والأكاديمية المختصة نصًا يساهم في تطور الدراسات والأبحاث في المنطق الإسلامي.
ولقد ساهم العديد من القامات العلمية والأكاديمية بالإشراف على هذه العمل، أولهم بلا شك : هو الأستاذ الدكتور علي دوروسوي؛ حيث قابلنا معه المخطوطة بشكل كامل لعدة مرات، وقد قام - أيضًا - بالمقابلة الأخيرة لها وأجرى عليها قلم التصحيح والتصويب والترجيح، ونحن نقدم عظيم امتناننا وتقديرنا الخاص له ثانيهم: الأستاذ الدكتور إحسان فضل أوغلو، ومساعده الأستاذ الدكتور فـروح أوزبيلا وجي؛ فقد ساعدانا في الحصول
Al-Mantiq al-Kabir. Associate Professor Dr. Turgut Akkoyun, who extensively studied these works and prepared this book for publication after conducting a detailed study of the manuscripts of al-Mantiq al-Kabir—of which only a single copy has reached us—in the form of a doctoral dissertation, thereby obtaining his PhD. 30/07/2021. Prof. Dr. Ali Durusoy, Faculty of Theology, Marmara University, Head of the Department of Philosophy and Religious Sciences. The Study 11. Preface. Fakhr al-Din al-Razi (d. 606 AH / 1210 CE) is considered one of the most prominent philosophers in the Islamic logical tradition, and he is among those who influenced the content and scope of subsequent logical writings. Due to his great impact, people vied to publish his works, to the extent that his works became the focus of research and various academic centers. Despite this, some of his works—despite their importance—remained confined to manuscript drawers, unpublished; among them is the book titled 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir'. We sought to publish it to draw the attention of scientific research centers to it in our current era. It is necessary to note that we obtained only a single manuscript copy of the book. We exerted our utmost effort to present a critical edition with a meticulous academic methodology in our editing of this unique and rare manuscript. We studied, edited, and prepared this manuscript during our doctoral studies under the supervision of a group of distinguished academics. Hence, through this critical edition of al-Mantiq al-Kabir, we aim to provide the specialized scientific and academic circles with a text that contributes to the development of studies and research in Islamic logic. Many scientific and academic figures contributed to supervising this work; the first of them, undoubtedly, is Professor Dr. Ali Durusoy. He reviewed the manuscript with us in its entirety several times, and he also conducted the final collation, applying corrections, adjustments, and preferences. We express our immense gratitude and special appreciation to him. Secondly, Professor Dr. Ihsan Fazlıoğlu and his assistant Professor Dr. Ferruh Özpelaycı, who helped us in obtaining...

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the critical edition of al-Mantiq al-Kabir. It first acknowledges the editor's academic background and the date. Then it presents a preface (تمهيد) that establishes the importance of Fakhr al-Din al-Razi within Islamic logic, highlighting his influence and the widespread attention his works have received. Despite this, the author notes that some of al-Razi's works, including 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir', remained unpublished. The editor explains that they obtained a single manuscript and undertook the task of producing a critical edition, aiming to benefit Islamic logic research. The preface concludes by thanking key supervisors: Prof. Dr. Ali Durusoy, Prof. Dr. Ihsan Fazlıoğlu, and his assistant Prof. Dr. Ferruh Özpelaycı, for their contributions to the project. The tone is scholarly and appreciative, setting the context for the edition.

Evaluating a Critical Edition: The Editor's Preface
Editor introduces the work and editorial methodology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key scholarly contributions and editorial methods described in the preface of a critical edition of an Islamic logic text.

Core Idea
Critical editions of manuscripts are foundational for rigorous study of Islamic logic.

This lesson examines the editor's preface to the critical edition of al-Mantiq al-Kabir. You will learn why this work is significant, what challenges the editor faced, and how a critical edition (tahqiq) is produced. Understanding the preface helps you evaluate the reliability and methodology of any scholarly edition you use in your studies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Author and His Significance
The preface states that Fakhr al-Din al-Razi (d. 606 AH) is one of the most prominent philosophers in Islamic logic. Note that his works influenced later writings and that many remain unpublished. This tells you that al-Mantiq al-Kabir is a major but previously unavailable text.
2
Recognize the Manuscript Status
The editor mentions that only one manuscript copy was obtained. This is crucial: a single manuscript means the edition relies heavily on the editor's corrections and judgment, making the tahqiq process especially important.
3
Understand the Editorial Methodology
The editor describes a meticulous academic process: the manuscript was studied, critically edited, and prepared during a doctoral project under supervision. Multiple scholars reviewed and corrected it. This shows the collaborative and rigorous nature of a critical edition.
4
Appreciate the Collaborative Effort
A long list of acknowledgments indicates that producing a critical edition is a team effort involving supervisors, manuscript providers, reviewers, and publishers. This highlights the scholarly community's role in preserving and transmitting knowledge.

يعد فخر الدين الرازي (ت: ٦٠٦ هـ / ١٢١٠م)، أحد أبرز الفلاسفة في التراث المنطقي الإسلامي، وهو من الذين أثروا على محتوى ونطاق الكتابات المنطقية اللاحقة، ونظرًا لعظم أثره؛ تسابق الناس إلى نشر أعماله، حتى أصبحت أعماله محل اهتمام في الأبحاث وفي المراكز الأكاديمية المختلفة. وبالرغم من ذلك، ظل بعضها - على أهميته - رهين أدراج المخطوطات، لم ينشر بعد؛ ومنها الكتاب المسمى بعنوان «المنطق الكبير». وقد سعينا في نشره كي نلفت انتباه مراكز البحث العلمي إليه في عصرنا الحالي، ومن الضروري أن ننبه أننا لم نتحصل إلا على نسخة مخطوطة واحدة فقط من الكتاب. وقد بذلنا قصارى جهدنا لتقديم نشرة علمية بمنهج أكاديمي متقن في تحقيقنا لهذه المخطوطة الفريدة والنادرة. وقد قمنا بدراسة وتحقيق وتحرير هذه المخطوطة خلال مرحلة الدكتوراه بإشراف ثلة من فضلاء الأكاديميين؛ ولهذا نهدف من خلال هذه النشرة العلمية المحققة لكتاب المنطق الكبير أن نُقدَّم للأوساط العلمية والأكاديمية المختصة نصًا يساهم في تطور الدراسات والأبحاث في المنطق الإسلامي. ولقد ساهم العديد من القامات العلمية والأكاديمية بالإشراف على هذه العمل، أولهم بلا شك : هو الأستاذ الدكتور علي دوروسوي؛ حيث قابلنا معه المخطوطة بشكل كامل لعدة مرات، وقد قام - أيضًا - بالمقابلة الأخيرة لها وأجرى عليها قلم التصحيح والتصويب والترجيح، ونحن نقدم عظيم امتناننا وتقديرنا الخاص له ثانيهم: الأستاذ الدكتور إحسان فضل أوغلو، ومساعده الأستاذ الدكتور فـروح أوزبيلا وجي؛ فقد ساعدانا في الحصول على عدد من المخطوطات. وتجدر الإشارة كذلك إلى البروفيسور الدكتور الدين ماجيت، والأستاذ الدكتور حسن حاجاك، والأستاذ الدكتور إبراهيم جاباك، والدكتور والخبير حسن تتيك، ومساعد الباحث عليَّة كولر، والسيدة فرانزيسكا كنوبل، والسيد زين العابدين بن خياط الزوقري؛ حيث قدموا مساهمات مباشرة وغير مباشرة في ظهور هذه الطبعة الفريدة لكتاب المنطق الكبير، ونحن بذلك ممتنون لمساهماتهم. وأخيرا، يجب أن نشكر البروفيسور الدكتور أولريج رودولف، وكذلك محرري دار فارس – لبعث التراث وتأصيل الفكر - الذين نقدر مساعيهم لنشر الكتاب. الدكتور/ طورغود آق يوز مدرّس المنطق في كلية الشريعة (الإلهيات) جامعة أرزنجان بن علي ييلديرم – تركيا Assoc. Prof. Turgut AKYUZ University of Erzincan Binali Yildirim Faculty of Theology, Department of Logic
Fakhr al-Din al-Razi (d. 606 AH / 1210 CE) is considered one of the most prominent philosophers in the Islamic logical heritage, and he is among those who influenced the content and scope of later logical writings. Due to the greatness of his impact, people competed to publish his works, so much so that his works became a subject of interest in research and various academic centers. Despite this, some of them - despite their importance - remained confined to manuscript drawers, unpublished; among them is the book titled 'Al-Mantiq al-Kabir'. We have endeavored to publish it in order to draw the attention of scientific research centers to it in our present era. It is necessary to note that we only obtained one manuscript copy of the book. We have exerted our utmost effort to produce a scientific edition with a meticulous academic methodology in our critical edition of this unique and rare manuscript. We studied, critically edited, and prepared this manuscript during our doctoral phase under the supervision of a group of distinguished academics. Through this scholarly critical edition of 'Al-Mantiq al-Kabir', we aim to present to the scientific and specialized academic circles a text that contributes to the development of studies and research in Islamic logic. Many academic figures contributed to supervising this work, foremost among them being Prof. Dr. Ali Dorusoy; we reviewed the manuscript with him several times in full, and he also conducted the final review and applied the pen of correction, emendation, and preference. We offer our great gratitude and special appreciation to him. Secondly: Prof. Dr. Ihsan Fazlioglu and his assistant Prof. Dr. Ferruh Ozpilic; they helped us obtain a number of manuscripts. Also worth mentioning are Prof. Dr. Elmin Magit, Prof. Dr. Hasan Hacak, Prof. Dr. Ibrahim Çapak, Dr. and Expert Hasan Tetik, Research Assistant Aliye Kuler, Ms. Franziska Knobloch, and Mr. Zayn al-Abidin bin Khayyat al-Zuqari; they made direct and indirect contributions to the appearance of this unique edition of 'Al-Mantiq al-Kabir', and we are grateful for their contributions. Finally, we must thank Prof. Dr. Ulrich Rudolph, as well as the editors of Dar Faris – for the revival of heritage and rooting of thought – who we appreciate for their efforts to publish the book. Dr. Turgut Akyuz, Lecturer of Logic at the Faculty of Theology (Ilahiyat), Erzincan Binali Yildirim University – Turkey. Assoc. Prof. Turgut AKYUZ, University of Erzincan Binali Yildirim, Faculty of Theology, Department of Logic.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is the editor's preface to the critical edition of Al-Mantiq al-Kabir. The editor begins by emphasizing the importance of Fakhr al-Din al-Razi in Islamic logic, noting that his works are widely studied yet some remain unpublished, including the present book. He explains that he used a single manuscript and aimed for a meticulous academic edition. He then acknowledges various scholars who supervised or assisted in the project, such as Ali Dorusoy, Ihsan Fazlioglu, and others. The preface concludes with thanks to Ulrich Rudolph and the publisher. The tone is formal and grateful, reflecting the collaborative effort behind the edition.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Key Figures in Islamic Logic
Overview of key figures in Islamic logic

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the contributions of Aristotle, al-Farabi, Ibn Sina, Ibn Hazm, al-Ghazali, and Fakhr al-Din al-Razi to the development of logic in Islamic civilization.

Core Idea
Logic's journey from Aristotle to Razi is a story of integration into Islamic sciences.

This passage introduces you to the intellectual giants who shaped Islamic logic. Each figure built upon the previous, transforming logic from a Greek import into an essential tool for Islamic scholarship. Understanding their roles helps you appreciate why logic became central to Kalam, Fiqh, and Usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the founder
Locate Aristotle in the text. He is called al-Mu'allim al-Awwal (the First Teacher). Note that he established the foundations of logic.
2
Trace the Islamic revival
Find al-Farabi (al-Mu'allim al-Thani). He rebuilt logic in the Islamic context. Notice the progression: from Aristotle to al-Farabi, logic was revived.
3
Recognize the systematizer
Ibn Sina (al-Shaykh al-Ra'is) refined and ordered classical logic. He removed obscurities and systematized the rules.
4
Note the legitimizers
Ibn Hazm and al-Ghazali worked to make logic acceptable and useful for religious sciences. Ibn Hazm used everyday language and fiqh examples; al-Ghazali integrated logic into Kalam and Usul.
5
Identify the completer
Fakhr al-Din al-Razi completed the work of his predecessors. He is called Khatimat al-Muhaqqiqin (Seal of Investigators). Understand that he represents the culmination of this historical development.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدراسة
المقدمة |
أرسى أرسطو (ت: ۳۲۲ ق.م) قواعد وأسس علم المنطق؛ وعرف بعدها باسم المعلم الأول ، وأعاد الفارابي (ت: ٣٣٩ هـ / ٩٥٠م) بناء قواعد هذا العلم في الحضارة الإسلامية وعرف بفضل هذه الجهود باسم «المعلم الثاني»، وقام بعد ذلك ابن سينا (ت: ٤٢٩ هـ / ١٠٣٧م) بتهذيب وترتيب أبوابه، من خلال إزالة غوامضه وترتيب قواعده، ونظم بذلك قواعد المنطق الكلاسيكي، و بسبب دوره وجهوده المتميزة ومعارفه المتكاملة المتنوعة استحق وبجدارة لقب الشيخ الرئيس .
وخلال الفترة التي أعقبت ابن سينا، حاول ابن حزم الأندلسي (ت: ٤٥٦ هـ / ١٠٦٤م)، وهو أحد أعلام و مجددي المذهب الظاهري، إضفاء الشرعية على المنطق والاستفادة منه في العلوم الدينية من خلال كتابه «التقريب لحد المنطق والمدخل إليه بالألفاظ العامية والأمثلة الفقهية».
ومن ثم قام الغزالي (ت: ٥٠٥هـ / ١١١١م) ببذل بعض الجهود والمساعي للحفاظ على هذه النتائج والسعي لتطويرها، وهو مؤلف معيار العلم والمستصفى»؛ حيث قام بإدخال المنطق في العلوم الإسلامية واستخدامه كآلة في علم الكلام والفقه والأصول. أرست أعمال ابن حزم والغزالي المنطقية الأسس التي أدت لظهور فخر الدين الرازي (ت: ٦٠٦ هـ / ١٢١٠م). وبعبارة أخرى، أكمل فخر الدين الرازي النشاط الذي بدأه ابن حزم والغزالي. وبسبب هذه الجهود المبذولة والمتميزة اعتبر فخر الدين الرازي «الإمام» في هذا الفن ولذلك قد أطلق عليه المناطقة الإسلاميين خاتمة المحققين - أفضل المتأخرين»(۱).
(۱) سراج الدين الآرموي، مطالع الأنوار، ۱۳ .
The Study | Introduction | Aristotle (d. 322 BCE) established the rules and foundations of the science of logic; after that he became known as the First Teacher. Al-Farabi (d. 339 AH / 950 CE) rebuilt the rules of this science in Islamic civilization and became known, due to these efforts, as the 'Second Teacher.' Then Ibn Sina (d. 429 AH / 1037 CE) refined and arranged its sections, by removing its obscurities and ordering its rules, and thereby systematized the rules of classical logic, and because of his distinguished role and efforts and his diverse integrated knowledge, he deserved and by merit the title of al-Shaykh al-Ra'is. During the period after Ibn Sina, Ibn Hazm al-Andalusi (d. 456 AH / 1064 CE), one of the prominent figures and renewers of the Zahiri school, attempted to legitimize logic and benefit from it in religious sciences through his book 'al-Taqrib li-Hadd al-Mantiq wa al-Madkhal ilayhi bi al-Alfaz al-'Ammiyya wa al-Amthila al-Fiqhiyya.' Then al-Ghazali (d. 505 AH / 1111 CE) made some efforts and endeavors to preserve these results and seek to develop them; he is the author of 'Mi'yar al-'Ilm' and 'al-Mustasfa'; he introduced logic into the Islamic sciences and used it as a tool in Kalam, Fiqh, and Usul. The logical works of Ibn Hazm and al-Ghazali established the foundations that led to the emergence of Fakhr al-Din al-Razi (d. 606 AH / 1210 CE). In other words, Fakhr al-Din al-Razi completed the activity begun by Ibn Hazm and al-Ghazali. And because of these distinguished efforts, Fakhr al-Din al-Razi was considered the 'Imam' in this art, and therefore the Islamic logicians called him 'Khatimat al-Muhaqqiqin - Afdal al-Muta'akhkhirin' (Seal of the Investigators - Best of the Later Scholars). (1) Siraj al-Din al-Urmawi, Matali' al-Anwar, 13.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage is an introduction summarizing the historical development of logic, particularly within Islamic civilization. It begins by acknowledging Aristotle as the founder of logic, known as the 'First Teacher' (al-Mu'allim al-Awwal). Then it highlights al-Farabi, who rebuilt the discipline in the Islamic context earning the title 'Second Teacher' (al-Mu'allim al-Thani). Ibn Sina (Avicenna) refined and systematized classical logic, earning the honorific 'al-Shaykh al-Ra'is' (the Chief Master). The passage then discusses subsequent figures: Ibn Hazm, who sought to legitimize logic for religious sciences using everyday language and legal examples; al-Ghazali, who integrated logic into Islamic theology (Kalam) and jurisprudence (Usul al-Fiqh) as a tool. These efforts paved the way for Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, who completed and perfected the integration of logic into Islamic sciences, earning the titles 'Imam' and 'Khatimat al-Muhaqqiqin – Afdal al-Muta'akhkhirin' (the Seal of Investigators, the Best of the Later Scholars). The footnote references Siraj al-Din al-Urmawi's Matali' al-Anwar, indicating the source of the last epithet.

Key Terms
المعلم الأول
المعلم الثاني
الشيخ الرئيس
خاتمة المحققين - أفضل المتأخرين
فخر الدين الرازي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who is referred to as 'al-Shaykh al-Ra'is' in the passage?
A) Aristotle
B) Al-Farabi
C) Ibn Sina
D) Fakhr al-Din al-Razi

Key Takeaway
The development of Islamic logic passed through distinct phases: foundation (Aristotle), revival (al-Farabi), systematization (Ibn Sina), legitimization (Ibn Hazm, al-Ghazali), and culmination (Fakhr al-Din al-Razi).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Create a timeline of the six figures mentioned (Aristotle, al-Farabi, Ibn Sina, Ibn Hazm, al-Ghazali, Fakhr al-Din al-Razi) and for each, write one sentence on their specific contribution to logic.
?
Look up the book title 'al-Taqrib li-Hadd al-Mantiq' by Ibn Hazm. Explain how using 'everyday words and legal examples' (al-alfaz al-'ammiyya wa al-amthila al-fiqhiyya) reflects his strategy to make logic accessible for religious scholars.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Integrating Logic into Islamic Sciences
Integration of logic into Islamic sciences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how Ibn Hazm and al-Ghazali contributed to legitimizing and integrating logic into Islamic religious sciences, and how Fakhr al-Din al-Razi completed that integration.

Core Idea
Logic became indispensable to Islamic sciences through the efforts of Ibn Hazm, al-Ghazali, and al-Razi.

This passage highlights a crucial turn: logic was not only translated into Arabic but also actively integrated into Islamic disciplines. Ibn Hazm made it accessible with everyday language and fiqh examples, al-Ghazali made it a tool for Kalam and Usul, and al-Razi perfected its application. This lesson focuses on that integration process.

Guided Path
1
Locate Ibn Hazm's contribution
Ibn Hazm wrote 'al-Taqrib li-Hadd al-Mantiq' to legitimize logic. Notice he used 'everyday words and legal examples' to make it relatable for jurists.
2
Locate al-Ghazali's contribution
Al-Ghazali wrote 'Mi'yar al-'Ilm' and 'al-Mustasfa'. He 'introduced logic into the Islamic sciences and used it as a tool in Kalam, Fiqh, and Usul.' Understand that he made logic a methodological instrument.
3
Identify al-Razi's role
Fakhr al-Din al-Razi 'completed the activity begun by Ibn Hazm and al-Ghazali.' He is called the 'Imam' and 'Seal of Investigators.' His work represents the full acceptance of logic in Islamic scholarship.
4
Summarize the integration
Combine the steps: logic went from being a foreign science to an essential part of Islamic education. Think about how this affects studying texts like al-Razi's 'Muhassal' or al-Ghazali's 'Mustasfa'.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

Fakhr al-Din al-Razi's Place in Islamic Logic
Author introduces al-Razi's importance and his independent school.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three schools of Islamic logicians according to Qutb al-Din al-Razi and explain what distinguishes al-Razi's school.

Core Idea
Al-Razi founded his own school of logic alongside al-Farabi and Ibn Sina.

This lesson introduces you to the historical context of Islamic logic. The passage you are about to read establishes Fakhr al-Din al-Razi as a major figure who developed his own positions on key logical concepts, leading later scholars to recognize a distinct Razi school. Understanding this will help you situate his works within the broader tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three schools
The text mentions schools of al-Farabi, Ibn Sina, and al-Razi. Locate these names in the passage.
Look for the phrases 'مدرسة المعلم الثاني الفارابي' and 'مدرسة الشيخ الرئيس ابن سينا' and 'مدرسة الإمام فخر الدين الرازي'.
2
Note al-Razi's independent positions
Find the two logical issues where al-Razi held his own definitions: tasawwur/tasdiq and 'aks (simple conversion and contrapositive).
The text explicitly mentions 'تعريف التصور والتصديق، وكذلك تعريف العكس المستوى والعكس النقيض'.
3
Understand the significance
Qutb al-Din al-Razi uses these independent positions to classify al-Razi as a separate school. Ask yourself: why does this matter for studying Islamic logic?
It shows that al-Razi is not merely a commentator but an original thinker.
4
Apply to later study
When you encounter a logical work, checking which school it follows can clarify its doctrinal background.
This classification helps in understanding later commentaries and debates.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالنظر إلى مصنفات فخر الدين الرازي في المنطق، يمكن اعتباره من أكبر الشخصيات العلمية التي أثرت في العالم الإسلامي بعد الفارابي وابن سينا. ومن خلال تبنيه لمدرسة المنطق السينوي، التي لقب مؤسسها من قبل البعض بـ «الشيخ الرئيس وقد اختار الخواجة نصير الدين الطوسي (ت: ٦٧٢هـ / ۱۲۷٤م) للفخر الرازي لقب؛ الشارح الفاضل). وبالإضافة إلى ذلك، نجد قطب الدين الرازي التحتاني (ت: ٧٦٦هـ / ١٣٦٥م) يشير إلى إن فخر الدين الرازي لديه آراؤه واختياراته الخاصة في بعض القضايا المنطقية مثل : تعريف التصور والتصديق، وكذلك تعريف العكس المستوى والعكس النقيض (۲)؛ لذلك وفقًا لقطب الدين الرازي، يمكننا تقسيم المناطقة الإسلاميين إلى ثلاثة مدارس أو مذاهب في العالم الإسلامي: مدرسة المعلم الثاني الفارابي، ومدرسة الشيخ الرئيس ابن سينا ومدرسة الإمام فخر الدين الرازي (۳). ومن خلال هذه المقدمة سنسعى إلى ذكر ما اشتمال عليه أوسع كتاب مؤلف في علم المنطق، وهو كتاب المنطق الكبير» الذي كتبه وحرره فخر الدين الرازي، والذي يعتبر أساس كتبه اللاحقة في المنطق، مثل: «الملخّص»، و شرح الإشارات والتنبيهات»، و «شرح عيون الحكمة». ومع كونه كذلك إلا أنه من خلال البحث الذي قمنا به وجدنا أن كتاب المنطق الكبير» لم تقدم حوله أي دراسات سابقة! ولم ينشر أصلا قبل هذه النشرة. وكذلك من خلال تتبع الأبحاث والدراسات التي تناولت جهود فخر الدين الرازي في علم المنطق ، لم نجدها تناولت كتاب المنطق الكبير بالدراسة ولا بالمناقشة، وإنما نجد الإشارة في بعضها لعنوان الكتاب فقط، ولهذا السبب، نأمل أن تقدم دراستنا مساهمة كبيرة في الأبحاث المتعلقة بمكانة وأهمية فخر الدين الرازي في الدراسات المنطقية. فإن إصدار ونشر الأعمال الرئيسة مثل هذا الكتاب لها أهمية من حيث دقة إجراء وتطبيق الدراسات المنطقية من خلال الاعتماد على المصادر الرئيسة بدلا من المصادر الثانوية - الفرعية. ومن خصائص كتاب المنطق «الكبير مشابهته لكتاب «الشفاء» لابن سينا في جزء المنطق منه؛ وعلى الرغم من كتابة المنطق الكبير على خمسة فصول (جمل) أساسية، إلا أنه يتضمن تسعة كتب في علم المنطق، وبضم المقدمة له يكون مكونا من عشرة كتب، وبالمقارنة مع نسق وأسلوب «كتاب الشفاء» يظهر لنا تقديم وتأخير الرازي لبعض مسائل وأبواب كتابه وفقاً لترتيب «كتاب الشفاء» ونقله عنه بعض المسائل كتصنيف المفرد (البسيط) والمركب، وذكره مسألة الحد، وبحثه الجهات داخل فصول القضايا، وبذلك يمكننا أن نؤكد أن كتاب «الإشارات والتنبيهات لابن سينا كان من مصادر فخر الدين الرازي من حيث صياغة وتنظيم فصول المنطق الكبير إلا أن المنطق الكبير للرازي يتميز عن الإشارات والتنبيهات لابن سينا في إضافته لمبحث: المقولات (=قاطيغورياس)، ومعالجته لفصل الصناعات الخمس) بمزيد من التفصيل والتوسع مقارنة بالأعمال الأخرى. ١ - المنطق الكبير : نسخ المخطوطة : كما يفهم من اسم الكتاب، يعتبر المنطق الكبير الكتاب الأكثر شمولا وبسطا في مجال المنطق بين مصنفات الرازي المتعددة. مع أخذنا في الاعتبار أسبقية تصنيفه لكتاب الآيات البينات الذي يتكون من عشر صفحات فقط وبذلك يمكن القول إن أول عمل منطقي رئيس للرازي هو كتاب المنطق الكبير. على الرغم من عدم بروزه في مصادر المنطق الكلاسيكي، إلا أن الرازي يشير إليه في كتبه؛ فيقول مثلا : ( وكتابنا الكبير ) (۱).
Considering the works of Fakhr al-Din al-Razi in logic, he can be considered one of the greatest scientific figures who influenced the Islamic world after al-Farabi and Ibn Sina. And through his adoption of the Avicennan school of logic, whose founder was titled by some as 'al-Shaykh al-Ra'is', and al-Khwaja Nasir al-Din al-Tusi (d. 672 AH/1274 CE) chose for Fakhr al-Razi the title 'al-Sharih al-Fadil' (the Excellent Commentator). Additionally, Qutb al-Din al-Razi al-Tahtani (d. 766 AH/1365 CE) indicates that Fakhr al-Din al-Razi had his own opinions and choices in some logical issues such as: the definition of conception (tasawwur) and assent (tasdiq), and the definition of simple conversion ('aks mustawi) and conversion by contrapositive ('aks al-naqid) (2); therefore according to Qutb al-Din al-Razi, we can divide Islamic logicians into three schools or doctrines in the Islamic world: the school of the Second Teacher al-Farabi, the school of the Chief Master Ibn Sina, and the school of Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi (3). And through this introduction we will strive to mention what is contained in the most comprehensive book authored on the science of logic, which is the book 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir' written and edited by Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, which is considered the basis of his later books on logic, such as 'al-Mulakhkhas', 'Sharh al-Isharat wa al-Tanbihat', and 'Sharh 'Uyun al-Hikmah'. And despite being such, through the research we conducted we found that the book 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir' has not been the subject of any previous studies! And it was not published at all before this edition. Also, by tracing the research and studies that dealt with the efforts of Fakhr al-Din al-Razi in the science of logic, we did not find them dealing with the book 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir' by study or discussion, rather we find mention in some of them of only the title of the book. For this reason, we hope that our study will make a significant contribution to research on the status and importance of Fakhr al-Din al-Razi in logical studies. Indeed, issuing and publishing major works such as this book is important in terms of the accuracy of conducting and applying logical studies by relying on primary sources instead of secondary-subordinate sources. Among the characteristics of the book 'al-Kabir' is its similarity to the book 'al-Shifa'' by Ibn Sina in the logic part thereof; and despite the writing of 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir' in five basic chapters (juman), it includes nine books on the science of logic, and with the introduction it becomes composed of ten books. Compared with the arrangement and style of the 'Book of al-Shifa'', we see al-Razi's advancement and postponement of some issues and chapters of his book according to the order of the 'Book of al-Shifa'' and his transmission from it of some issues such as the classification of the simple (al-mufrad/al-basit) and compound, and his mention of the issue of definition (hadd), and his discussion of modalities within the chapters of propositions. Thus we can confirm that the book 'al-Isharat wa al-Tanbihat' by Ibn Sina was among the sources of Fakhr al-Din al-Razi in terms of formulating and organizing the chapters of 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir', except that 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir' by al-Razi is distinguished from 'al-Isharat wa al-Tanbihat' by Ibn Sina by his addition of the section: the categories (=Qatigurias), and his treatment of the chapter of the five arts (al-sina'at al-khams) with more detail and expansion compared to other works. 1 - al-Mantiq al-Kabir: Manuscript copies: As understood from the name of the book, 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir' is the most comprehensive and extensive book in the field of logic among the multiple works of al-Razi. Taking into account the priority of his authorship of the book 'al-Ayat al-Bayyinat' which consists of only ten pages, it can be said that the first major logical work of al-Razi is the book 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir'. Despite its lack of prominence in classical logic sources, al-Razi refers to it in his books; for example he says: 'and our great book' (1).
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is an introduction to the book 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir' by Fakhr al-Din al-Razi. It begins by establishing al-Razi's importance in Islamic logic after al-Farabi and Ibn Sina, noting that he adopted the Avicennan school and was titled 'al-Sharih al-Fadil' by Nasir al-Din al-Tusi. The author then mentions that Qutb al-Din al-Razi identified three schools of Islamic logicians: al-Farabi's, Ibn Sina's, and Fakhr al-Din al-Razi's own school (due to al-Razi's independent opinions on issues like the definitions of tasawwur/tasdiq and conversion). The passage next explains that the purpose of this introduction is to introduce 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir', which is al-Razi's most comprehensive logical work and the basis for his later books like 'al-Mulakhkhas' and 'Sharh al-Isharat'. The author notes that no previous studies have focused on this book, nor has it been published before this edition, so this study aims to fill that gap. The passage then describes characteristics of 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir': it is similar to Ibn Sina's 'al-Shifa'' in its logical part but is organized into five main chapters that contain nine books (ten including the introduction). It follows the order of 'al-Shifa'' in some issues but also adds a section on categories (al-maqulat) and treats the five arts in more detail than Ibn Sina's 'al-Isharat'. Finally, the passage discusses the manuscript copies, stating that 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir' is al-Razi's first major logical work, even though it is not prominent in classical sources; al-Razi himself refers to it as 'our great book'.

Checkpoint
According to Qutb al-Din al-Razi, how many schools of Islamic logicians are there?
A) Two

Key Takeaway
Fakhr al-Din al-Razi is not merely a follower of Avicenna but the founder of his own school of logic.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In a later text, you find that a logician defines tasawwur differently from Ibn Sina. Which school might he belong to? Al-Razi's school.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
7 min
Key Features of al-Mantiq al-Kabir
Author describes characteristics of al-Mantiq al-Kabir and its relation to Ibn Sina's works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare al-Mantiq al-Kabir with Ibn Sina's al-Isharat in terms of structure, sources, and original additions.

Core Idea
Al-Mantiq al-Kabir is the most comprehensive Avicennan logic work with added categories and expanded five arts.

This lesson examines the unique features of al-Razi's major work, al-Mantiq al-Kabir. The passage highlights its relation to Ibn Sina's texts, its structure, and what sets it apart. Understanding these features will help you appreciate the book's significance in the logical tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the structure
The text says the book is written in five chapters but contains nine books (ten with introduction).
The Arabic: 'على خمسة فصول...تسعة كتب...وعشرة بالمقدمة'.
2
Compare sources
It draws from Ibn Sina's al-Shifa' and al-Isharat, but reorganizes and adds content.
Look for the mention of 'الشفاء' and 'الإشارات والتنبيهات'.
3
Spot the additions
Two key additions: the section on categories (al-maqulat) and expanded treatment of the five arts.
The text says: 'إضافته لمبحث: المقولات' and 'معالجته لفصل الصناعات الخمس بمزيد من التفصيل'.
4
Assess its role
It is the basis for al-Razi's later logical works and is his first major logical work.
The text: 'يعتبر أساس كتبه اللاحقة...أول عمل منطقي رئيس للرازي'.

The passage then describes characteristics of 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir': it is similar to Ibn Sina's 'al-Shifa'' in its logical part but is organized into five main chapters that contain nine books (ten including the introduction). It follows the order of 'al-Shifa'' in some issues but also adds a section on categories (al-maqulat) and treats the five arts in more detail than Ibn Sina's 'al-Isharat'. Finally, the passage discusses the manuscript copies, stating that 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir' is al-Razi's first major logical work, even though it is not prominent in classical sources; al-Razi himself refers to it as 'our great book'.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
10 min
Understanding al-Razi's Mantiq al-Kabir: Scope and Sources
Author describes the significance, structure, chronology, and sources of Mantiq al-Kabir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key structural and chronological features of al-Razi's Mantiq al-Kabir and distinguish it from its sources.

Core Idea
Al-Razi's Mantiq al-Kabir is the most comprehensive logic work in Islam after Ibn Sina's al-Shifa.

This lesson introduces Fakhr al-Din al-Razi's monumental logical work, al-Mantiq al-Kabir. You will learn how the book is structured, how it relates to earlier works by Ibn Sina, and what makes it original. Understanding the scope and sources of a major text helps you appreciate its place in the Islamic logical tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's purpose
Read the opening of the passage. The author states that publishing major works like this one is important for accurate logical studies. Al-Razi wrote the book to provide a comprehensive treatment of logic relying on primary sources.
2
Compare structure with Ibn Sina's al-Shifa
The passage says that Mantiq al-Kabir is similar in structure to the logic section of al-Shifa. Al-Razi follows the order of al-Shifa in some topics, e.g., classification of terms, definition, and modalities in propositions. But Mantiq al-Kabir has nine books plus an introduction, making ten books, organized into five main chapters.
Note that while al-Shifa is larger overall, Mantiq al-Kabir is more comprehensive in logic specifically.
3
Note original additions beyond Ibn Sina's al-Isharat
Al-Razi added a section on categories (Qatigurias) and treated the five arts in much more detail than in Ibn Sina's al-Isharat wa al-Tanbihat. This shows his independent contribution.
The passage explicitly states that these additions distinguish his work from al-Isharat.
4
Determine the chronological placement
The passage provides evidence that Mantiq al-Kabir was written after al-Ayat al-Bayyinat and al-Mabahith al-Mashriqiyya, but before his commentaries on al-Isharat and Uyun al-Hikma. It was completed around 576 AH / 1180 CE when al-Razi was 32-33 years old. This helps establish its place in al-Razi's intellectual development.
Al-Razi himself refers to it as 'our great book' in his later works, confirming its importance.

ومن خلال النظر في المصادر التي يستشهد بها الرازي في كتابه «المنطق الكبير، يثبت عندنا تصنيفه له بعد كتاب الآيات البينات» و «المباحث «المشرقية وقبل تصنيفه لـ «شرح الإشارات والتنبيهات» و «شرح عيون الحكمة. مع مراعاة أن الرازي بدأ بتحرير كتبه الأخرى قبل الانتهاء من «الملخص»، و«المنطق الكبير »(۱). ومع هذه القرائن، يتضح لنا أن الرازي قد أنهى هذا العمل بعد (٥٧٦هـ/ ۱۱۸٠م) في سن ۳۲ أو ۳۳(۲).

Study - Fakhr al-Din al-Razi in logical studies. Indeed, the publication and dissemination of major works such as this book have importance in terms of the accuracy of conducting and applying logical studies by relying on primary sources instead of secondary-subordinate sources. Among the characteristics of the book 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir' is its similarity to Ibn Sina's 'al-Shifa' in its logic section; although al-Mantiq al-Kabir is written in five basic chapters (jumal), it contains nine books on logic, and with the introduction it comprises ten books. In comparison with the arrangement and style of 'al-Shifa', we see al-Razi's advancement and delay of some issues and chapters of his book according to the order of 'al-Shifa', and his transmission from it of some issues such as the classification of the simple and composite, his mention of the issue of definition (hadd), and his discussion of modalities within the chapters on propositions. Thus we can confirm that Ibn Sina's 'al-Isharat wa al-Tanbihat' was among the sources of Fakhr al-Din al-Razi in terms of the formulation and organization of the chapters of al-Mantiq al-Kabir, except that al-Razi's al-Mantiq al-Kabir is distinguished from Ibn Sina's al-Isharat wa al-Tanbihat by his addition of the section on categories (Qatigurias) and his treatment of the chapter on the five arts with more detail and expansion compared to other works. 1 - al-Mantiq al-Kabir: Manuscript copies: As understood from the name of the book, al-Mantiq al-Kabir is considered the most comprehensive and expansive book in the field of logic among al-Razi's multiple works. Taking into account the precedence of his writing of the book 'al-Ayat al-Bayyinat' which consists of only ten pages, it can be said that al-Razi's first major logical work is the book al-Mantiq al-Kabir. Despite its lack of prominence in classical sources of logic, al-Razi refers to it in his books; for example he says: 'and our great book' (1). Commentary
This passage is a scholarly introduction to Fakhr al-Din al-Razi's Mantiq al-Kabir. It opens by emphasizing the importance of publishing major works like this for accurate logical studies, stressing reliance on primary sources. The author then compares Mantiq al-Kabir to Ibn Sina's al-Shifa, noting that although the book is organized into five main chapters (jumal), it actually contains nine books on logic plus an introduction, making ten. Al-Razi follows the order of al-Shifa in some topics and borrows classifications such as simple and composite terms, the discussion of definition (hadd), and the inclusion of modalities in the chapters on propositions. However, the key distinction from Ibn Sina's al-Isharat wa al-Tanbihat is the addition of a section on the categories (Qatigurias) and a more detailed treatment of the five arts. The passage then discusses the manuscript tradition, establishing that Mantiq al-Kabir is al-Razi's first major logical work, preceded only by the short al-Ayat al-Bayyinat. Al-Razi himself refers to it as 'our great book' in his later works. Through citations, it is determined that the work was written after al-Mabahith al-Mashriqiyya and before his commentaries on al-Isharat and Uyun al-Hikma. Chronological evidence suggests it was completed after 576 AH (1180 CE), when al-Razi was 32 or 33 years old. The text confirms that Mantiq al-Kabir is the most extensive logic book in Islamic civilization after Ibn Sina's al-Shifa. The manuscript shows that after praising God and the Prophet, al-Razi immediately begins with the topics of logic and concludes with his own analyses. Finally, it notes that this is al-Razi's first lengthy logical work, in which he critiques Aristotle, al-Farabi, Ibn Sina, al-Sawi, and al-Baghdadi, and lists his other logical works, especially al-Mulakhkhas fi al-Mantiq.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Dating and Significance of Mantiq Kabir
Establishes the dating of Mantiq Kabir and compares it to other works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to locate Mantiq Kabir within al-Razi's corpus and assess its comparative size among Islamic logic works.

Core Idea
Mantiq Kabir is the most comprehensive logic work in Islam after Ibn Sina's al-Shifa.

Before we dive into the logical content of Mantiq Kabir, we need to understand its place in Islamic intellectual history. This front-matter lesson establishes when al-Razi wrote this work, how it relates to his other books, and why it is considered a landmark text. Knowing this will help you appreciate the magnitude of the logical project you are about to undertake.

Guided Path
1
Identify al-Razi's other works mentioned
Locate the titles: 'Clear Signs', 'Eastern Investigations', 'Commentary on the Pointers', 'Commentary on the Sources of Wisdom', 'The Summary', and 'The Product'. These are the books the passage uses to bracket Mantiq Kabir chronologically.
This helps you see the range of al-Razi's interests – logic, philosophy, theology, and usul al-fiqh.
2
Find the chronological indicators
The passage states Mantiq Kabir was written after the first two and before the commentaries. Also look for the date: after 576 AH / 1180 CE. This means al-Razi was around 32-33 when he finished it.
Understanding the timeline gives insight into his intellectual development.
3
Assess the comparative claim
The author claims Mantiq Kabir is 'the widest book in logic in Islamic civilization after Ibn Sina's al-Shifa'. Compare this assertion with the fact that the passage also says it is al-Razi's first lengthy logic work.
Consider the evidence: the author likely made this judgment by surveying other major logic works.
4
Note the source's critical engagement
The passage says al-Razi discusses opinions of Aristotle, al-Farabi, Ibn Sina, al-Sawi, and al-Baghdadi. This shows Mantiq Kabir is not a mere summary but a critical, synthetic work.
This prepares you for the dialectical style you will encounter in the text.

The Great Logic. And by examining the sources that al-Razi cites in his book 'The Great Logic', it is established for us that he classified it after the book 'Clear Signs' and 'Eastern Investigations' and before his classification of 'Commentary on the Pointers and Reminders' and 'Commentary on the Sources of Wisdom'. When comparing the book 'The Great Logic' with classical books in logic up to our present time, we can confirm that 'The Great Logic' is the widest book in logic in Islamic civilization after Ibn Sina's 'The Healing'. And it appears to us from the manuscript that the author of the book, after mentioning praise of God and prayers upon His Messenger, begins the work directly dealing with the topics and sections of the science of logic (3) and concludes it with his reports, results, and logical opinions (4). And through this book he tried to secure his position in scientific circles and research centers. And as a result of complete tracking and induction of the works of Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, it is established for us that al-Razi finished composing the book 'The Great Logic' in the same period in which he finished composing the book 'The Product in the Principles of Jurisprudence' (1).

Commentary
This passage is a modern scholarly discussion about Fakhr al-Din al-Razi's book 'Mantiq Kabir' (The Great Logic). It begins by establishing the date of composition through cross-referencing with al-Razi's other works. The author states that al-Razi wrote this book after his 'Clear Signs' and 'Eastern Investigations' but before his commentaries on Ibn Sina's works. This places the completion after 576 AH, when al-Razi was about 32-33 years old. The passage then compares Mantiq Kabir to classical logic works, claiming it is the most comprehensive book in Islamic logic after Ibn Sina's al-Shifa. It notes that al-Razi starts directly with the subject matter after the opening praise. The text further explains that Mantiq Kabir is al-Razi's first lengthy logic work, where he critically engages with major philosophers like Aristotle, al-Farabi, Ibn Sina, al-Sawi, and al-Baghdadi. Finally, it correlates the completion of Mantiq Kabir with that of al-Razi's usul al-fiqh work, al-Mahsul, indicating that both were written around the same time. The passage uses footnotes for citations, typical of modern academic writing.

Describes the manuscript and the novelty of the current study of Mantiq Kabir.

Core Idea
Not all manuscripts are authentic; critical verification is essential for reliable scholarship.

This passage shows how researchers established that only one of eight manuscripts of al-Razi's Mantiq Kabir is genuine. The process of verification is a crucial skill for anyone working with classical Islamic texts, as it ensures that the logical arguments we study are based on authentic sources.

The introduction of 'The Great Logic' indicates that the book is not a commentary or an abridgement, but rather the opposite: a comprehensive encyclopedic classification and an independent scientific composition (2). Identifying Manuscript Misattributions: The Case of al-Mantiq al-Kabir
Describes two copies mistakenly attributed to al-Razi as actually by al-Samarqandi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to detect when a manuscript's stated author is unlikely based on content comparison and identify the correct author.

Core Idea
Manuscripts lie; textual content reveals true authorship.

This passage corrects a common misattribution: two manuscripts wrongly labelled as al-Razi's 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir' are actually al-Samarqandi's 'Adab al-Bahth wa al-Munazara'. Understanding how to spot such errors is crucial for anyone working with Islamic manuscripts. This lesson teaches you the basic skills of textual attribution analysis.

Guided Path
1
Read the attribution on the manuscript
Note what the manuscript's first page claims. In this case, it claims 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir' by al-Razi.
Attributions on title pages are not always reliable.
2
Compare the content with known works of the alleged author
Check if the content matches the style and subject matter of al-Razi's known works. Here, the content is about dialectical method, not logic per se.
3
Identify the actual work by matching to known texts
Recognize the text as 'Adab al-Bahth wa al-Munazara' by al-Samarqandi, a standard work on debate.
Familiarity with key texts in the field helps.
4
Verify using external sources
Cross-check with bibliographic sources or other catalogues to confirm.
Scholarly consensus and manuscript catalogues are valuable.

The Purpose and Classification of Logic
Author opens with praise of God and explains the need for logic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why logic is considered an instrumental science and identify its subject matter (secondary intelligibles) as distinct from the subject matter of other sciences.

Core Idea
Logic is the tool that guards the intellect from error, not a science of existence but a normative discipline.

This opening passage from al-Razi's al-Mantiq al-Kabir establishes the rationale for studying logic. It draws a powerful analogy: logic is to the intellect as a carpenter's tool is to wood. Understanding this instrumental role is key to appreciating why Muslim scholars gave logic a central place in the curriculum. Here we will parse the author's classification of sciences and the unique domain of logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's praise and its purpose
The author begins with hamdala, praising God for giving humans intellect and sending messengers. This frames logic as a divine gift and a means to know truths. Note that this is a standard opening in Islamic scholarly works, connecting the subject to revelation.
2
Extract the analogy for logic
The text compares logic to a carpenter's tool: just as a craftsman needs a tool to shape wood, the intellect needs logic to avoid error. This analogy shows that logic is not an end in itself but an instrument (آلة) for other sciences.
3
Analyze the classification of sciences
The author distinguishes sciences sought for themselves (first philosophy/metaphysics) from those sought for other things (logic and other tools). Then he divides theoretical sciences into natural, mathematical, and divine. This classification helps locate logic's place.
4
Locate the subject matter of logic
The passage states logic investigates secondary intelligibles (المعقولات الثانية). These are concepts that apply to primary concepts, like 'subject' and 'predicate'. This distinguishes logic from metaphysics, which studies existence as such.
5
Reflect on the instrumental nature of logic
Logic is not a science that discovers new facts about the world; rather, it provides rules for correct reasoning. This instrumental view means logic is indispensable for any discipline that aims at certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحمد لله الذي جعل الإنسان متميزاً بالعقل، وهداه إلى معرفة الحقائق، وأرسل الرسل مبشرين ومنذرين. وبعد: فإن أشرف العلوم وأعلاها علم المنطق، الذي به تعرف صحة الأفكار من فسادها، وبه تنال المعارف اليقينية. ولولا المنطق لاضطربت الأحكام والعلوم. وسبب وضعه أن الإنسان يحتاج إلى قانون يعصمه من الخطأ في نظره، كما أن النجار يحتاج إلى آلة ليصنع الخشب. فالمنطق آلة للعلوم. ثم اعلم أن العلوم منها ما هو مطلوب لذاته ومنها ما هو مطلوب لغيره. والمطلوب لذاته هو الفلسفة الأولى، والمطلوب لغيره هو المنطق وغيره من الآلات. ثم العلوم النظرية تنقسم إلى أقسام: طبيعي ورياضي وإلهي. والمنطق إنما يبحث عن المعقولات الثانية.
Praise be to God who distinguished man with intellect, guided him to knowledge of truths, and sent messengers as bringers of good news and warners. After this: the most noble and highest of sciences is the science of logic, by which the correctness of ideas is known from their corruption, and by which certain knowledge is attained. Were it not for logic, judgments and sciences would be disordered. The reason for its invention is that man needs a law that protects him from error in his reasoning, just as the carpenter needs a tool to work wood. So logic is a tool for the sciences. Then know that among the sciences, some are sought for themselves and some are sought for other than themselves. What is sought for itself is first philosophy; what is sought for other than itself is logic and other tools. Then the theoretical sciences are divided into divisions: natural, mathematical, and divine. Logic only investigates secondary intelligibles.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is the opening of al-Razi's al-Mantiq al-Kabir. It begins with the basmala and hamdala, then states the subject: logic is the most noble science because it preserves the mind from error. The author gives an analogy: logic is to the intellect as a tool is to a craftsman. He then classifies sciences into those sought for themselves (first philosophy/metaphysics) and those sought for other things (instrumental sciences like logic). Finally, he briefly outlines the division of theoretical sciences into natural, mathematical, and divine, and states that logic deals with secondary intelligibles (al-ma'qulat al-thaniyya). This is a standard preface in logic works, establishing the importance and scope of the discipline.

Key Terms
المنطق
المعقولات الثانية
آلة للعلوم

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because logic is a branch of metaphysics.

Key Takeaway
Logic is an instrumental science (ala) that provides rules for correct reasoning; its subject matter is secondary intelligibles, and it serves as a tool for all other sciences.
