Evaluating Manuscript Authorship: The Case of al-Mantiq al-Kabir
Modern scholar argues against al-Razi's authorship based on missing citations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate evidence for and against the authorship of a manuscript using external and internal criteria.

Core Idea
Authorship attribution requires balancing external silence against internal self-reference.

In this lesson, we examine a scholarly debate about whether al-Mantiq al-Kabir was truly written by Fakhr al-Din al-Razi. The passage presents evidence against his authorship based on classical bibliographies, then counters with al-Razi's own references to a 'great book'. This teaches us a critical method for evaluating manuscript attributions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim being investigated
The passage investigates whether al-Mantiq al-Kabir is authentically by al-Razi. Note that the author presents both evidence against and for the attribution.
2
Extract the external evidence
The author notes that classical biographers like Ibn Abi Usaybi'a, al-Abhari, and al-Safadi do not list this work. This is evidence from silence in authoritative sources.
3
Extract the internal evidence
Al-Razi himself refers to a 'great book' in Sharh al-Isharat, and stylistic similarity is observed. This is positive internal evidence supporting authorship.
4
Weigh the evidence
External silence is significant but not conclusive; internal evidence is positive but could be ambiguous. The author ultimately suggests the attribution is plausible.
5
Recognize the scholarly method
This balance of external (bio-bibliographical) and internal (self-citation, style) evidence is standard in textual criticism of Islamic manuscripts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يمكن القول إن ذكر القزويني على المخطوطة هو إثبات ملكية لا بيانًا لإسم المؤلف، وربما عزا الطبسي النسخة إلى القزويني الذي احتفظ بها لفترة. وكاحتمال آخر، قد تكون هذه الملاحظات إرشادية فقط، تدل على أنه تمت قراءة أو مراجعة الكتاب من قبل القزويني. يوجد رقم ١٥ أسفل اسم الطبسي على (۱) (و) وأيضًا يوجد رقم ٥١ تحت ۱ اسم الكتاب ولا نجد تفسيرًا واضحًا لهذه الأرقام المدونة، ولكنها قد تشير إلى المبالغ المدفوعة لحامل هذه النسخة أو إلى رقم فهرست الكتاب. هناك دليل آخر يقوي الادعاءات بأن النسخة الحالية ليست من تأليف الرازي، هو عدم وجود أي ذكر للمنطق الكبير في المصادر الكلاسيكية ومطولات علم المنطق. وعلى ذلك يمكننا اختيار ثلاثة أسماء هي أقرب المصادر الببلوغرافيا العلوم الفخر الرازي: ابن أبي أصيبعة (ت: ٦٦٨هـ / ١٢٧٠م) تلميذ أفضل الدين الخونجي (ت: ١٢٤٨/٦٤٦) المذكور ضمن تلاميذ الفخر الرازي. ب أثير الدين الأبهري (ت: ٦٦٣هـ / ١٢٦٥م) تلميذ ابن خلکان (ت: ٦٨٠هـ / ١٢٨٢م). ج صلاح الدين خليل بن أيبك الصفدي (ت: ٧٦٤هـ / ١٣٦٣م) تلميذ شمس الدين الأصفهاني (المتوفى ١٣٤٩/٧٤٩). لم ينسب هؤلاء المؤرخين الثلاثة ولا كتاب الطبقات للرازي كتابا باسم المنطق الكبير. والجواب عن هذا الأمر أننا قد وضحنا سابقاً أن الرازي ذكر بنفسه تصنيفه لكتاب بعنوان «المنطق الكبير» في أعماله المتعددة. وأشار لكتابه الموسع بـ المنطق «الكبير في تلك الأعمال وفي عدة مواضع من كتبه، وبالمقارنة يظهر لنا التشابه في تناوله للقضايا بين المنطق الكبير وأعماله الأخرى، وكذلك أسلوبه الذي يتميز بالدقة والتحرير. ويمكن سرد المراجع المذكورة أعلاه على النحو التالي: شرح الإشارات والتنبيهات : يقول الرازي: [فنقول هذه الشكوك وإن حللناها في كتابنا الكبير لكنا نقول : العلم بماهية العلة لا يقتضي العلم
It can be said that the mention of al-Qazwini on the manuscript is a proof of ownership, not a statement of the author's name, and perhaps al-Tabasi attributed the copy to al-Qazwini who kept it for a while. As another possibility, these notes may be merely indicative, showing that the book was read or reviewed by al-Qazwini. There is a number 15 below the name of al-Tabasi on (1) (w) and also a number 51 under the name of the book, and we find no clear explanation for these recorded numbers, but they may refer to amounts paid to the holder of this copy or to the book's index number. There is another evidence that strengthens the claims that the current copy is not by al-Razi, which is the absence of any mention of al-Mantiq al-Kabir in classical sources and lengthy works of logic. Accordingly, we can choose three names that are the closest bibliographic sources for the sciences of Fakhr al-Razi: Ibn Abi Usaybi'a (d. 668 AH / 1270 CE), student of Afdal al-Din al-Khunji (d. 1248/646) mentioned among the students of Fakhr al-Razi. B. Athir al-Din al-Abhari (d. 663 AH / 1265 CE), student of Ibn Khallikan (d. 680 AH / 1282 CE). C. Salah al-Din Khalil ibn Aybak al-Safadi (d. 764 AH / 1363 CE), student of Shams al-Din al-Isfahani (d. 1349/749). These three historians and the Kitab al-Tabaqat did not attribute to al-Razi a book called al-Mantiq al-Kabir. The answer to this is that we have previously clarified that al-Razi himself mentioned his authorship of a book entitled 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir' in his various works. And he referred to his extensive book as 'al-Kabir' in those works and in several places in his books, and by comparison we see the similarity in his treatment of issues between al-Mantiq al-Kabir and his other works, as well as his style characterized by precision and editing. The aforementioned references can be listed as follows: Sharh al-Isharat wa al-Tanbihat: al-Razi says: 'We say: these doubts, even if we have resolved them in our great book, we say: knowledge of the essence of the cause does not necessitate knowledge...'
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a scholarly discussion about the authorship of a manuscript titled 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir', traditionally attributed to Fakhr al-Din al-Razi. The passage begins by examining the presence of al-Qazwini's name on the manuscript, suggesting it may indicate ownership rather than authorship. It then presents a key piece of evidence against al-Razi's authorship: the absence of any mention of 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir' in classical biographical and bibliographical sources. Three specific historians—Ibn Abi Usaybi'a, Athir al-Din al-Abhari, and al-Safadi—are cited as authorities who do not list this work among al-Razi's writings. The author then counters this argument by pointing out that al-Razi himself references a 'great book' (al-kitab al-kabir) in his other works, such as Sharh al-Isharat wa al-Tanbihat. The similarity in style and content between the manuscript and al-Razi's known works is also noted as supporting his authorship. The passage concludes by quoting al-Razi mentioning his 'great book' in relation to resolving doubts about causality.

Key Terms
المنطق الكبير
مخطوطة
إثبات ملكية

Key Takeaway
Attribution debates rely on both external references in biographical works and internal cross-references within the author's corpus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider a short treatise on logic found in a manuscript. No classical biographer mentions it, but the author of a known work seems to refer to 'my shorter logic'. Using the method from this lesson, construct an argument for or against its authenticity.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
The Subject of Logic: From Five Universals to Knowledge as Such
Compares two definitions of the subject matter of logic before and after al-Razi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two historical definitions of logic's subject matter and explain the shift from the five universals to knowledge as such.

Core Idea
Logic's subject shifted from the five universals to knowledge as such.

In this lesson, we explore a key historical development in Islamic logic: the redefinition of its subject matter. Before al-Razi, logicians defined the subject of logic as the logical secondary intelligibles—essentially the five universals. After Nasir al-Din al-Tusi, a new definition emerged: logic is the study of knowledge as such. This shift, reflected in texts like al-Mantiq al-Kabir, reveals deeper questions about the scope and purpose of logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the earlier definition
Find the phrase 'al-ma'qulat al-thaniyya al-mantiqiyya' in the passage. Note that it is equated with 'al-kulliyat al-khams' (the five universals). This was the definition before al-Razi and used by him.
2
Identify the later definition
Find the phrase 'al-ilm min haythu huwa al-ilm' (knowledge as such). This definition appeared after al-Tusi.
3
Trace the historical shift
The passage states that the earlier definition was common before al-Razi, and the later definition was adopted after al-Tusi. Note that al-Mantiq al-Kabir contains both, creating a problem.
The likely explanation is that the later definition was added by later logicians.
4
Understand the implications
Consider why redefining the subject matter is significant: it changes the focus of logic from conceptual tools to the nature of knowledge itself. This affects how logic interacts with other sciences like kalam and usul al-fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ر - وأخيرا، نريد أن نتطرق إلى موضوع علم المنطق قبل الرازي، فقد تم تعريف موضوع المنطق على أنه: المعقولات الثانية المنطقية أي الكليات الخمس بشكل عام، وقد تم اعتماد هذا التعريف كأساس في أعمال الرازي الأخرى. ولكن في حقبة ما بعد نصير الدين الطوسي، تم تعريف موضوع المنطق بأنه العلم من حيث هو العلم. وهذا التعريف مدرج بالفعل في كتاب المنطق الكبير وهو يخلق بعض الإشكال. ومن المحتمل أنه قد تم إضافة هذا التعريف في المنطق الكبير لاحقا من قبل المنطقيين مثل الكشي والطوسي والخونجي والقزويني.
R - Finally, we want to address the subject of logic before al-Razi. The subject of logic was defined as: the logical secondary intelligibles, i.e., the five universals in general, and this definition was adopted as a basis in al-Razi's other works. But in the era after Nasir al-Din al-Tusi, the subject of logic was defined as knowledge as such. And this definition is already included in the book al-Mantiq al-Kabir, and it creates some problems. And it is probable that this definition was added to al-Mantiq al-Kabir later by logicians such as al-Kashi, al-Tusi, al-Khunji, and al-Qazwini.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage discusses the historical change in the definition of the subject matter of logic. It begins by stating the earlier definition prevalent before al-Razi: the subject of logic is 'al-ma'qulat al-thaniyya al-mantiqiyya' (the logical secondary intelligibles), which are essentially the five universals (kulliyat khams: genus, species, differentia, property, accident). This definition was used by al-Razi in his other works. Then it notes a shift after Nasir al-Din al-Tusi: the subject was redefined as 'al-ilm min haythu huwa al-ilm' (knowledge as such). Interestingly, this latter definition appears in the book al-Mantiq al-Kabir itself, which creates a problem because it is inconsistent with al-Razi's usual definition. The author suggests that this second definition was likely added later by later logicians such as al-Kashi, al-Tusi, al-Khunji, and al-Qazwini, rather than being original to al-Razi. This passage thus highlights a textual and doctrinal issue in the history of logic.

Key Terms
المعقولات الثانية المنطقية (al-ma'qulat al-thaniyya al-mantiqiyya)
الكليات الخمس (al-kulliyat al-khams)
العلم من حيث هو العلم (al-ilm min haythu huwa al-ilm)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What was the original definition of the subject of logic before Nasir al-Din al-Tusi?
A) Knowledge as such
B) The five universals
C) Secondary intelligibles
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
The subject of logic underwent a significant redefinition from the five universals to knowledge as such, reflecting evolving views on the nature of logical inquiry.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Compare the table of contents of two logic works: one from before al-Tusi (e.g., al-Razi's Talkhis) and one from after (e.g., al-Taftazani's Tahdhib). Note how the structure reflects the definition of the subject matter.
?
Write a short paragraph explaining why the definition of logic as 'knowledge as such' is broader than the definition as 'the five universals'.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
5 min
Shift in Definition of Logic's Subject
Comparison of two definitions of logic's subject

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to contrast the two historical definitions of the subject of logic and identify which logicians promoted each definition.

Core Idea
The definition of logic's subject shifted from secondary intelligibles to knowledge itself.

In this lesson, we explore a pivotal shift in Islamic logic: the redefinition of its subject matter. The passage reveals that before Nasir al-Din al-Tusi, logic was defined as dealing with secondary intelligibles, particularly the five universals. After al-Tusi, logic came to be defined as 'knowledge insofar as it is knowledge.' Understanding this shift helps us trace the evolution of the discipline.

Guided Path
1
Identify the earlier definition
Locate in the passage where the subject of logic before al-Razi is defined as 'al-ma'qulat al-thaniya al-mantiqiyya' (the secondary intelligibles) specifically the five universals. Note how this definition was used in al-Razi's own works.
This is the classical definition found in many pre-Tusi works.
2
Identify the later definition
Find the later definition introduced after Nasir al-Din al-Tusi: 'al-'ilm min haythu huwa al-'ilm' (knowledge insofar as it is knowledge). The passage mentions that this definition appears in al-Mantiq al-Kabir and causes problems.
This definition marks a shift toward epistemological concerns.
3
Compare the two definitions
Note the differences: the earlier definition focuses on the objects of thought (secondary intelligibles), while the later one focuses on the nature of knowledge itself. Consider how this changes the scope of logic.
The shift may reflect Tusi's influence from the Peripatetic tradition.
4
Evaluate the interpolation hypothesis
The passage suggests the later definition might be a later addition by logicians like al-Kashshi, al-Tusi, al-Khunaji, and al-Qazwini. Consider why this might have been added and what evidence supports or refutes this.
This shows how texts can be modified over time.

Al-Mantiq al-Kabir. 'Al-Muntashira' is a term mentioned in the book 'Al-Ayat al-Bayinat' by al-Razi, and it differs from what came after al-Razi. It was also mentioned in 'Sharh 'Uyun al-Hikmah' (1). That the two styles of 'al-'urfiya' and 'al-mashruta' are also included in the same works (3). In this case we cannot accept the idea of distortion of the content of al-Mantiq al-Kabir. Finally, we want to touch on the subject of the science of logic before al-Razi. The subject of logic was defined as: 'the secondary intelligibles, i.e., the five universals in general', and this definition was adopted as a basis in al-Razi's other works (3). But in the era after Nasir al-Din al-Tusi, the subject of logic was defined as 'knowledge insofar as it is knowledge'. This definition is already included in the book al-Mantiq al-Kabir, and it creates some problems (4). We also find clear overlap and intersection between the content of al-Mantiq al-Kabir and al-Razi's other works. While taking into account the existence of some modifications and distortions in the current copy of al-Mantiq al-Kabir, despite these small differences, there is no doubt about the proven attribution of the current copy of al-Mantiq al-Kabir to al-Razi. This proves that al-Qazwini was only one of the owners of the manuscript of al-Mantiq al-Kabir for some time, despite some people mentioning him as the author of the book. Another name attributed to the authorship of al-Mantiq al-Kabir is Siraj al-Din al-Urmawi. Upon checking his published and manuscript works, no work with this name has been proven for him. Thus, it can be said with full confidence: al-Mantiq al-Kabir is not among his books. Likewise, the works of Zayn al-Din al-Kashshi were examined, and no evidence was found proving his authorship of this book. — Among the important points that eliminate the possibility of the book's authorship after al-Razi and confirm his authorship is that we have not found any quotation from or reference to him with titles like 'Afdal al-Muta'akhkhirin' or 'Khatimat al-Muhaqqiqin' — these are the formulae used in praising him. Commentary
This passage is a modern scholarly analysis of the book al-Mantiq al-Kabir, attributed to Fakhr al-Din al-Razi. The author first discusses a term 'al-Muntashira' found in another work by al-Razi and notes its difference from later usage. The passage then addresses the definition of the subject of logic: before al-Razi, it was the secondary intelligibles, specifically the five universals, and al-Razi's works used this definition. After Nasir al-Din al-Tusi, the definition shifted to 'knowledge insofar as it is knowledge,' which is also found in al-Mantiq al-Kabir, causing some issue. The author suggests this latter definition might be a later interpolation by logicians such as al-Kashshi, al-Tusi, al-Khunaji, and al-Qazwini. The summary affirms the harmony between al-Mantiq al-Kabir and al-Shifa' by Avicenna, and with al-Razi's other works, arguing that despite some modifications, the attribution to al-Razi is certain. The passage then moves to ownership marks and refutes alternative attributions to al-Qazwini, al-Urmawi, and al-Kashshi by checking their known works. Finally, it argues that the absence of certain honorific titles for al-Razi in the manuscript suggests it was not composed after his time, but many later authors still referenced it.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate

Authorship of al-Mantiq al-Kabir
Authorship investigation of al-Mantiq al-Kabir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the evidence for the authorship of al-Mantiq al-Kabir and argue whether it can be attributed to Fakhr al-Din al-Razi.

Core Idea
Al-Mantiq al-Kabir is almost certainly by al-Razi despite later claims to the contrary.

Who wrote al-Mantiq al-Kabir? This lesson examines the scholarly debate over its authorship. The passage refutes attributions to al-Qazwini, al-Urmawi, and al-Kashshi, and uses evidence from manuscript ownership and honorific titles to affirm al-Razi's authorship. By evaluating this evidence, you will learn how historians of logic determine authorship.

Guided Path
1
Identify alternative authors
The passage mentions three other names proposed as authors: Najm al-Din al-Qazwini al-Katibi, Siraj al-Din al-Urmawi, and Zayn al-Din al-Kashshi. List each one.
These are known logicians from the post-Razi period.
2
Examine the evidence against each
For each proposed author, find the passage's argument: al-Qazwini's name appears on the manuscript only as an owner, not author; al-Urmawi has no known work by that title; al-Kashshi leaves no evidence. Summarize each refutation.
This shows how ownership and authorship are often confused.
3
Consider the positive evidence for al-Razi
The passage points to harmony between al-Mantiq al-Kabir and al-Razi's other works, and the absence of later honorific titles like 'Afdal al-Muta'akhkhirin'. Identify why this supports al-Razi's authorship.
Such titles are anachronistic if applied to al-Razi during his lifetime.
4
Weigh the overall case
Despite some modifications in the manuscript, the passage concludes there is no doubt about al-Razi's authorship. Consider the strength of each piece of evidence and decide if you agree.
This exercise builds critical thinking about manuscript attribution.

That the two styles of 'al-'urfiya' and 'al-mashruta' are also included in the same works (3). In this case we cannot accept the idea of distortion of the content of al-Mantiq al-Kabir. Finally, we want to touch on the subject of the science of logic before al-Razi. The subject of logic was defined as: 'the secondary intelligibles, i.e., the five universals in general', and this definition was adopted as a basis in al-Razi's other works (3). But in the era after Nasir al-Din al-Tusi, the subject of logic was defined as 'knowledge insofar as it is knowledge'. This definition is already included in the book al-Mantiq al-Kabir, and it creates some problems (4). It is probable that this definition was added to al-Mantiq al-Kabir later by logicians such as al-Kashshi, al-Tusi, al-Khunaji, and al-Qazwini. Summary: we find great harmony between the two books al-Mantiq al-Kabir and al-Shifa', except for some issues. We also find clear overlap and intersection between the content of al-Mantiq al-Kabir and al-Razi's other works. While taking into account the existence of some modifications and distortions in the current copy of al-Mantiq al-Kabir, despite these small differences, there is no doubt about the proven attribution of the current copy of al-Mantiq al-Kabir to al-Razi. Ahmad III: no. 3401, 1 wa, statement of ownership of al-Qazwini on the left side and al-Tabasi on the right side. 6 - Some researchers decide that the true author of al-Mantiq al-Kabir is Najm al-Din al-Qazwini al-Katibi. After investigation, we have verified that no book on logic titled 'al-Kabir' has been attributed to al-Qazwini before. This proves that al-Qazwini was only one of the owners of the manuscript of al-Mantiq al-Kabir for some time, despite some people mentioning him as the author of the book. Another name attributed to the authorship of al-Mantiq al-Kabir is Siraj al-Din al-Urmawi. Upon checking his published and manuscript works, no work with this name has been proven for him. Thus, it can be said with full confidence: al-Mantiq al-Kabir is not among his books. Likewise, the works of Zayn al-Din al-Kashshi were examined, and no evidence was found proving his authorship of this book. — Among the important points that eliminate the possibility of the book's authorship after al-Razi and confirm his authorship is that we have not found any quotation from or reference to him with titles like 'Afdal al-Muta'akhkhirin' or 'Khatimat al-Muhaqqiqin' — these are the formulae used in praising him. Nevertheless, many authors after al-Razi have been found, most notably

Commentary
This passage is a modern scholarly analysis of the book al-Mantiq al-Kabir, attributed to Fakhr al-Din al-Razi. The author first discusses a term 'al-Muntashira' found in another work by al-Razi and notes its difference from later usage. The passage then addresses the definition of the subject of logic: before al-Razi, it was the secondary intelligibles, specifically the five universals, and al-Razi's works used this definition. After Nasir al-Din al-Tusi, the definition shifted to 'knowledge insofar as it is knowledge,' which is also found in al-Mantiq al-Kabir, causing some issue. The author suggests this latter definition might be a later interpolation by logicians such as al-Kashshi, al-Tusi, al-Khunaji, and al-Qazwini. The summary affirms the harmony between al-Mantiq al-Kabir and al-Shifa' by Avicenna, and with al-Razi's other works, arguing that despite some modifications, the attribution to al-Razi is certain. The passage then moves to ownership marks and refutes alternative attributions to al-Qazwini, al-Urmawi, and al-Kashshi by checking their known works. Finally, it argues that the absence of certain honorific titles for al-Razi in the manuscript suggests it was not composed after his time, but many later authors still referenced it.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
5 min
Evaluating Authorship Evidence for al-Mantiq al-Kabir
Discussion of authorship evidence for al-Mantiq al-Kabir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate manuscript evidence for authorship by analyzing stylistic similarities and scribal additions.

Core Idea
Scribal honorifics and marginal notes do not disprove authorship—style comparison is key.

Attributing a classical text to its correct author is a critical skill in Islamic scholarship. This lesson walks you through the reasoning used to confirm Fakhr al-Din al-Razi's authorship of al-Mantiq al-Kabir, focusing on stylistic comparison and careful interpretation of manuscript features like honorifics and marginal notes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the text's references to other scholars
Note which authors are cited and how they are referred to. In al-Mantiq al-Kabir, Aristotle, al-Farabi, Ibn Sina, and al-Sawi are mentioned. This indicates the text engages with earlier authorities.
Al-Armawi's own writings refer to al-Razi as 'the Chief', but the text itself does not.
2
Compare the style with known works of the proposed author
Look for similarities in phrasing, structure, and analytical approach. The passage states that al-Mantiq al-Kabir shares style with al-Razi's Sharh 'Uyun al-Hikmah, Sharh al-Isharat, and al-Mulakhkhas.
This comparison is explicit in the source and strengthens the attribution.
3
Distinguish between tasnif and ta'liq
Determine whether the manuscript is an original authored work (tasnif) or a student's commentary/notes (ta'liq). The presence of a scribe's name (Zayn al-Din al-Kashi) and honorifics might suggest ta'liq, but the passage argues the core text is tasnif.
Even if notes were added, the main body remains al-Razi's composition.
4
Evaluate scribal additions and honorifics
Honorifics like 'al-Imam' and third-person phrasing ('Fakhr al-Din al-Razi said') are common scribal practices showing respect. They do not indicate a different author.
The passage explicitly says these additions cannot be taken as evidence against al-Razi's authorship.

للنص، وكذلك لا تحتوي على أي تعليقات أو ملاحظات جانبية لشخص غير الرازي. من المحتمل أن تكون فقرات الكشي الأربعة هي الملاحظات التي سجلها من معلمه أو ملاحظاته التي كتبها أسفل النسخة التي نسخها من نسخة معلمه. ومن الممكن أن يكون الناسخ قد حافظ على هذه الإضافات لتعظيمه للكشي. وبدلا من ذلك، تم نسخ العمل أو لا للكشي بدلا من القزويني وبعد ذلك، تم تسليمه إلى الأخير. وبذلك، يمكننا القول إن الناسخ أضاف الملاحظات الخاصة بالقزويني أثناء عملية النسخ الأولى للعمل. واستخدام تعبيرات مثل «قال الامام فخر الدين الرازي...» بدلا من أسلوب المتكلم: «أقول ذلك أو قولي...» الذي يستخدم لإثبات هوية المتكلم، وليس لنفي يوجد دليل ينفي نسبة تأليف الرازي للكتاب.
Al-Armawi, who frequently refers to al-Razi with phrases like 'The opinion of the Chief in this matter is...' or 'The Chief said...'. As for the text of 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir', it is the opposite, for it refers to the opinions of logicians such as Aristotle, al-Farabi, Ibn Sina, and 'Umar ibn Sahlan al-Sawi. We find in the existing copy that al-Farabi and Ibn Sina are referred to as 'the best of the later ones'; and it is known that during the period following al-Razi, both al-Farabi and Ibn Sina were considered from the first layer, and the second layer (the later ones) began with al-Razi. A comparison of 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir' with al-Razi's other works gives us a certain result, due to the similarity of the style of formulation of 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir' with 'Sharh 'Uyun al-Hikmah', 'Sharh al-Isharat wa al-Tanbihat', and also 'al-Mulakhkhas', and this matter is apparent to the reader. And we can take into account the similarity in style, content, and analysis. There is a final question that must be answered: Is the existing copy of 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir' a classification or a commentary? The name of Zayn al-Din al-Kashi appears in four paragraphs of the text. We find in one of its paragraphs the designation of al-Razi as 'al-Imam'. This designation is found only in the supplementary leaves and some corrections that the copyist made for the spelling errors of the text, and it also does not contain any comments or marginal notes from anyone other than al-Razi. It is possible that the four paragraphs of al-Kashi are the notes he recorded from his teacher or his notes that he wrote at the bottom of the copy he made from his teacher's copy. And it is possible that the copyist preserved these additions out of reverence for al-Kashi. Alternatively, the work was copied first for al-Kashi instead of al-Qazwini, and then handed over to the latter. Thus, we can say that the copyist added the notes of al-Qazwini during the first copying of the work. And the use of expressions like 'al-Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi said...' instead of the first-person style 'I say that' or 'my saying...', which is used to establish the identity of the speaker, is not to negate the authorship of al-Razi for this book, and some students may add titles in their copies out of respect and honor for the teacher, and we conclude that the appearance of al-Razi's name as 'Imam' in the existing copy cannot be considered evidence against the authorship of al-Razi nor in favor of someone else. Finally, after verifying the works of the طبقات books and the bibliography of the classical period, as well as verifying the texts and contents of al-Razi's books, including the existing copy of 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir', we can say that there is no evidence that negates the attribution of the book's authorship to al-Razi.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is a scholarly discussion about the text 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir' attributed to Fakhr al-Din al-Razi. It first notes that al-Armawi (a commentator) frequently cites al-Razi as 'the Chief', whereas 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir' itself references earlier logicians like Aristotle, al-Farabi, Ibn Sina, and al-Sawi. It also mentions that in the manuscript, al-Farabi and Ibn Sina are called 'the best of the later ones', indicating a historiographical division where the first layer of logicians ended with them and the second layer began with al-Razi. The passage then argues that a comparison of al-Mantiq al-Kabir with al-Razi's known works (Sharh 'Uyun al-Hikmah, Sharh al-Isharat, al-Mulakhkhas) shows a clear similarity in style, content, and analysis, supporting al-Razi's authorship. The central question is whether the existing manuscript is a classification (tasnif) by al-Razi or a commentary (ta'liq) by someone else. The name of Zayn al-Din al-Kashi appears in four places, and one passage calls al-Razi 'al-Imam'. The author argues that this title appears only in supplementary leaves and scribal corrections, and does not indicate non-authorship. The use of 'al-Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi said' instead of a first-person voice is typical of scribes showing respect, not evidence of another author. Ultimately, after checking bibliographic sources and the content, the passage concludes there is no evidence against al-Razi's authorship.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate

Establishing the Authorship of al-Mantiq al-Kabir
Authorship evidence and counterarguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the evidence for and against Fakhr al-Din al-Razi's authorship of al-Mantiq al-Kabir and articulate why honorific titles do not negate attribution.

Core Idea
Honorific titles in manuscripts reflect scribal respect, not authorship denial.

Scholars sometimes question authorship based on scribal additions like 'al-Imam' before a name. This lesson examines how such titles appear in manuscripts of al-Mantiq al-Kabir and why they are not evidence against al-Razi's authorship. You will learn to assess manuscript evidence critically, a skill essential for working with classical Islamic texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the authorship claim and counterclaim
Locate the passage where the author discusses the use of 'al-Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi said...' and the counterargument that this might negate al-Razi's authorship. Understand the two positions.
2
Analyze the scribal addition argument
The passage argues that students may add respectful titles when copying. Consider why a scribe would add 'al-Imam'—is it to claim a different author or to honor the teacher? The text says it 'is used to establish the identity of the speaker, not to negate al-Razi's authorship.'
3
Examine the bibliographic and textual evidence
The author states that after checking Tabaqat books and examining al-Razi's other works, 'there is no evidence denying the attribution.' List the types of evidence mentioned: biographical dictionaries, textual content analysis, and existing manuscript copy.
4
Formulate your own assessment
Based on the passage, decide whether you agree with the conclusion. Write a one-sentence summary of why the authorship is attributed to al-Razi despite the honorific titles.
This step requires you to weigh the evidence yourself.

المنطق الكبير
- مصادر المنطق الكبير :
المنطق الكبير هو أول كتاب للمؤلف عن المنطق، ولهذا السبب سيكون من المناسب الحديث عن مصادره وأصالته هنا
ذكرنا سابقاً أن الرازي لا يقلّد طريقة أسلافه في التصنيف ولا يتجاهل مساهماتهم العلمية. ففي نسخة المنطق الكبير»، نجده يستشهد صراحةً بأسماء المناطقة الذين يشاطرهم آراءه وأفكاره، ومن جهة أخرى، يحلل ويشرح النقاط
التي يعارضهم بها ويوضح ويفند القضايا التي يعتقد أنه أسيء فهمها.
يحتوي المنطق الكبير على اقتباسات كثيرة ومتنوعة من أرسطو، وأفلاطون (ت: ٣٤٧ ق.م)، والفارابي، وابن سينا وعمر بن سهلان الساوي. ونجد لابن سينا النصيب الأكبر ؛ ومن خلال التحليل والتدقيق لمادة الكتاب بأكمله، اتضح لنا أن المنطق الكبير»، وعلى نطاق واسع تم تصنيفه بالاعتماد على أعمال ابن سينا المنطقية، مع مراعاة التشابه في المنهجية والموضوع، فإن أكثر الكتب التي تم الاستشهاد بها في المنطق الكبير» هو كتاب «الشفاء» لابن سينا. كما ذكرنا من قبل، فإن جميع موضوعات الكتاب التسعة هي منوطة بـ المنطق الكبير». ولذلك، هناك بعض التداخلات بين المنطق الكبير و الإشارات والتنبيهات لابن سينا في مباحث معينة؛ على سبيل المثال، يتعامل كلاهما مع فصل التعريف قبل فصل العرض. وقد تم الاستشهاد بـ الإشارات والتنبيهات» بشكل مباشر وأحيانًا بشكل غير مباشر. وأخيرًا، ينبغي معرفة أن لأرسطو ذكر كبير في المنطق الكبير» كما في كتاب «الشفاء».
في الصفحة التالية، سيجد القارئ جدولا بخصوص مصادر الكتاب التي تم الاقتباس منها مباشرة مع ذكر المصدر.
These additions to magnify him for al-Kashshi. Instead, the work was copied or not for al-Kashshi instead of al-Qazwini, and after that, it was handed over to the latter. Thus, we can say that the scribe added the notes of al-Qazwini during the first copying of the work. And the use of expressions like 'al-Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi said...' instead of the speaker's style: 'I say that or my saying...' which is used to establish the identity of the speaker, not to negate al-Razi's authorship of this book. Some students may add titles in their copies out of veneration and respect for the teacher. We conclude from this that the appearance of al-Razi's name as 'Imam' in the existing copy cannot be considered evidence either for al-Razi's authorship or for someone else.
Finally, after verifying the works of the Tabaqat books and bibliography about the classical period, as well as examining the texts and contents of al-Razi's books, including the existing copy of 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir', we can say that there is no evidence denying the attribution of authorship of the book to al-Razi.
al-Mantiq al-Kabir
- Sources of al-Mantiq al-Kabir:
al-Mantiq al-Kabir is the author's first book on logic, and for this reason it will be appropriate to speak about its sources and authenticity here.
We mentioned earlier that al-Razi does not blindly follow the method of his predecessors in classification, nor does he ignore their scholarly contributions. In the copy of 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir', we find him explicitly citing the names of the logicians who share his views and ideas. On the other hand, he analyzes and explains the points he disagrees with them on, and clarifies and refutes the issues he believes have been misunderstood.
al-Mantiq al-Kabir contains many diverse quotations from Aristotle, Plato (d. 347 BC), al-Farabi, Ibn Sina, and 'Umar ibn Sahlan al-Sawi. We find that Ibn Sina has the largest share; and through analysis and scrutiny of the material of the entire book, it became clear to us that 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir' was largely classified based on the logical works of Ibn Sina. Taking into account similarity in methodology and subject matter, the most cited book in 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir' is Ibn Sina's 'al-Shifa''. As we mentioned before, all nine topics of the book are attached to 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir'. Therefore, there are some overlaps between 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir' and Ibn Sina's 'al-Isharat wa al-Tanbihat' in certain topics; for example, both deal with the chapter on definition before the chapter on accident. 'al-Isharat wa al-Tanbihat' was cited directly and sometimes indirectly. Finally, one should know that Aristotle has a significant mention in 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir' as in 'al-Shifa''.
On the following page, the reader will find a table regarding the sources of the book that were directly quoted with mention of the source.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage is a scholarly discussion about the authorship and sources of the work 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir'. It begins by addressing the issue of scribal additions and the use of honorifics like 'al-Imam' for Fakhr al-Din al-Razi. The author argues that such titles do not disprove al-Razi's authorship; rather, students may add them out of respect. The conclusion after verifying bibliographic sources and examining the text itself is that there is no evidence against attributing the book to al-Razi. Then the passage discusses the sources of 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir'. It emphasizes that al-Razi does not simply imitate his predecessors but engages critically with them. The book contains quotations from Aristotle, Plato, al-Farabi, Ibn Sina, and others, with Ibn Sina having the largest influence. The most cited work is Ibn Sina's 'al-Shifa''. There are also overlaps with Ibn Sina's 'al-Isharat wa al-Tanbihat', such as the order of chapters (definition before accident). Aristotle also features prominently. Finally, the reader is informed that a table of direct quotations follows on the next page.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
5 min
Sources of al-Mantiq al-Kabir and the Primacy of Ibn Sina
Listing and analyzing the sources.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major sources of al-Mantiq al-Kabir and explain why Ibn Sina's works, especially al-Shifa', are the most influential.

Core Idea
Al-Razi's logic is built on Ibn Sina, yet he critically engages rather than blindly follows.

A text does not emerge in isolation. Al-Razi's al-Mantiq al-Kabir draws heavily on earlier logicians, especially Ibn Sina. This lesson maps the key sources—Aristotle, al-Farabi, Ibn Sina, and others—and shows how al-Razi cites, critiques, and reworks them. Understanding this helps you see how the Islamic logical tradition developed through engagement, not mere repetition.

Guided Path
1
List the explicitly named sources
Scan the passage for the names of philosophers: Aristotle, Plato, al-Farabi, Ibn Sina, and 'Umar ibn Sahlan al-Sawi.
Note that Plato is mentioned but rarely cited in logic works; his inclusion indicates al-Razi's broad reading.
2
Determine the most cited source
The passage says 'we find that Ibn Sina has the largest share' and 'the most cited book is Ibn Sina's al-Shifa''. Identify the evidence: both methodology and topics align.
3
Identify overlaps with Ibn Sina's al-Isharat wa al-Tanbihat
The passage gives a specific example: both works place the chapter on definition before the chapter on accident. Find this in the text.
4
Understand al-Razi's critical method
Al-Razi does not simply copy; he 'analyzes and explains the points he disagrees with' and 'refutes the issues he believes have been misunderstood.' This shows active critique, not passive transmission.

المنطق الكبير
- مصادر المنطق الكبير :
المنطق الكبير هو أول كتاب للمؤلف عن المنطق، ولهذا السبب سيكون من المناسب الحديث عن مصادره وأصالته هنا
ذكرنا سابقاً أن الرازي لا يقلّد طريقة أسلافه في التصنيف ولا يتجاهل مساهماتهم العلمية. ففي نسخة المنطق الكبير»، نجده يستشهد صراحةً بأسماء المناطقة الذين يشاطرهم آراءه وأفكاره، ومن جهة أخرى، يحلل ويشرح النقاط
التي يعارضهم بها ويوضح ويفند القضايا التي يعتقد أنه أسيء فهمها.
يحتوي المنطق الكبير على اقتباسات كثيرة ومتنوعة من أرسطو، وأفلاطون (ت: ٣٤٧ ق.م)، والفارابي، وابن سينا وعمر بن سهلان الساوي. ونجد لابن سينا النصيب الأكبر ؛ ومن خلال التحليل والتدقيق لمادة الكتاب بأكمله، اتضح لنا أن المنطق الكبير»، وعلى نطاق واسع تم تصنيفه بالاعتماد على أعمال ابن سينا المنطقية، مع مراعاة التشابه في المنهجية والموضوع، فإن أكثر الكتب التي تم الاستشهاد بها في المنطق الكبير» هو كتاب «الشفاء» لابن سينا. كما ذكرنا من قبل، فإن جميع موضوعات الكتاب التسعة هي منوطة بـ المنطق الكبير». ولذلك، هناك بعض التداخلات بين المنطق الكبير و الإشارات والتنبيهات لابن سينا في مباحث معينة؛ على سبيل المثال، يتعامل كلاهما مع فصل التعريف قبل فصل العرض. وقد تم الاستشهاد بـ الإشارات والتنبيهات» بشكل مباشر وأحيانًا بشكل غير مباشر. وأخيرًا، ينبغي معرفة أن لأرسطو ذكر كبير في المنطق الكبير» كما في كتاب «الشفاء».
في الصفحة التالية، سيجد القارئ جدولا بخصوص مصادر الكتاب التي تم الاقتباس منها مباشرة مع ذكر المصدر.
These additions to magnify him for al-Kashshi. Instead, the work was copied or not for al-Kashshi instead of al-Qazwini, and after that, it was handed over to the latter. Thus, we can say that the scribe added the notes of al-Qazwini during the first copying of the work. And the use of expressions like 'al-Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi said...' instead of the speaker's style: 'I say that or my saying...' which is used to establish the identity of the speaker, not to negate al-Razi's authorship of this book. Some students may add titles in their copies out of veneration and respect for the teacher. We conclude from this that the appearance of al-Razi's name as 'Imam' in the existing copy cannot be considered evidence either for al-Razi's authorship or for someone else.
Finally, after verifying the works of the Tabaqat books and bibliography about the classical period, as well as examining the texts and contents of al-Razi's books, including the existing copy of 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir', we can say that there is no evidence denying the attribution of authorship of the book to al-Razi.
al-Mantiq al-Kabir
- Sources of al-Mantiq al-Kabir:
al-Mantiq al-Kabir is the author's first book on logic, and for this reason it will be appropriate to speak about its sources and authenticity here.
We mentioned earlier that al-Razi does not blindly follow the method of his predecessors in classification, nor does he ignore their scholarly contributions. In the copy of 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir', we find him explicitly citing the names of the logicians who share his views and ideas. On the other hand, he analyzes and explains the points he disagrees with them on, and clarifies and refutes the issues he believes have been misunderstood.
al-Mantiq al-Kabir contains many diverse quotations from Aristotle, Plato (d. 347 BC), al-Farabi, Ibn Sina, and 'Umar ibn Sahlan al-Sawi. We find that Ibn Sina has the largest share; and through analysis and scrutiny of the material of the entire book, it became clear to us that 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir' was largely classified based on the logical works of Ibn Sina. Taking into account similarity in methodology and subject matter, the most cited book in 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir' is Ibn Sina's 'al-Shifa''. As we mentioned before, all nine topics of the book are attached to 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir'. Therefore, there are some overlaps between 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir' and Ibn Sina's 'al-Isharat wa al-Tanbihat' in certain topics; for example, both deal with the chapter on definition before the chapter on accident. 'al-Isharat wa al-Tanbihat' was cited directly and sometimes indirectly. Finally, one should know that Aristotle has a significant mention in 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir' as in 'al-Shifa''.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Tracing the Sources of al-Mantiq al-Kabir
Author discusses sources and reliance on Ibn Sina.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the main sources of al-Razi's al-Mantiq al-Kabir and determine the relative influence of each based on the passage.

Core Idea
Al-Razi builds on Ibn Sina's foundation while critically engaging the entire logical tradition.

This passage from a modern study of al-Mantiq al-Kabir reveals the intellectual roots of Fakhr al-Din al-Razi's first logic work. Rather than working in isolation, al-Razi explicitly cites his predecessors, with Ibn Sina's al-Shifa being the most quoted source. Understanding this helps us see how Islamic logic developed as a cumulative tradition where new works respond to earlier ones. Let's examine the passage to uncover these influences.

Guided Path
1
Identify all named sources
Scan the passage and list every philosopher or book that al-Razi cites. Names include Aristotle, Plato, al-Farabi, Ibn Sina, and 'Umar ibn Sahlan al-Sawi. Note the specific books mentioned: al-Shifa and al-Isharat wa al-Tanbihat by Ibn Sina, and the Organon (al-Ta'lim al-Awwal) by Aristotle.
2
Determine the most influential source
The passage explicitly states that Ibn Sina has 'the largest share' of quotations and that the book relies heavily on Ibn Sina's logical works. Count the number of specific folio references or the language of emphasis to confirm that Ibn Sina is the primary source.
Check the table at the end for frequency of citations.
3
Analyze the nature of dependence
The passage notes that al-Razi's methodology and subject matter are similar to Ibn Sina's, and that both treat the chapter on definition before accident. This suggests structural borrowing, not just isolated quotes. Ask yourself: is al-Razi merely summarizing, or does he critically engage? The passage says he 'analyzes and explains the points on which he opposes them' – so his use is critical.
4
Identify other contributors besides Ibn Sina
Look for mentions of Aristotle (al-Mu'allim al-Awwal), al-Farabi, and al-Sawi. Note that Aristotle is frequently mentioned, indicating al-Razi's grounding in Peripatetic logic. Al-Farabi and al-Sawi appear less often, showing they are secondary but present.
5
Evaluate the significance of this source tracing
Consider why a modern scholar would compile this information. Recognizing the sources helps us see the continuity and innovation in Islamic logic. Al-Razi's work is not isolated; it is a critical synthesis of the Avicennan tradition with earlier Peripatetic elements. This lesson trains you to do the same kind of source analysis when studying any classical text.

Al-Mantiq al-Kabir
- Sources of al-Mantiq al-Kabir:
Al-Mantiq al-Kabir is the author's first book on logic, and for this reason it will be appropriate to discuss its sources and authenticity here.
We mentioned previously that al-Razi does not imitate the method of his predecessors in classification, nor does he ignore their scientific contributions. In the copy of al-Mantiq al-Kabir, we find him explicitly citing the names of the logicians who share his views and ideas, and on the other hand, he analyzes and explains the points on which he opposes them and clarifies and refutes the issues he believes have been misunderstood.
Al-Mantiq al-Kabir contains numerous and varied quotations from Aristotle, Plato (d. 347 BC), al-Farabi, Ibn Sina, and 'Umar ibn Sahlan al-Sawi. We find Ibn Sina has the largest share; and through analysis and scrutiny of the entire book's material, it became clear to us that al-Mantiq al-Kabir, to a large extent, was composed relying on Ibn Sina's logical works, considering the similarity in methodology and subject matter, so the most cited book in al-Mantiq al-Kabir is Ibn Sina's al-Shifa. As we mentioned before, all nine subjects of the book are attached to al-Mantiq al-Kabir. Therefore, there are some overlaps between al-Mantiq al-Kabir and Ibn Sina's al-Isharat wa al-Tanbihat in certain topics; for example, both deal with the chapter on definition before the chapter on accident. Al-Isharat wa al-Tanbihat has been cited directly and sometimes indirectly. Finally, it should be known that Aristotle has a large mention in al-Mantiq al-Kabir as in al-Shifa.

Commentary
This passage is a front-matter discussion of the sources of al-Mantiq al-Kabir, the first logic book by Fakhr al-Din al-Razi. The author explains that al-Razi, despite his independence, explicitly cites earlier logicians. The passage then enumerates the key sources: Aristotle, Plato, al-Farabi, Ibn Sina, and 'Umar ibn Sahlan al-Sawi, with Ibn Sina being the most influential. It notes that al-Razi's book heavily depends on Ibn Sina's al-Shifa, both in methodology and content, and also shows overlaps with Ibn Sina's al-Isharat wa al-Tanbihat, such as placing the chapter on definition before accident. The passage concludes by stating that Aristotle is also frequently mentioned. A table on the next page lists folio references for quotations from these sources. This evidences the strong continuity between al-Razi and the Peripatetic/Avicennan tradition in Islamic logic, while also highlighting al-Razi's critical engagement.

D) Ibn Sina's al-Isharat wa al-Tanbihat

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi's al-Mantiq al-Kabir is deeply indebted to Ibn Sina's logical works, while also critically engaging Aristotle, al-Farabi, and others.

Reading Manuscript Page References in Islamic Logic Texts
Lists names and page numbers of figures and groups cited in the work.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to interpret page references using the abbreviations ظ (verso) and و (recto) and identify the categories of cited figures in a classical logic text.

Core Idea
Mastering ظ and و unlocks any classical manuscript index.

This lesson takes you inside the front matter of a major logic work. The index you see lists groups and individuals cited throughout the book, with page references using traditional manuscript abbreviations. Learning to read these abbreviations and categories will allow you to quickly locate discussions of key figures and schools in the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the structure of index entries
Notice that entries are either broad categories (e.g., الحكماء) or specific individuals (e.g., سيبويه). Categories often have page references that span multiple pages.
The list is not alphabetical; it follows the order of appearance or thematic grouping.
2
Recognize the abbreviations for recto and verso
The Arabic abbreviations: 'و' for recto (وجه) and 'ظ' for verso (ظهر). These are placed after the page number. For example, '۲۰ و' means page 20 recto.
These are standard in Arabic manuscripts and critical for locating the exact folio side.
3
Parse the page numbers
Page numbers are in Arabic numerals (e.g., ١٠, ۲۰). Some entries list multiple references separated by commas. The index uses 'و' and 'ظ' consistently.
Some numbers may have stray punctuation from OCR; the pattern is clear: number + و/ظ.
4
Examine the categories used
Categories include الحكماء (sages), الفلاسفة (philosophers), المتقدمون (earlier scholars), المتأخرون (later scholars), الجمهور (general public), النحويون (grammarians), الرياضيون (mathematicians). These show the author's classification of sources.
These categories reflect the intellectual landscape of the text.
5
Note the named individuals
Individuals like سيبويه (Sibawayh), صاحب الكشاف (al-Zamakhshari), أفلاطون (Plato), أرسطو (Aristotle), إقليدس (Euclid), أبقراط (Hippocrates) are listed with folio references.
These names are key to understanding the text's engagement with earlier authorities.

Al-Razi's Quotation Sources and Influences
Explains the quotation sources in al-Razi's work.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key authorities quoted by Fakhr al-Din al-Razi in his logical work and explain the significance of their citation frequencies.

Core Idea
Al-Razi's logical work is deeply indebted to Aristotle and Ibn Sina, with only minor references to others.

This lesson examines the evidence from the index table of al-Razi's logical writings, revealing the extent of his reliance on earlier authorities. Understanding these sources helps situate his logical project within the Islamic tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the quoted authorities
Look at the list of authorities in the table: Aristotle (54 quotations), Ibn Sina (47), al-Farabi (2), 'Umar ibn Sahlan al-Sawi (2). Also noted are Plato, Alexander of Aphrodisias, and Euclid. Count the numbers.
The numbers are counts of quotations, not page references.
2
Compare the frequencies
Notice that Aristotle and Ibn Sina dominate with 54 and 47 quotations respectively, while al-Farabi and al-Sawi have only 2 each. This indicates that al-Razi's primary sources are Aristotle and Ibn Sina.
3
Notice the absence
The passage explicitly states there is no direct quotation from Abu al-Barakat al-Baghdadi. Consider what this suggests about al-Razi's engagement with other contemporaries.
4
Draw conclusions about al-Razi's intellectual influences
Based on the evidence, al-Razi's logical project is heavily dependent on Aristotle and Ibn Sina, with other figures playing a minor role. This helps in understanding his place in the logical tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the index table presented earlier. It begins by summarizing the quotation sources found in the book, listing the number of quotations from each authority: 54 from Aristotle, 47 from Ibn Sina, 2 from al-Farabi, and 2 from 'Umar ibn Sahlan al-Sawi. It also notes the absence of direct quotations from Abu al-Barakat al-Baghdadi. The passage then mentions that the book contains many other quotations, especially from Plato, Alexander of Aphrodisias, and Euclid. From this evidence, the commentator draws a conclusion about al-Razi's classification of his predecessors: al-Razi uses the term 'al-salaf' (predecessors) to refer to the earlier logicians, and he divides them into two distinct groups: 'al-muta'akhkhirūn' (the later ones) and 'al-mutaqaddimūn' (the earlier ones). The commentator notes the difficulty in precisely determining the chronological boundaries of these periods, suggesting that al-Razi's division may be based on conceptual rather than strict historical criteria. The passage ends with a footnote referencing Ibn Sina's 'al-Shifa'' (al-Fannat, p. 424).

Al-Razi's Classification of Logician Predecessors
Explains al-Razi's classification of his logician predecessors.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two groups of logician predecessors (muta'akhkhirun and mutaqaddimun) as classified by al-Razi and explain the difficulty in dating these categories.

Core Idea
Al-Razi classifies earlier logicians into two conceptual groups, not strictly chronological.

This lesson explores al-Razi's division of his logical predecessors into 'the later ones' (al-muta'akhkhirun) and 'the earlier ones' (al-mutaqaddimun). The commentator notes the challenge of precisely defining these periods, suggesting that al-Razi's classification may reflect conceptual differences rather than mere chronology.

Guided Path
1
Locate the classification in the passage
Find where the passage says that al-Razi divides his logician predecessors into two separate groups: al-muta'akhkhirun (the later ones) and al-mutaqaddimun (the earlier ones).
2
Understand the terminology
The term 'al-salaf' here specifically means the earlier logicians (al-munatiqa al-awail). Note the shift from its usual meaning in Islamic usul (early generations of Muslims). The two groups are distinguished by being 'later' or 'earlier'.
3
Consider the chronological challenge
The passage states it is difficult to determine the beginning and end of each period precisely. Why might that be? Possibly because the division is based on methodological or doctrinal differences, not pure dates.
4
Relate the classification to the quotation evidence
Think about which quoted authorities might belong to each group. Aristotle and Ibn Sina (with many quotations) are likely among the 'earlier ones', while al-Sawi (fewer quotations) might be 'later'. However, the passage does not provide explicit assignment.

Establishing Authorship of al-Mantiq al-Kabir
Study confirms al-Razi's authorship of al-Mantiq al-Kabir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate claims of authorship for a medieval logical work by analyzing internal evidence (author’s own statements) and external evidence (biographical sources).

Core Idea
Authorship is proven by the author's own claims and absence of contrary evidence in biographical literature.

When a great logical work like al-Mantiq al-Kabir is sometimes misattributed, how do scholars settle the matter? This lesson walks you through the method used in this study to confirm al-Razi's authorship, a critical first step before engaging with the text’s content.

Guided Path
1
Identify the competing claim
Note the claim that al-Mantiq al-Kabir was authored by Najm al-Din al-Katibi al-Qazwini. Recognize that this is a misattribution that needs to be tested.
2
Search the author’s own works
Examine whether al-Razi himself mentions authoring a book with this title in his other writings. Here, the passage confirms that al-Razi explicitly mentions it in multiple works.
Internal evidence: author's own testimony is strong.
3
Check biographical dictionaries
Consult tabaqat and tarajim works to see if any compiler lists a book called 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir' under al-Katibi’s name. The passage states none do.
Absence of external evidence for the counterclaim.
4
Evaluate the strength of evidence
Weigh the internal evidence (al-Razi’s own claims) against the external counterclaim (lack of corroboration). Conclude that al-Razi is the confirmed author.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخاتمة
نريد أن نختتم هذه الدراسة - التي تهدف إلى تحرير «المنطق الكبير» من أدراج المخطوطات - بتسليط الضوء على أهم النقاط الرئيسية:
أولا: أن الرازي ذكر وصرح بتصنيفه لكتاب «المنطق الكبير» في أعماله المتعددة، وأن من نسب هذا العمل لنجم الدين الكاتبي القزويني لم يجد ما يثبت هذه الدعوى، ولم يذكر كتاب الطبقات والتراجم مصنفاً للقزويني يحمل عنوان المنطق الكبير»، وبذلك يمكننا القول بلا أدنى شك إن المنطق الكبير من تأليف الرازي.
من خلال دراسة وتتبع محتوى كتاب المنطق الكبير يظهر لنا أن الرازي يعتبر أرسطو وابن سينا من مصادر المعرفة المعتمدة، وقد تم إثبات جميع مصادر أرسطو من خلال أعمال ابن سينا. وقد تمت الإشارة كثيراً إلى إقليدس والفارابي والفلاسفة الآخرين من خلال كتب ابن سينا. وبذلك نستنتج أن تراث ابن سينا والمنطق السينيوي من مصادر الرازي المعتمدة.
أما بالنسبة للأسئلة حول سبب تأليف الرازي لكتاب المنطق الكبير وأهمية هذا الكتاب في الدراسات المنطقية، فهناك الكثير من الإجابات التي يجب تقديمها. أولاً: يجب علينا ذكر مميزات المصنف (= الرازي): أهمها : تقدمه وتجديده لهذا العلم وفقا لمتطلبات عصره. وبذلك، يمكننا القول بكل ثقة إنه أصبح من محققي تراث المنطق السينوي، وقد تميزت أعماله بالتعليقات المثمرة. وكذلك استخدامه للمنطق على نطاق واسع، وفي مجالات متعددة كعلم أصول الفقه وعلم الكلام. ولذلك نجده اعتبر الفلسفة والبحث الفلسفي من مقياس الحقيقة واليقين. ولذلك سعى لتطبيق المعرفة التي اكتسبها من خلال المنطق والبرهان في مجالات مختلفة كعلم أصول الفقة وعلم الكلام.
يعد المنطق الكبير هو العمل الأكثر شمولا عن الصناعات الخمس بعد الشفاء لابن سينا، وقد ركز على البرهان والجدل، والمغالطة، والخطابة والشعر. إلى جانب ذلك قدم الرازي بعض التفسيرات المهمة حول قضايا محددة، مثالاً على ذلك، أن المعرفة بديهية ولا تحتاج إلى تعريف، وأن المنطق علم يتعامل مع المعرفة البشرية بشكل كامل. وعلى ذلك، يمكننا تسجيل العديد من هذه مميزات: تصور أنماط العرفية» و«الحينية» وتوضيح تعريفاتها، فحص المختلطات، وانتقاد التعاريف الحالية للعكس المستوي والعكس النقيض، محاولة منه للوصول إلى التعاريف مقبولة لها.
وبالنهاية، فتصنيف الكتب المطولة والموسوعية في المنطق وغيره من العلوم توضح العلاقات المتداخلة بين (أصول الفقه والمنطق) وبذلك جعلت الرازي يمتلك العديد من الألقاب ويقدم على غيره في هذا الفنون. اعتبر بذلك كمؤسس لأحد المذاهب المنطقية، بجانب كلاً من الفارابي وابن سينا، وقد جذب منهج الرازي في التعامل مع أعمال الشيخ الرئيس الأنظار إليه، وقد أطلق على الرازي لقب الشارح «الفاضل لما قدم من جهود و خدمات لهذا العلم. كما يحمل » لقب الإمام (خاتمة المحققين). ويشير هذا الاسم إلى حقيقة ثابتة وهي أن الرازي نجح في عملية الجمع بين المنطق والعلوم الإسلامية التي بدأها ابن حزم والغزالي، كما أثر بشكل كبير على جميع المنطقيين، وعلى الأخص الأشعريين.
Conclusion
We want to conclude this study - which aims to liberate 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir' from the shelves of manuscripts - by highlighting the most important main points:
First: That al-Razi mentioned and declared his authorship of the book 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir' in his various works, and that whoever attributed this work to Najm al-Din al-Katibi al-Qazwini found nothing to prove this claim, and the books of classes and biographies do not mention a work by al-Qazwini bearing the title 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir'. Thus we can say without any doubt that al-Mantiq al-Kabir is authored by al-Razi.
Through studying and tracking the content of the book al-Mantiq al-Kabir, it appears to us that al-Razi considers Aristotle and Ibn Sina as reliable sources of knowledge, and all of Aristotle's sources have been proven through the works of Ibn Sina. Euclid, al-Farabi, and other philosophers have been frequently referenced through Ibn Sina's books. Thus we conclude that the legacy of Ibn Sina and Avicennian logic are among al-Razi's reliable sources.
As for the questions about the reason for al-Razi's authorship of al-Mantiq al-Kabir and the importance of this book in logical studies, there are many answers to be provided. First: We must mention the characteristics of the author (= al-Razi): the most important: his advancement and renewal of this science according to the requirements of his era. Thus, we can confidently say that he became one of the investigators of the Avicennian logical legacy, and his works were distinguished by fruitful commentaries. As well as his extensive use of logic in multiple fields such as usul al-fiqh and kalam. Therefore we find him considering philosophy and philosophical inquiry as the measure of truth and certainty. Therefore he sought to apply the knowledge he acquired through logic and demonstration in various fields such as usul al-fiqh and kalam.
Al-Mantiq al-Kabir is the most comprehensive work on the five arts after Ibn Sina's al-Shifa, and it focused on demonstration, dialectic, sophistry, rhetoric, and poetry. Alongside that, al-Razi provided some important explanations on specific issues, for example, that knowledge is intuitive and does not need definition, and that logic is a science that deals with human knowledge completely. Accordingly, we can record many of these features: conceptualizing the patterns of 'urfiyya and hayniyya and clarifying their definitions, examining mixed syllogisms, and criticizing current definitions of simple conversion and contrapositive, in an attempt to reach acceptable definitions for them.
In the end, the classification of lengthy and encyclopedic books in logic and other sciences clarifies the overlapping relationships between (usul al-fiqh and logic), and thus made al-Razi possess many titles and be preferred over others in these arts. He was thus considered a founder of one of the logical schools, alongside both al-Farabi and Ibn Sina, and al-Razi's approach in dealing with the works of the Chief Master (Ibn Sina) attracted attention. Al-Razi was given the title al-Sharih 'al-Fadil' for what he presented of efforts and services to this science. He also bears the title 'al-Imam' (the Seal of the Investigators). This name indicates an established fact: that al-Razi succeeded in the process of combining logic and Islamic sciences that was begun by Ibn Hazm and al-Ghazali, and he greatly influenced all logicians, especially the Ash'aris.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is the concluding section of a modern study on al-Razi's al-Mantiq al-Kabir. It summarizes the key findings: first, it confirms al-Razi's authorship of the work, refuting claims attributing it to al-Katibi. Second, it identifies Ibn Sina (and through him Aristotle, Euclid, al-Farabi) as al-Razi's main sources, establishing the Avicennian foundation. Third, it explains the significance of the book: it is the most comprehensive work on the five arts (demonstration, dialectic, sophistry, rhetoric, poetry) after Ibn Sina's al-Shifa. Al-Razi's innovation lies in his integration of logic with Islamic sciences like usul al-fiqh and kalam, and his treatment of logic as dealing with all human knowledge. Specific features mentioned: his conceptualization of 'urfiyya and hayniyya patterns (perhaps referring to types of definitions or propositions), examination of mixed syllogisms, and critique of definitions of simple conversion and contrapositive. The passage concludes by highlighting al-Razi's status as a founder of a logical school, alongside al-Farabi and Ibn Sina, and his success in synthesizing logic with Islamic sciences, influencing later logicians, especially the Ash'aris.

Key Terms
فخر الدين الرازي
المنطق الكبير
نجم الدين الكاتبي القزويني

Checkpoint
What does the passage say about the evidence for al-Razi's authorship of al-Mantiq al-Kabir?
A) No clear evidence is provided.
B) Al-Razi mentioned it in his works and no biographies attribute it to al-Katibi.
C) Only al-Katibi's works mention it.
D) It was proven by handwriting analysis.

Key Takeaway
Authorship of a classical work is confirmed by the author's own statements and the silence of biographical sources regarding alternative attributions.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Tracing the Sources of al-Razi's al-Mantiq al-Kabir
Study identifies Ibn Sina and Avicennian logic as al-Razi's main sources.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the main sources of a logical work by analysing explicit citations and the intellectual lineage presented in the text.

Core Idea
Al-Razi's primary source is Ibn Sina, through whom he accesses Aristotle and other philosophers.

Every scholar builds on predecessors. Al-Razi's al-Mantiq al-Kabir is deeply rooted in the Avicennian tradition. In this lesson, you will learn how to trace the sources of a logical work from the author's own references and the study's analysis.

Guided Path
1
List explicitly named authorities
The passage mentions Aristotle, Ibn Sina, Euclid, and al-Farabi as figures referenced. Note that Aristotle's sources are cited through Ibn Sina.
2
Identify the primary conduit
Notice that Ibn Sina is the main intermediary: all Aristotle references come via Ibn Sina, and Euclid and al-Farabi are also mentioned through Ibn Sina's books.
This suggests al-Razi relied heavily on Ibn Sina's works.
3
Classify the type of sources
Distinguish between direct sources (Ibn Sina) and indirect sources (Aristotle via Ibn Sina). The passage states: 'the legacy of Ibn Sina and Avicennian logic are among al-Razi's reliable sources.'
4
Conclude the intellectual lineage
Al-Razi's logical method is Avicennian, building on the foundation of Ibn Sina's al-Shifa and other works.
This explains why his work is considered the most comprehensive after al-Shifa.

الخاتمة

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
6 min
Al-Razi's Integration of Logic with Islamic Sciences
Study highlights al-Razi's integration of logic with usul al-fiqh and kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how al-Razi applied logical methods to usul al-fiqh and kalam, and why this integration was significant for the development of Islamic thought.

Core Idea
Al-Razi made logic the measure of truth for Islamic sciences, bridging philosophy and fiqh/kalam.

One of al-Razi's greatest contributions was not just writing a comprehensive logic book, but using logic to transform other Islamic disciplines. This lesson examines how he applied logical reasoning to usul al-fiqh and kalam, making him a pioneer of interdisciplinary scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Identify al-Razi's approach to logic
Note that he considered logic as dealing with all human knowledge and used it widely in fiqh and kalam. He saw philosophy as the measure of truth.
2
Recognize the fields of application
The passage explicitly mentions usul al-fiqh (principles of jurisprudence) and kalam (theology) as areas where he applied logical methods.
3
Understand the historical context
This integration was begun by Ibn Hazm and al-Ghazali. Al-Razi perfected it, earning him the title 'Seal of the Investigators' and influence over Ash'ari logicians.
4
Assess the impact
By combining logic with Islamic sciences, al-Razi founded a logical school and elevated the standard of reasoning in these disciplines.

أما بالنسبة للأسئلة حول سبب تأليف الرازي لكتاب المنطق الكبير وأهمية هذا الكتاب في الدراسات المنطقية، فهناك الكثير من الإجابات التي يجب تقديمها. أولاً: يجب علينا ذكر مميزات المصنف (= الرازي): أهمها : تقدمه وتجديده لهذا العلم وفقا لمتطلبات عصره. وبذلك، يمكننا القول بكل ثقة إنه أصبح من محققي تراث المنطق السينوي، وقد تميزت أعماله بالتعليقات المثمرة. وكذلك استخدامه للمنطق على نطاق واسع، وفي مجالات متعددة كعلم أصول الفقه وعلم الكلام. ولذلك نجده اعتبر الفلسفة والبحث الفلسفي من مقياس الحقيقة واليقين. ولذلك سعى لتطبيق المعرفة التي اكتسبها من خلال المنطق والبرهان في مجالات مختلفة كعلم أصول الفقة وعلم الكلام.
يعد المنطق الكبير هو العمل الأكثر شمولا عن الصناعات الخمس بعد الشفاء لابن سينا، وقد ركز على البرهان والجدل، والمغالطة، والخطابة والشعر. إلى جانب ذلك قدم الرازي بعض التفسيرات المهمة حول قضايا محددة، مثالاً على ذلك، أن المعرفة بديهية ولا تحتاج إلى تعريف، وأن المنطق علم يتعامل مع المعرفة البشرية بشكل كامل. وعلى ذلك، يمكننا تسجيل العديد من هذه مميزات: تصور أنماط العرفية» و«الحينية» وتوضيح تعريفاتها، فحص المختلطات، وانتقاد التعاريف الحالية للعكس المستوي والعكس النقيض، محاولة منه للوصول إلى التعاريف مقبولة لها.
وبالنهاية، فتصنيف الكتب المطولة والموسوعية في المنطق وغيره من العلوم توضح العلاقات المتداخلة بين (أصول الفقه والمنطق) وبذلك جعلت الرازي يمتلك العديد من الألقاب ويقدم على غيره في هذا الفنون. اعتبر بذلك كمؤسس لأحد المذاهب المنطقية، بجانب كلاً من الفارابي وابن سينا، وقد جذب منهج الرازي في التعامل مع أعمال الشيخ الرئيس الأنظار إليه، وقد أطلق على الرازي لقب الشارح «الفاضل لما قدم من جهود و خدمات لهذا العلم. كما يحمل » لقب الإمام (خاتمة المحققين). ويشير هذا الاسم إلى حقيقة ثابتة وهي أن الرازي نجح في عملية الجمع بين المنطق والعلوم الإسلامية التي بدأها ابن حزم والغزالي، كما أثر بشكل كبير على جميع المنطقيين، وعلى الأخص الأشعريين.
Conclusion
We want to conclude this study - which aims to liberate 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir' from the shelves of manuscripts - by highlighting the most important main points:
First: That al-Razi mentioned and declared his authorship of the book 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir' in his various works, and that whoever attributed this work to Najm al-Din al-Katibi al-Qazwini found nothing to prove this claim, and the books of classes and biographies do not mention a work by al-Qazwini bearing the title 'al-Mantiq al-Kabir'. Thus we can say without any doubt that al-Mantiq al-Kabir is authored by al-Razi.
Through studying and tracking the content of the book al-Mantiq al-Kabir, it appears to us that al-Razi considers Aristotle and Ibn Sina as reliable sources of knowledge, and all of Aristotle's sources have been proven through the works of Ibn Sina. Euclid, al-Farabi, and other philosophers have been frequently referenced through Ibn Sina's books. Thus we conclude that the legacy of Ibn Sina and Avicennian logic are among al-Razi's reliable sources.
As for the questions about the reason for al-Razi's authorship of al-Mantiq al-Kabir and the importance of this book in logical studies, there are many answers to be provided. First: We must mention the characteristics of the author (= al-Razi): the most important: his advancement and renewal of this science according to the requirements of his era. Thus, we can confidently say that he became one of the investigators of the Avicennian logical legacy, and his works were distinguished by fruitful commentaries. As well as his extensive use of logic in multiple fields such as usul al-fiqh and kalam. Therefore we find him considering philosophy and philosophical inquiry as the measure of truth and certainty. Therefore he sought to apply the knowledge he acquired through logic and demonstration in various fields such as usul al-fiqh and kalam.
Al-Mantiq al-Kabir is the most comprehensive work on the five arts after Ibn Sina's al-Shifa, and it focused on demonstration, dialectic, sophistry, rhetoric, and poetry. Alongside that, al-Razi provided some important explanations on specific issues, for example, that knowledge is intuitive and does not need definition, and that logic is a science that deals with human knowledge completely. Accordingly, we can record many of these features: conceptualizing the patterns of 'urfiyya and hayniyya and clarifying their definitions, examining mixed syllogisms, and criticizing current definitions of simple conversion and contrapositive, in an attempt to reach acceptable definitions for them.
In the end, the classification of lengthy and encyclopedic books in logic and other sciences clarifies the overlapping relationships between (usul al-fiqh and logic), and thus made al-Razi possess many titles and be preferred over others in these arts. He was thus considered a founder of one of the logical schools, alongside both al-Farabi and Ibn Sina, and al-Razi's approach in dealing with the works of the Chief Master (Ibn Sina) attracted attention. Al-Razi was given the title al-Sharih 'al-Fadil' for what he presented of efforts and services to this science. He also bears the title 'al-Imam' (the Seal of the Investigators). This name indicates an established fact: that al-Razi succeeded in the process of combining logic and Islamic sciences that was begun by Ibn Hazm and al-Ghazali, and he greatly influenced all logicians, especially the Ash'aris.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is the concluding section of a modern study on al-Razi's al-Mantiq al-Kabir. It summarizes the key findings: first, it confirms al-Razi's authorship of the work, refuting claims attributing it to al-Katibi. Second, it identifies Ibn Sina (and through him Aristotle, Euclid, al-Farabi) as al-Razi's main sources, establishing the Avicennian foundation. Third, it explains the significance of the book: it is the most comprehensive work on the five arts (demonstration, dialectic, sophistry, rhetoric, poetry) after Ibn Sina's al-Shifa. Al-Razi's innovation lies in his integration of logic with Islamic sciences like usul al-fiqh and kalam, and his treatment of logic as dealing with all human knowledge. Specific features mentioned: his conceptualization of 'urfiyya and hayniyya patterns (perhaps referring to types of definitions or propositions), examination of mixed syllogisms, and critique of definitions of simple conversion and contrapositive. The passage concludes by highlighting al-Razi's status as a founder of a logical school, alongside al-Farabi and Ibn Sina, and his success in synthesizing logic with Islamic sciences, influencing later logicians, especially the Ash'aris.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
The Foundational Role of Logic in the Islamic Sciences
Author opens with praise of knowledge and logic as the foundation of all sciences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the author considers logic the root, foundation, divider, and measure of all sciences, and identify the consequences of neglecting it.

Core Idea
Logic is the root, foundation, divider, and measure of all sciences; without it intellects are confused and proofs neglected.

The author opens his work with a powerful declaration: logic is not merely a helper to other sciences—it is their root, foundation, divider, and measure. He warns that without logic, intellects become confused and proofs remain neglected. This lesson will help you unpack this foundational claim and see why logic is indispensable for certainty in Islamic knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key metaphors
The author uses four metaphors: logic is the root (أصل), foundation (أساس), divider (مقطع), and measure (مقياس) of sciences. Find these in the Arabic and note what each implies about logic's role.
Root suggests origin, foundation suggests support, divider suggests distinguishing truth from falsehood, measure suggests standard of evaluation.
2
Understand the consequences of neglect
The author says without logic, intellects would be confused (تحيرت العقول) and strong doubts would force struggle (اضطرت الشبه الفحول). Locate these phrases and consider what state of knowledge would result.
3
Connect to divine science
The author states that divine science (العلم الإلهي) is known through logic and composed from its principles. Reflect on how logic serves as the tool for achieving certainty in theological matters.
4
Apply to a real Islamic science
Choose a science like Kalam or Usul al-Fiqh and think how logic functions as its root and measure. For example, in Kalam, logical syllogisms are used to prove God's existence and attributes.
